出自tedxboston這個開放的演講中 , 理查德・雷斯尼克告訴我們基因測序是如何廉價並快速得顛覆醫療體制 。	in this open talk by tedx boston , richard resnick told us how genetic sequencing is cheap and rapidly disrupting healthcare .
dna , biotech , healthcare , science , technology	dna , biotech , healthcare , you've got it .
理查德・雷斯尼克:歡迎進入基因革命時代	richard risnick: welcome to the age of genetic revolution .
女士們先生們 , 我向您展示人類基因組	ladies and gentlemen , i'm showing you the human genome .
左上是一號染色體	so on the left is chromosome 1 .
右下是性染色體	here's a sex chromosome .
女性有兩條那個大大的x染色體男性有個x當然 , 還有個小小的y	women have two big x chromosomes , men have an x , and , of course , a little y .
男士們 , 不好意思 , 就是那個小東西讓你不同	guys , sorry , that little thing makes you different .
如果放大這條基因組你看到的當然就是這個雙螺旋結構生命的密碼就是由這些生化的字母組成或者說鹼基 , 對吧:a , c , g和t	if you zoom in on the genome , of course you see the password of this doublehelix structure , which is made up of these biochemical letters , or base , right , a , c , g and t .

夸克以色荷為載體透過強力相互作用色荷分三種紅綠藍	the quarks use charge as a carrier in israel interact with a strong force , three different types of charges: red , green , and blue .

如果我們把超荷和弱荷分開在這個二維載荷空間上畫出粒子的載荷電荷就在這些粒子的垂直方向上	if we separate the hypercharge and weak charge into this twodimensional charge space , the charges of the particles are on the vertical direction of those part

因為希格斯粒子的緣故我們只對電荷有了解卻不知道超荷和弱荷	because of the way that the higgs particles do , we only know about electric charge but we don't know about supercharge and weak charge .
左邊的希格斯粒子質量很大打破了電弱圖案的對稱性	the higgs particle on the left is massively disrupting the symmetries of the electrical weak pattern .
透過給弱子較大的質量使弱力更加弱	by giving the weak mass to the weak , weakening the weak force .
由於大量的希格斯粒子在水平方向分佈產生電磁力的光子仍然沒有質量而且在載荷空間中和電荷相互作用	because of the massive higgs particles distributed in the horizontal direction , the photons of electromagnetic force remain massless and interact with electric charges in the charge space .
所以電磁力和弱力在這個二維空間中透過粒子載荷的圖案表示出來	so electromagnetic and weak forces are represented in this twodimensional pattern of particle charges .
我們可以把強力沿兩個載荷的方向表示出來然後將載荷用夸克形式沿這兩個方向畫出來	we can express the strong force along two charge directions and draw the charges in the form of quarks along these two directions .
所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四維空間中畫出來然後投影到二維空間以便我們能觀察到	the charges of all known particles can be drawn out in four dimensions and projected into two dimensions , so that we can see them .
無論粒子如何作用自然會在這四個載荷方向上保持完美的平衡	no matter how particles act , nature keeps perfect balance on these four charge directions .
一個粒子如果和它的反粒子相撞會產生能量四個電荷方向的載荷疊加變為零	if a particle collides with its antiparticles , it creates a charge added to zero charges in the four charge directions .
這樣只要保持能量相同和載荷總量為零可以產生任何物質	so as long as you have the same amount of energy and the total amount of charge , you can make any material .
比如說這個弱子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生	for example , this weak particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .
在之後的相互作用中載荷必須保持平衡	in later interactions , charges must remain balanced .
一個弱子可以衰退成一個電子和一個反中微子而這三個的總載荷仍然是零	a weak man can decay into an electron and an antimicroneutrino , and these three charges remain zero .
大自然總是會保持完美的平衡	nature always keeps a perfect balance .
所以這些電荷的圖案不僅漂亮	so these charge patterns aren't just beautiful .
還告訴我們什麼樣的相互作用是符合規則的	and tell us what kind of interactions are made to fit rules .
如果在四維空間中旋轉載荷空間可以從更好的角度觀察強相互作用也就是這個美麗的對稱六角形結構	if you rotate the charge space in four dimensions , you can look at the strong interaction from a better angle , which is this beautiful hexagonal symmetry .
在強相互作用中強子比如說這個會和色夸克相互作用比如這個綠夸克這樣的作用會讓夸克帶上不同的色荷比如這個紅夸克	in strong interactions , the strong forces , such as this one , interact with the colored quark , such as this green quark , that cause the quarks to carry different color charges , such as this red quark .
強相互作用每秒鐘會在我們身體的每個原子裡發生上百萬次使原子核保持一體	strong interactions occur millions of times in every atom of our bodies , keeping atomic nuclei one .
但是和三種力相對應的這四種載荷還不是終點	but these four charges correspond to three forces are not the finish line .
我們還可以根據重力匯入兩個載荷	and we can also convey two charges according to gravity .
匯入後每個粒子會有自旋向上和自旋向下兩種自旋載荷	when each particle comes in , it's spinning upwards and spinning down two spin charges .
若把它們全部分開會在六維載荷空間中形成漂亮的圖案	and if you split them all up , they form beautiful patterns in sixdimensional charge spaces .
在六維空間中將這個圖案進行旋轉我們會發現它十分漂亮	we're going to rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and we'll see it's pretty .
這個圖案把我們已知的自然界在微觀世界中的粒子組成完全呈現出來了	this pattern reveals the particles that we already know in the microscale world entirely .
這是我們能確定的	this is something we can be sure of .
其中的一些粒子在實驗中很難看到	some of these particles are very hard to see in experiments .
從這個圖案中我們瞭解了微觀世界的粒子組成宇宙在這種微觀世界中的執行模式是異常美麗的	from this pattern , we understand that particles in the microworld are executed in such a microworld that the executive pattern of the universe is incredibly beautiful .
接下去我想講一下關於未知領域的一些新老觀念	so i'm going to give you a little bit of a new idea about the unknown .
我們把這個圖案用數學方法進一步擴充套件看看能不能俯瞰全貌	we take this pattern and we expand it in a mathematical way , and see if we can look at the whole thing .
我們希望找到構成宇宙的所有種類的粒子和力	we want to find all the particles and forces that make up the universe .
然後在獲得更高能量進行實驗之前用這幅圖案預測新的粒子	and then , before you get higher energies , you use this pattern to predict new particles .
量子物理學的舊觀念認為這個不對稱的載荷圖案源於一個更完美的圖案跟希格斯粒子使電弱圖案分裂產生電磁力是一個道理	the old idea of quantum physics is that this asymmetric charge pattern comes from a more perfect pattern , and the higgs particles divide the pattern to generate electromagnetic force .
因此我們要匯入含有新的載荷方向的新的力	so we're going to combine new forces with new charge directions .
在匯入新方向的時候我們要猜測在這個方向上粒子帶有什麼樣的載荷然後我們就能讓它和其他粒子一起旋轉	and in the new direction , we have to guess what charges the particles carry in this direction , and then we can rotate it along with other particles .
如果猜對的話我們就可以在六維載荷空間中構造標準載荷集作為更完美的七維載荷空間圖案的非對稱子集	if we guess right , we can construct standard charges in sixdimensional charge spaces as a nonsymmetrical symmetry for the patterns of the
這種粒子選擇方法由帕蒂和薩拉姆在1973年提出它是大統一理論的一種探索	it was chosen by pati and salam in 1973 , and it was an exploration of the unified theory .
在我們看到這個新的合成圖案時發現有些空間應該有粒子卻空出來了	and when we look at this new synthetic pattern , we see that there are spaces that should be particles , but they're empty .
這是統一理論的研究方式	this is how the unified theory works .
物理學家將已有的結構作為子集探索更大更對稱的結構	physicists will explore larger , more symmetrical structures as subset .
這個更大的結構可以讓我們預測那些實際存在卻沒有被觀察到的粒子	this much larger structure allows us to predict the particles that actually exist but don't .
這個統一模型推測出了這兩種新子對應的粒子它們應該和弱力很相似但是效果更弱	this unification model suggests that these two new types of particles should be similar to the weak force , but they're even weaker .
現在可以在七維空間中旋轉這個載荷集同時考慮一下關於粒子的奇怪現象:在六維載荷空間中物質的第二代和第三代擁有和第一代物質相同的載荷	now we can rotate this episode in seven dimensions , and consider the strange phenomenon of particles: the second generation of matter in sixdimensional charge space and third generations have the same charge as the first generation .
這些粒子透過對應的六個載荷無法一一識別	these particles can't identify by corresponding to six charges .
在標準載荷空間上他們會彼此疊加	in the standard charge space , they overlap each other .
然而在八維載荷空間中我們可以賦予每一個粒子唯一的新載荷	however , in eightdimensional charge space , we can give each particle the only new charge .
然後在八維空間中旋轉看看整體的圖案是什麼樣的	and then rotate in eight dimensions and see what the overall pattern looks like .
這裡我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代透過一種叫 " 三重性 " 對稱和第一代相關聯	here we see the second generation of matter and third generations associated with the first generation through a symmetry called " triplicity . "
在八維中的這個特殊的載荷圖案是數學中最為漂亮的幾何結構之一	this particular charge pattern in eight dimensions is one of the most beautiful geometric structures in mathematics .
這是最大的例外型李群e8的圖案	this is the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .
李群是光滑曲線形的248維空間	lie groups are 248dimensional spaces of smooth curves .
圖案的每一點都能這個極其複雜而又美麗的圖案中找到對稱點	each point in the pattern can be found in this incredibly complicated and beautiful pattern .
e8中的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論中用來解釋重力的扭曲時空	a small part of e8 can be used to describe the distortion of gravity in einstein's general theory of general relativity .
這個幾何形狀和量子力學一起能夠以最小的尺度描述萬物之理	this geometry , together with quantum mechanics , is able to describe everything at the smallest scales .
而在八維載荷空間中的這個圖案顯得異常美麗它還囊括了上千種這些基本粒子之間可能的相互作用每一種作用只是這個複雜形狀的一個平面	and this pattern in the eightdimensional charge space shows an extraordinary beauty , and it includes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each acting as a complex shape .
轉動它時可以看到包含其中的很多錯綜複雜的圖案	and as you rotate it , you can see many of these intricate patterns contained .
透過某種旋轉我們可以在八維空間沿一個對稱軸方向觀察這個圖案並且一次看盡所有粒子	through some kind of rotation , we can look at this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .
這是個很美的結構和其他統一理論一樣我們可以看到在這個圖案中有一些空格需要新的粒子來填補	it's a beautiful structure , and like any unification theory , we can see that there are empty spaces in this pattern that need new particles to be filled .
在這有20個空格需要新粒子來填補其中兩個已有帕蒂和薩拉姆粒子填補	there are 20 gaps that need new particles to be filled , two of which have been filled with patty and salaam particles .
從圖案的位置我們知道這些新粒子和希格斯粒子一樣存在於標量場中但是它們擁有色荷且和強力相互作用	from the location of the pattern , we know that these new particles are like the higgs particles in the quantum field , but they have color charge and interact with strong forces .
填入這些新粒子使圖案完整讓我們得到完整的e8	we fill in these new particles , and the pattern is complete , and we get an entire e8 .
這個e8圖案有著深厚的數學根基	this e8 pattern has a thick mathematical root .
在數學界中它被很多人認為是最美麗的結構	in mathematics , it's thought to be the most beautiful structure among many people .
有人預言這個擁有無比數學美的結構能夠以我們可以想象到的最小尺寸描述粒子相互作用的真相	some people predict that this structure with incredible mathematical beauty can describe the interaction of particles at the smallest scale that we can imagine .
而這個數學描述自然的理論並不是剛剛出來的	and this mathematical description of nature is not just coming out .
1623年伽利略寫道: " 大自然這本一直展示在我們面前的書是用數學的語言寫的	in 1623 , galileo wrote , " nature has been shown to be written in the language of mathematics .
它由三角形圓形和其他幾何形狀組成沒有了這些東西在人力所及的範圍裡我們根本不能瞭解沒有了這些我們會迷失在黑暗的迷宮中 "	it's made up of triangles and circles and other geometric shapes that are not understood in the range of human achievements , and we are lost in the dark labyrinth . "
我相信這是真的我曾試過按照伽利略的指導只用三角形圓形和其他的幾何形狀去描述量子物理的數學性	i believe this is true , and i've tried to describe the mathematics of quantum physics using only triangle circles and other geometric shapes .
當我和其他物理學家在研究這些東西時數學就像一個黑暗的迷宮	and while other physicists and i were studying these things , mathematics was like a dark labyrinth .
但是我們確信數學的核心是純粹美麗的幾何學	but we're convinced that the core of mathematics is purely beautiful geometry .
數學和量子力學一起把我們的宇宙描述為一個在成長的e8珊瑚同時粒子在每個可能的位置相互作用展現出美麗的圖案	mathematics and quantum mechanics together describe our universe as a growing e8 coral , while particles interact in every possible position .
藉助大型強子對撞機之類的新型機器圖案得到進一步豐富我們可能看到到底e8圖案還是另一種圖案反映了自然的本質	with new machine patterns like the large hadron collider , we might see e8 patterns or a different pattern reflecting nature .
這個探索過程是一個奇妙的探險	this process of exploration is a wonderful adventure .
如果對撞機發現了符合e8圖案的粒子那可太酷了	if the lhc finds particles that fit the e8 pattern , that's pretty cool .
如果對撞機發現了新粒子但不符合這個圖案那會非常有趣雖然對e8理論不利	if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't match the pattern , that's very interesting , although theory is bad for e8 .
而且在一定程度上對我不利	and in a way , it's bad for me .
那到底有多不利呢 ?	how bad is that ?
恩那是十分的不利啊	well , that's very bad .
但推測大自然的運作總是很冒險的	but it's always adventurous that nature works .
這個理論和其他這型別的理論都是在下大注	it's a theory , and it's a whole other theory , and it's all about paying attention .
即使花很多精力取得很多成果也不一定能得出自然的真理	even with a lot of effort , it doesn't necessarily come to a natural truth .
理論物理就是這樣失敗是很常見的	that's how theoretical physics works . it's very common .
這樣看來新物理理論就像新開的公司	in this way , new physics theories are like startup companies .
巨大投資後對那些失敗的嘗試情感上總會難以割捨	after enormous investments , it's emotionally hard to get rid of those attempts that fail .
但在科學界如果沒有用就要丟掉它再試試別的	but in science , if it doesn't work , throw it away and try something else .
而在這些不確定中唯一能夠保持理智並獲得幸福的方法是在生活中保持平衡和明察事理	and in these uncertainties , the only way to be rational and acquire happiness is to keep balance and perspective in life .
我已經儘可能保持生活的平衡了	i've kept my life as balanced as possible .
我試著在物理愛情和衝浪中尋找平衡就是我三個載荷的方向	i tried to balance my own three charges in physical love and surfing directions .
這樣就算我的物理研究沒有任何成果我依然擁有美好的生活	so even if my physics didn't work , i still had a good life .
我試著在風景優美的地方居住	i'm trying to live in a beautiful place .
過去十年我大部分時間都住在毛伊島一個超級漂亮的地方	i've spent most of the last decade living in the island of maui , a very beautiful place .
現在我父母最大的謎團是我是怎樣在沒有一個全職工作的情況下活下來的	now , the greatest mystery of my parents is how i survived without a fulltime job .
我要告訴你們這個秘密	i'm going to tell you the secret .
這是我在毛伊島上的家庭辦公室的照片	this is a picture of my family's office on maui .
你們可能注意到這些照片似曾相似但背景稍有不同	you may notice that these images were similar , but backgrounds were slightly different .
因為這曾經是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室	because this was my home and office in maui .
我選擇了一種不同尋常的生活	i chose a different kind of life .
不擔心房租讓我把時間花在喜歡做的事情上	not worrying about rent , let me spend my time doing things that i love .
流浪的生活方式有時會很艱難也正因此我才能可生活在美麗的地方維持我所喜歡的平衡的生活	living a nomadic lifestyle can be hard sometimes , and because of that , i can live in beautiful places and maintain the balance that i like .
我可以花大量的時間在超級聰明的珊瑚上	i could spend a lot of time on superintelligent corals .
同時我也很樂意和超級聰明的人打交道	and at the same time , i would love to talk to hyperintelligent people .
很高興能被邀請到這兒演講	it's great to be invited to speak here .
我想我只懂了百分之二的部分 , 但是我絕對喜歡它 。 所以我想獻一下醜 。	i think i know only two percent , but i absolutely like it . so i'd like to give it a little ugly .
你的萬物理論...我喜歡稱之為珊瑚理論	your theory of everything i like to call it coral .
好吧 , 它讓人們興奮的原因是如果你是對的 , 那就把重力和量子理論結合了起來 。	well , the reason it gets people excited is that if you're right , it combines gravity and quantum theory .
所以你是不是說我們應該瞭解在宇宙中那些最微小的事物有可能就是e8模型 ?	so are you saying that we should understand that the tiniest things in the universe might be e8 ?
我是說 , 你心裡是不是有一個最小的尺寸 , 還是.... ?	i mean , did you have a smallest size in your mind or . . .
嗯 , 剛剛給你們看得圖案就是我們所知的基本粒子物理 , 而且它已經是一個很漂亮的圖案了 。	well , the pattern i showed you is what we know about the fundamental particle physics , and it's already a beautiful pattern .
那個就是我所說的我們很確信的地方 。	that's what i'm talking about . we're pretty sure .
而這個形狀和e8有著明顯的相似處 , 在剩下的圖片中幾乎和e8合為一體 。	and this shape has a remarkable similarity to e8 , almost integrated into the rest of the picture .
我給你們看得這些點狀圖案實際上代表著高維物體的對稱性 , 這些圖案在我們生活的時空中 , 蜷曲 , 移動和舞蹈 。	i'm showing you these spot patterns that actually represent the symmetries of highdimensional objects that curl up and move and dance in the spacetime we live .
這就解釋了所有的我們所看見的基本粒子 。	and that explains all the elementary particles that we see .
克里斯:但是就我的理解 , 弦理論家會在更小的弦震動裡解釋電子--我知道你不喜歡弦理論 。	ca: but in my understanding , string theorists explain electrons in smaller string vibrations i know you don't like string theory .
但我們該怎樣理解在e8模型中的電子 ?	but how do we understand electrons in e8 ?
加勒特:不 , 它將會是這個e8型狀對稱性的一部分 。	gk: no , it's going to be part of this e8shaped symmetry .
所以實際上 , 當這個形狀在時空中游走 , 它會扭曲 。 而它扭曲的方向就是我們所看到的粒子 。 所以就是--e8形狀的大小 , 是怎麼樣和電子相聯絡的呢 ?	so actually , when the shape is swimming through spacetime , it's warping . and the direction it's distorting is the particles that we're seeing . so that's the size of the e8 shape , how is it contacting the electron ?
我自己有些想象不出來 。	i couldn't think of it myself .
它會大些還是小些 ?	is it bigger or smaller ?
嗯 , 就我們所知電子是點粒子 , 所以這個會讓我們看到最小的尺寸 。	well , as far as we know , electrons are point particles , so that's the smallest thing we're going to see .
所以在量子場論中 , 這些東西的解釋方式是所有的可能性都在同時展開發展 。	so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is that all the possibilities are unfolding simultaneously .
這也是我為什麼拿珊瑚作類比 。	that's why i'm analogizing corals .
因為這樣 , e8的進入方式是一個可以連線時空中每一點的形狀 。	because of that , the way e8 comes in is it's a shape that connects every bit of dot in spacetime .
還有 , 想我所說的 , 形狀在經過這個曲線的表面時它的扭曲的方式和其的扭曲方向是基本粒子它們自己 。	and as i said , the shape twists in the surface of this curve and its distortion in the direction of the fundamental particles themselves .
所以根據量子場論 , 它們自己把放大到和點一樣 , 然後相互作用 。	so according to quantum field theory , they zoom in on themselves and interact with each other .
我不知道我能不能解釋得更加清楚了 。	i don't know if i can explain that better .
克里斯:沒關係 。	ca: that's ok .
它已經激起了我們的興趣 。 我確定我想了解的更多 。	it's really piqued our interest . i'm sure i want to understand more .
太感謝你的光臨了 。 你的演說太吸引人了 。	thank you so much for coming . your talk is so fascinating .
研究黑猩猩的傳奇人物珍•古道爾講述有關tacare計劃以及她別的社群計劃 , 藉助這些計劃 , 在日益繁榮的非洲城鎮 , 人與瀕危動物可以和睦相處 。	studying the chimpanzee legend jane goodall talking about the tacare plan and her community project , and by helping these programs , humans and endangered african towns can work alongside in increasingly thriving africa .

下午好 , 晚上好	good afternoon , good evening .
或者我們也可以說 , jambo , gutenabend , bonsoir , 又或者......	or we can say , gunbo , gumbo , tenabend , bonsoir , or . . .
黑猩猩在晚上睡覺前就是這麼打招呼的	that's how the chimpanzees greet before they go to sleep at night .
你聽見這種叫聲從山谷這頭傳到那頭從一群猩猩窩傳到另一群猩猩窩	you're hearing this call , from the valley , to the point where you get from one group of chimpanzee nests to another group of chimpanzees .
我今晚的演講想從澤雷•阿蘭希格昨天留下的話題開始	i want to start my talk tonight with jersey alanshig yesterday .
他談的是這個令人驚異的靈長類幼仔 , 叫selam , 三歲大	he was talking about this amazing primate , selam , threeyearold primate .
我們還聽了透過測繪dna基因所得的人類的歷史和族譜	we've also heard the history and family trees of the human dna gene by mapping the dna gene .
已故古生物學家路易斯•李奇是他把我引上研究黑猩猩之路的	the late paleontologist louis leakey was the path to study chimpanzees .
回顧過去 , 這條路實在不同尋常	looking back in the past , it's an extraordinary path .
現在看來比較普通可他的論據是 , 因為他曾尋找在非洲的早期人類化石遺蹟	now it looks more ordinary , but his argument is that he looked for early human fossil miracles in africa .
這些化石上 , 從附屬肌肉的形狀上 , 對於那些早期人類的模樣像什麼都能給研究者很多啟示從由他們身邊發現的原始工具上可以看出一些關於他們生活方式的端倪	these fossils , from the shape of the attachment muscles , give researchers a lot of revelations , from the primitive tools that they've discovered around them , and you can tell a little bit about their lifestyle .
但他們的行為表現是什麼樣的 ? 這是他想知道的	but what is their behavior like ? that's what he wanted to know .
當然 , 行為沒有在化石裡體現	of course , behavior doesn't appear in fossils .
他辨稱如果我們發現當代人類在行為模式上與和其最相近的物種巨猿相似或者相同那麼或許這些行為在大概七百萬年前在似猿似人的祖先身上存在過	he recognizes that if we find ourselves in a modern mode as similar to their most apelike species , then maybe these behaviors existed in an apelike ancestor about seven million years ago .
因此 , 也許我們身上的那些行為特徵是從遠古時代傳下來的	so , maybe the behavioral features that we have in our bodies have come from ancient times .
噢 , 如果你看一下現在講人類進化的書就會常常發現 , 人們是基於黑猩猩的行為表現來思考早期人類可能的行為方式	oh , if you look at the books that we have evolved today , it's often discovered that people are based on the behavior of chimpanzees to think about the way that early humans behave .
與別的存活動物相比 , 他們更像我們這一點我在這次ted會議中聽到過	they're more like us than any other activity , which i've heard at this ted conference .
所以我今天要講的就是黑猩猩是在其行為方式的與人類的相似點	so i'm going to talk to you today about how chimpanzees behave in the same way they behave .
每個黑猩猩都有他/她自己的個性	every chimpanzee has him or her own personality .
當然 , 我給他們起名字 。 他們能活60歲或者更長儘管我們覺得他們中的絕大多數在野生環境活不到60歲	of course , i gave them names . they lived 60 or more , although we think the vast majority of them lived under 60 in the wild .
這是wurzel猩猩 。 母猩猩在11或12歲時生第一個孩子	this is wurzel chimpanzees . females gave birth to their first baby when they were 11 or 12 .
之後每五年或每六年她只生一仔這麼長的童年期內小猩猩很有依賴性 , 需要照料晚上和媽媽一起睡 , 騎在她背上	and every five years or six years , she's got this long childhood , and the chimpanzees are dependent on it , and they're taking care of it at night with their mom and riding on her back .
我們認為這麼長的童年期對黑猩猩很重要 , 這牽涉到學習 , 就像童年之於我們一樣	we think this longterm childhood is so important for chimpanzees , and it involves learning , like our childhood .
在各種不同形態動物的進化過程中由於大腦變得日益複雜我們發現 , 在一種個體的生命歷程中學習的作用日益重要	in the evolution of all different forms of animals , because the brain becomes more and more complex , we found that learning is increasingly important in an individual's lifespan .
年紀小的黑猩猩花很長時間觀察它們的長輩做什麼	young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .
我們現在知道 , 他們能模仿所見的行為表現	we now know that they can mimic how they behave .
我們認為正是由此從那些在非洲研究的所有不同黑猩猩種群身上看到的使用工具的不同行為這些行為是怎樣透過觀察、模仿和實踐從一代傳到另一代的所以 , 我們可以把這些使用工具的行為說成是原始文化	and we think it's that way , from all of the different behaviors that we've seen in africa , in chimpanzee groups of africa , how these behaviors , through observations , imitation and practices , from generations to generations , so that we can take these tool use behaviors as primitive cultures .
黑猩猩沒有語言 , 我們以前提到過	chimpanzees don't have language . we talked about it before .
但他們確實有一整套非常豐富的姿態和動作其中許多與我們的很像 , 甚至一模一樣並且具有相同涵義黑猩猩打招呼時會擁抱	but they do have a very rich set of gestures and motions , many of which are very similar to ours , even identical , and embrace when chimpanzees say hello .
他們也親吻、牽手、一個拍另一個的背	they also kiss , hold hands , pat one on the other .
他們也虛張聲勢地恐嚇 , 或者仍石頭	they're also terrified , or they're still rocky .
在黑猩猩的社會里 , 我們發現很多很多憐憫、示愛以及真正利他的例子	in chimpanzee societies , we found a lot of compassion , love and real altruism .
和我們一樣 , 不幸的是 , 他們也有天性中陰暗的一面	unfortunately , like us , they have a dark side of their nature .
他們可以極度兇殘 , 甚至像一種原始戰爭	they can be incredibly brutal , even a primordial war .
多數情況下 , 這些極具攻擊性的行為是直接針對相鄰社群中個體的	in most cases , these extreme aggressive behaviors are directly targeted to individuals in adjacent communities .
這些攻擊大多是為了爭奪地盤	most of these attacks are to compete for territory .
我覺得 , 與別的生物相比黑猩猩更有助於我們認識到 , 人類和動物王國裡的其他成員終歸併無明顯界限	i think it's even helpful to realize that humans and other members in the kingdom of animals remain inexplicable .
這種界限非常模糊 , 並且隨著我們更多的觀察會一直更加模糊下去	the boundaries are very blurred , and as we get more observations , they stay blurred .
我1960年開始的研究一直持續到現在	i started my research in 1960 , and it's been going on .
這些黑猩猩在野生環境過著複雜的社會生活最重要的是 , 他們幫助我們認識到 , 我們與形形色色的動物在地球上共處 , 我們是其中一部分不能與這些動物分割開來	these chimpanzees have a complicated social life in the wildlife environment , and most importantly , they help us realize that we share a color with animals on earth , and we're part of it that can't be separated from these animals .
所以 , 發現黑猩猩和世界上其他眾多生物一樣失去聚居地 , 是很讓人難過的	so it's sad to find out that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures in the world , are losing places .
這只是一張從空中拍的照片你可以看到森林覆蓋的gombe高地	this is just a photograph from the air , and you can see the gombe highlands covered in the forest .
16年前 , 我走遍整個地區意識到在公園之外 , 這片森林在1960年時沿著tanganyika湖東岸綿延不絕小巧的、面積只有30平方英里的gombe國家公園就坐落在這裡那時一個問題進入我腦海	16 years ago , i traveled all over the region to realize that outside the park , this forest stretched along the east coast of lake tanganyika , 30 square miles of gomb national park , where a problem went into my mind .
" 我們怎麼能進而去試圖拯救這些出了名的黑猩猩 , 而住在國家公園周圍的人卻在為生存而掙扎 ? "	" how can we get there trying to save these famous chimpanzees , and people who live around the national park are struggling to survive ? "
那裡人口眾多 , 非單薄的土地所能承受	there's a lot of people out there , not just thin fields .
隨著來自蒲隆地的難民湧入來自剛果的人跨湖過來 , 住在那裡的人數增加著	as refugees from burundi flooded in from congo crossing lakes , the number of people lived there .
那些人非常窮無力從別的地方買吃的	those are the people who are very , very poor , who are buying it from other places .
一個計劃由此產生 , 我們稱之為 " 關愛 "	and that's where a project arose , which we call love .
它用整體化的方式來改善住在湖周圍村子裡的人的生活	it's integrated to improve people's lives around lake villages .
剛開始是小規模的 , 有12個村子 。 現在是24個	it started out small , with 12 villages . it's 24 .
這裡沒有時間去深入介紹 , 不過該計劃包括象林木苗圃等事情 , 以及適於在山上這片目前嚴重剝蝕幾近沙漠的土地上耕種的方法	there's no time to go into this , but it's a program that includes the beds of the lyndon , and it's appropriate to the mountains that's currently peeling near the landscape of desert .
控制、防止土地侵蝕的方法	control , prevent land erosion .
收回過度使用的農田的方法以便兩年內這些農田可以重新有收成	and the way overused farmland can be recycled in two years , and these farms can be recycled again .
幫助村民從井裡取得淡水	help the villagers get fresh water from the well .
或許建一些校舍	maybe you build some schoolrooms .
我認為最重要的是與小規模群體婦女合作給她們提供微型信用貸款的機會	i think what's most important is working with smallscale groups of women and giving them opportunities for microcredit loans .
全世界的情況一樣 , 在所有貸款中我們收回了大約95%	in the world , we collect about 95 percent of all loans .
使婦女能夠受教育後工作給女孩子提供獎學金 , 以便讓她們完成中學學業很清楚 , 世界各地婦女的教育程度提高了 , 家庭人口數目就會下降	it allows women to be educated and work with scholarships for girls so that they can finish high school , and it's clear that women are educated around the world , and the population is going to decline .
我們提供計劃生育和艾滋病及其病毒方面的資訊	we provide information about planning and reproduction and hiv and its viruses .
這項計劃實施之後自然保護方面發生了一些事情	and when this project was done , something happened to natural protection .
自然保護方面發生的事情是 , 住在這24個村子裡的農民並沒有把我們看成是跑來研究整個一夥兒猴子的一夥兒白人順便說一下 , 現在很多工作人員是坦尚尼亞人而當我們開始 " 關愛 " 計劃時進入村子的是一個坦尚尼亞小組	what's happening to natural conservation is that farmers who live in these 24 villages are not looking at us as being a bunch of white guys , by the way , who are now tanzanians , and when we started the village with love project , it was a tanzanian team .
和村民交談的是一個坦尚尼亞小組詢問村民對什麼感興趣	i talked to the villagers as a tanzanian group and asked the villagers what interests them .
他們對自然保護感興趣嗎 ? 一點也不	are they interested in nature conservation ?
他們對健康感興趣 , 他們對教育感興趣	they're interested in health . they're interested in education .
隨著時間推移 , 隨著他們境況開始改善他們開始不斷理解更多有關自然保護的必要性	over time , as their circumstances began to improve , they began to understand more about the need for natural protection .
他們開始理解當山上較高位置的數被砍光以後可怕的土地侵蝕和泥流就來了	they began to understand that when the higher numbers on the mountain were cut off , the horrible land eroded and mud streams came .
現在 , 我們正在開發所說的大gombe生態系統	now , we're developing what we call the biggombe ecosystem .
這是一片國家公園以外的地區綿延包括了所有這些各種各樣剝蝕了的土地	this is an area outside the national park that's extended , including all these different lands that have eroded .
由於這些村子生活標準高一些他們實際上同意把他們土地的10-20%放到高地一側以便當樹長回來時黑猩猩會再次擁有綠色走廊它們可以藉此穿行以便這是他們基因繁殖所必需的與國家公園外其它殘餘群體互動	and because these villages live a little bit more standards , they actually agree to put 10 to 20 percent of their land on the high ground , so that when the trees come back , the chimps will have green corridors , and they'll be able to wear them so that this is what they need to reproduce and interact with the rest of the community outside of the national park .
所以 " 關愛 " 計劃成功了	so the love project succeeded .
我們在非洲其它地區複製這項計劃在其它面臨極端人口壓力的荒野之地	we replicated this program in other parts of africa in other parts of the land of extreme population pressure .
但是 , 就像我們在ted開始的所有這幾天一直討論的非洲的問題是主要問題	but , as with all of the problems that we've been discussing here at ted over the last few days , the problem is the main problem .
那裡非常貧窮	it's very poor .
有大量的人生活在不那麼肥沃的土地上尤其當你把樹砍倒使得土壤裸露 , 任風侵蝕同時處於絕望的人砍倒越來越多的樹以便為他們自己和家人努力培育糧食這樣會發生什麼 ? 有些東西會開始犧牲讓步	there are a lot of people living on less fertile grounds , especially when you cut down trees and you erode the soil , and people who are in despair are falling down more and more trees for themselves and their families , and what happens when something starts to sacrifice them .
還有別的問題不僅在非洲而且是其它所有發展中世界 , 甚至是地球上所有地方我們在對我們的地球做什麼呢 ?	there are other questions not only in africa , but in all the developing world , and in all the places on earth , what are we doing to our planet ?
著名科學家 , e.o.威爾遜說過 , 如果地球上每個人的生活標準都達到歐美平均水平我們就再需要三個地球	the famous scientist , e . o . wilson , said that if everybody on this planet had a standard of living in the u . s . average , we would need three more planets .
今天他們說是四個 。 可我們沒那些個 , 我們只有一個	today they say it's four . we don't have those . we only have one .
發生了什麼 ? 我是說 , 這裡的問題是 , 我們在這裡或許可稱為地球上有史以來最有智慧的生命有著非凡的大腦能夠運用這些ted會議上闡述備至的這些技術但我們卻在毀壞著這個惟一的家園	what's going on here ? i mean , the question here is , we might call the most intelligent life on earth the most intelligent life on earth , with extraordinary brains capable of using these ted conferences to describe these equipment techniques , but we're destroying this single home .
全球各地的原住民在做重要決定前都會坐到一起 , 然後問 " 這決定如何影響我們接下來的七代人 ? "	indigenous peoples around the world would sit together before making important decisions , and ask , " how does this decision affect the next seven generations ? "
今天 , 重要決定我這裡不特別談非洲而是發達世界牽涉幾百萬美元以及以及幾百萬人的重要決定卻只是問 " 這會如何影響下次股東大會 ? "	today , it's important that i don't talk about africa , but the developed world involves millions of dollars and millions of people's important decisions , and it just asks , " how does this affect the next shareholder meeting ? "
這些決定卻影響非洲	these decisions affect africa .
當我開始遊歷非洲談論黑猩猩面臨的問題及其日益消逝的森林我愈來愈意識到如此之多的非洲問題是如何與以前的殖民開發有關的	as i started traveling around africa talking about chimpanzees and their increasingly dying forests , i became aware of how africa's problems were associated with its past colonial development .
因此我開始在非洲之外旅行 , 在歐洲演講在美國演講 , 去亞洲	so i started traveling outside africa , speaking in europe , speaking in the united states , going to asia .
每一地都有這些糟糕的問題	everywhere , there's these terrible problems .
你知道我說的是什麼問題 , 這包括汙染問題	you know what i'm talking about , including pollution .
我們呼吸的空氣經常毒害我們	the air that we breathe constantly poisons us .
泥土毒害我們的食物	mud poisons our food .
水水也許是本世紀我們要面對的最要緊問題之一每一地 , 水都被農業、工業、家用化學制品所汙染全世界都還在噴這些製品似乎沒辦法從過去的經驗獲利	water may be one of the biggest problems that we face in this century , and everywhere , water is polluted by agriculture , industries , home chemicals , and the world is still jetting all over the world , and these products seem to be failing to profit from the past .
紅樹被砍倒海嘯等影響日益加重	redwoods are being cut down , and tsunami is becoming more and more .
我們談過土壤侵蝕	we talked about soil erosion .
我們不計後果地燒過化石燃料連同其它所謂溫室氣體導致了氣候變化	we have burned fossil fuels regardless , along with other socalled greenhouse gases , causing climate change .
終於 , 全世界的人都開始相信有什麼事發生了 , 我們的氣候不對勁兒了	and finally , all over the world , people are believing in what's going on , that something's wrong with our climate .
全球氣候互相牽連	global climate is interconnected .
最受不利影響的是窮人	the worst impact on the poor is the poor .
已經受影響的是非洲	africa has been affected .
在次撒哈拉非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱非常嚴重	in many parts of subsaharan africa , drought is very , very serious .
雨終於下起來時 , 又常常導致洪水及更多的不幸 , 貧窮、飢餓和疾病週而復始	and when the rain finally rises , it often leads to floods and more , and unfortunately , poverty , hunger and disease recovery .
還有很多人住在土地供養不起的地區太窮 , 買不起食物因為全部土地都剝蝕了 , 所以也沒法離開	and there's a lot of people living in remarkable land supplys , too poor to afford food , because all the land is eroded , so there's no way to go .
於是有了沙漠化一點點漫延 , 漫延 , 漫延同時最後的樹也被砍倒	so with desertification , a little bit of desertification , a little bit of delay , and a little bit of delay , and a little bit of delay .
這種事情不光在非洲遍佈全球	this is not just happening all over the world .
所以我不覺得奇怪當我在世界各地旅行時碰到那麼多年輕人 , 他們看上去失去了希望	so i don't think it's surprising that when i travel around the world , there are so many young people who seem to have lost hope .
我們似乎已經失去了智慧 , 那種屬於原住民的智慧	we've lost wisdom , the wisdom of indigenous peoples .
我想問 , 這是為什麼 ?	i wanted to ask , why is this ?
你們覺得在這異常聰明的大腦ted技術作為例證的那種大腦和人的心臟之間會有某種隔絕嗎 ? 用非科學的術語來談談根據愛和同情 。 有隔絕嗎 ?	do you think there's some sort of isolation between the brain and the human heart , that's not scientifically based on love and compassion ?
這些年輕人 , 當我和他們講話時基本上他們要麼情緒低落 , 要麼無動於衷或者痛苦、憤怒他們或多或少說的是同一件事情 " 我們這麼感覺是因為我們覺得你們損害了我們的未來 , 並且我們對此無能為力 。 "	these young people , when i talk to them , essentially they're either unacceptable or painful or outraged , they're saying the same thing more or less , " we feel like it's because we feel like you've damaged our future and we can't do anything about it . "
我們確實已經毀壞了他們的未來	we have certainly destroyed their future .
我有三個小孫子 , 每次看著他們我就想 , 從我像他們那麼大以來 , 我們是如何損害這個美麗的地球的我感覺到這種絕望	i have three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them , i think , how we've damaged this beautiful planet since i was as big as them , and i feel this despair .
我們由此開展這項我們稱之為 " 根與芽 " 的計劃恰好始於這裡 , 坦尚尼亞現在已經傳播到世界上97個國家	so we started this project called roots and shoots , which we've just started , and here , tanzania has now spread to 97 countries around the world .
專案的名字是具有象徵意義的根造就堅實的基礎	the name of the project is a symbolic root , and it's a very strong foundation .
芽看上去細小 , 在陽光照耀下卻可穿破磚牆	shoots look tiny ; the sun shines through brick walls .
磚可以看成是我們給地球造成的環境的和社會的問題這是希望的訊息	bricks are the kind of environmental and social issues that we've created on earth , and that's the message of hope .
世界各地成千上萬的年輕人可以取得突破 , 為了所有生物 , 讓這個世界更美好	hundreds of thousands of young people around the world can achieve breakthroughs , make the world a better place for all living things .
" 根與芽 " 的最重要訊息每一天 , 我們每一個人都在改變世界	the most important message of roots and shoots is that every day , every single one of us is changing the world .
我們有一個選擇這屋子裡我們每一個人我們都有一個選擇 , 關於我們想做些什麼來改變世界	we have an option for each and every one of us in this room , and we have a choice about what we want to do to change the world .
很窮的人沒有選擇我們要改變這些事以便窮人也有選擇	very poor people have no choice . we have to change those things so that the poor have choices .
" 根與芽 " 小組都選三個方案	the roots and shoots group choose three programs .
取決於成員年齡 , 所在國家在城市還是鄉下 , 來選不同的方案	it depends on member age , in the country , in the country , in the country , in the country , in the country , to choose a different solution .
基本上 , 我們現在的計劃從學前一直到大學愈來愈多的成人開始建立他們自己的 " 根與芽 " 小組	basically , our project right now goes from school to college , and adults are starting to build their own roots and shoots groups .
每個小組在彼此之間選擇三種不同的方案 , 來創造更加美好的世界承認所有這些不同問題是互相聯絡彼此影響的	each group chooses three different programs between them to create a better world acknowledging that all of these different problems are contacts and influence each other .
因此他們的方案之一將會幫助他們自己的人類社群	so one of their programs is going to help them have their own human community .
然後 , 如果他們能幹 , 他們可以籌集資金幫助世界上其它地區的社群	and if they can do it , they can raise funds to help communities in other parts of the world .
他們的方案之一將會幫助動物不光是野生動物也包括家養動物	one of their solutions will help the animals , not only the wildlife , but the domestic feeding animals .
他們的方案之一將會幫助我們共處的環境	one of their solutions is going to help us live together .
交織在所有這些方案中的訊息是學著與我們自己、家庭、社群和諧相處 , 包括國家之間 , 不同文化之間不同宗教信仰之間 , 以及我們和自然世界之間	the message of all of these programs is to learn to harmonize ourselves , families , communities , and nations , between cultures , between religious beliefs and between us and the natural world .
我們需要自然世界我們不能繼續象現在這樣破壞世界了	we need the natural world , and we can't continue to destroy it this way .
我們只有一個地球	we only have one planet .
就在非洲這裡 , 僅僅選出一個或兩個 " 根與芽 " 小組正在實施的方案只要一個或兩個方案在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果、布拉扎維、獅子山、喀麥隆以及別的團體 。 就象我說的 , 遍佈世界97個國家	here in africa , just one or two roots and shoots groups implemented only one or two programs in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congo , in sierra leone , in cameroon and other groups .
當然 , 他們種樹 , 他們種有機蔬菜	of course , they plant trees . they grow organic vegetables .
他們在難民營養小雞賣雞蛋得些微薄收入或只是把雞蛋給家人吃並覺得自豪和獲得權力因為他們自己種植蔬菜養殖小雞就不再無助 , 不再依賴他人	they raise eggs in refugee camps and sell eggs tiny income , or just give eggs to their families and feel proud and empowered , because they grow their own vegetables , and no longer depend on others .
這個方案在烏干達實施了給予前童軍一些心理上的幫助	this program implemented psychological help in uganda .
實施這些方案讓他們重塑自我	implementing these programs allows them to reinvent themselves .
再一次 , 他們成為社會上的有用一員	and once again , they become useful members of society .
我們也在監獄實施該計劃	we also implemented it in prisons .
所以現在沒時間實施更多的 " 根與芽 " 計劃	so there's no time for more roots and shoots .
哦 , 他們也致力於艾滋病及其病毒方面的工作	oh , they're also working on aids and their viruses .
那是 " 根與芽 " 計劃非常重要的組成部分由大孩子跟小孩子談話	it's a very important component of roots and shoots , and it's partly adults talking to kids .
還有無意懷孕及類似事情年輕人更願意聽別的孩子的 , 而不是成人的	and there's unintended pregnancy and things like young people who are more willing to listen to other children than adults .
希望 。 我周遊世界被問及的就是這個問題 " 珍 , 你見過這麼多可怕的事情 , 你看著你的黑猩猩數量在減少 , 從世紀之交的大約一百萬到現在的不足15萬 。 那麼多其它動物也一樣	hope . the question that i've been asked around the world is this: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , and you're looking at the decline in your chimpanzee population from about a million to 150 , 000 animals .
森林消失 , 過去是森林的地方變成沙漠	the forest disappears . it used to be a place of forest to turn into a desert .
你真的有希望 ? " 嗯 , 有 。	do you really have hope ? " " yeah , yeah .
你不可能來參加象ted這樣的會議 , 卻不報希望 , 對吧 ?	you can't come to a ted conference like this , but you don't wish , right ?
當然 , 有希望 。 希望之一是這令人稱奇的人腦	of course , there is hope . one of the hopes is this amazing human brain .
我是說 , 想一想技術	i mean , think about technology .
我最後還是很激動 , 碰到人們談論堆肥廁所	i ended up getting excited about composting toilets .
這是我愛討論的話題之一	this is one of the topics i love to talk about .
我們就把所有這些水衝下馬桶 , 這很可怕	we just sprinted all these waters down the toilet . it was terrifying .
然後談論了可再生能源 , 非常重要	and then talk about renewable energy , very important .
我們為孩子關心過地球嗎 ?	have we cared about the planet for our children ?

藝術家戴安娜•科恩分享關於塑膠汙染對大海和我們日常生活嚴重影響的事實和一些想法 , 幫助大家來擺脫塑膠包圍圈 。	artist diana kahn shared the fact that plastic pollution has a serious effect on the ocean and on our daily lives to help people get out of plastic surroundings .
consumerism , globalissues , green , missionblue , oceans , plastic	consumerism , global issues , green , missionblue , oceans , playstics .
戴安娜•科恩diannacohen:關於塑膠汙染的嚴峻事實	diane cohen: the tough truth about plastic pollution .
我是個視覺藝術家 , 也是塑膠汙染聯盟的創始人之一 。	i'm a visual artist and one of the founders of the plastic pollution coalition .
過去20年 , 我一直參與塑膠包的工作 , 我藝術創作的原材料是裁製和縫合塑膠 。	for the last 20 years , i've been involved in plastic packets , and the raw material i've created in my art is tailored and sewn plastic .
讓塑膠變為平面和立體型藝術 , 雕塑和藝術裝置 。	it makes plastic flat and threedimensional art , sculpture and art installation .
在與塑膠打交道的八年之後 , 我的一些作品開始開裂碎成許多小塑膠塊 。	eight years after dealing with plastic , some of my work began to break into smaller pieces of plastic .
我想 , " 好極了 。	and i thought , " great .
塑膠就像我們人類一樣短命 。 "	plastic is like us . "
我自學進一步深入瞭解塑膠 , 我的確瞭解到塑膠是個壞材料 。	i've learned to go a little further into plastic , and i do realize that plastic is a bad material .
塑膠碎成許多小塊 , 但它還是塑膠 , 這很糟糕 。	plastic is shredded into lots of little bits , but it's still plastic , and it's terrible .
我們發現有很多塑膠漂浮於大海 。	we found a lot of plastic floating in the ocean .
然而在過去的幾年 , 我知道太平洋垃圾環流和垃圾漩渦 。	however , in the last few years , i know pacific garbage gyres and garbage gyres .
我第一反應--我想這也是多數人的第一反應 , 知道這之後-- " 喔 , 我的上帝 !	my first reaction i think that's the first reaction to most people , who knows , " oh , my god !
我們要去那裡並清理這些塑膠 。 "	we're going to go there and clean up the plastic . "
所以我提議一隻貨船 , 兩隻退役拖網漁船 , 一臺起重機 , 一臺削片機和一臺冷壓機出海 。	so i proposed a cargo ship , two retired trawlers , a crane , an exploiter and a refrigerator .
我計劃是航行到垃圾環流帶 , 提高對於此汙染的高度重視 , 開始回收塑膠 , 切割它變成小片 , 然後冷壓變成塑膠塊 , 它可能被用來作為欠發達社群的建築材料 。	my plan is to navigate to the garbage zone , to raise the high value of pollution , to start recycling plastic , cutting it into smaller slices , then turning it into a plastic chunk , which could be used as an architectural material that owes the community .
我同那些曾去過垃圾環流帶的人們談過 , 他們也曾研究過塑膠汙染對海洋環境的汙染 , 交談之後 , 我開始意識到海上清理塑膠相比起全球每天產生塑膠的生產量就如大海撈針一樣 , 我必須回過頭想想 , 要展望更大的藍圖 。	i spoke with people who've been to the garbage dumpsters , and they've also studied plastic pollution pollution on marine environments , and after talking , i've come to realize that shanghai cleansing plastics is as much plastic as those needles in the ocean every day as the oceans are producing , and i have to go back and think about looking at the bigger blueprints .
真正的解決辦法就是:我們需要在源頭找到解決方法 。	the real solution is that we need to find solutions at the source .
我們需要切斷一次性使用塑膠和一次性塑膠的源頭 , 使得它們在全球範圍內每天不會再進入大海 。	we need to cut the sources of plastic and oneoff plastic so that they don't enter the ocean every day in the world .
看看這個 , 我也知道我非常生氣 。	look at this , and i know i'm angry .
我並不只關心你也可能想象到的在太平洋中部我們現在所知的 , 權威資料是 , 11個垃圾塑膠環流帶 , 遍及世界五大海洋 。	and not only do i care about what you might imagine in the middle of the pacific , authority data is , 11 junk zones spread across five oceans around the world .
我不僅僅是關心塑膠環流帶 , 也包括超市的塑膠包圍圈 。	i'm not just concerned about the plastic circulation but also about the plastic surrounding of the supermarket .
我要去超市 , 所有事物都是塑膠包裝 。	i'm going to the supermarket , and everything is plastic packaging .
所有飲料都是塑膠包裝 , 甚至健康的有機市場 。	all the drinks are plastic packaging , even healthy organic markets .
我也關注在冰箱的塑膠 , 還有塑膠以及濾取塑膠的毒素被我們吃下和吸收到我們身體裡 。	i also focused on refrigerator plastic , and plastic and toxins that filter plastic are eaten and absorbed in our bodies .
我和其他的一群人們都關注這個塑膠汙染問題 , 組建了塑膠汙染聯盟 。	i and a bunch of other people looked at this plastic pollution problem , and we built the plastic pollution coalition .
我們為解決這問題開始許多活動 , 它們中的一些是非常簡單的 。	we started a lot of activity to solve this problem , and some of them were very simple .
其中一個是:在大海 , 我們發現百分80到百分90海洋廢棄物是塑膠 , 然後我們為什麼不稱其為:	one is: in the ocean , we found that 80 to 90 percent of the ocean waste is plastic , and why don't we call it ?
再迴圈 。 關於可持續和再迴圈的環保想法的書籍都是類似的觀點 。	books about sustainability and recycling are similar ideas .
大家扔東西到垃圾桶裡 , 但是從來沒有再想過此事 。	people throw things in the garbage can , but they never thought about it .
現實是什麼呢 ?	what is reality ?
在美國 , 塑膠垃圾回收率少於百分之七 。	in the united states , plastic recycling is less than seven percent .
大家想實際看看 , 特別當塑膠變成塑膠瓶 , 絕大多數塑膠瓶僅被降級回收 , 或者焚燒 , 或運到中國 。	you want to actually see , especially when plastic becomes a plastic bottle , the vast majority of plastic bottles are just being recycled or burned or
當一個塑膠瓶可以被重製成一個塑膠瓶 , 或者重被使用時 , 正是被降級回收 , 使得塑膠瓶被製成小塑膠體 , 使得一個塑膠瓶不再被製成塑膠瓶回收利用 。	when a plastic bottle can be recreated into a plastic bottle , or reused , it's reduced to recycle it so that a plastic bottle can be made into small plastic bottles so that a plastic bottle is no longer recycled .
對我們而言 , 這是個重大問題 。	it's a huge problem for us .
我們關注 , 並讓人們思考的另一件事是我們在原本3個r原則前 , reduce、reuse、recycle , 加了第四個r原則 , 它就是拒絕使用 。	the other thing we looked at and made people think about was that before we had three r principles , reduce , reuse , recycle , plus the fourth rr principle , it was rejection use .
無論何時 , 拒絕使用一次性使用塑膠和即丟塑膠 。	whenever you refuse to use plastic and disposable plastic .
有替代品的使用 。 其中一些是非常老套 。	there are alternative uses . some of them are very old .
我自己現在收集這些很酷的耐熱玻璃容器 , 使用這些而替換高興派和特百惠派塑膠容器來儲存食物 。	i'm now collecting these cool , rehearsal glass vessels using these for replacing pleasure patches and trivial plastic vessels for food .
我知道我這樣做有利於我自己和我的家庭 。	i know that i do it for myself and for my family .
我們選擇使用不鏽鋼瓶和玻璃瓶是很容易的 , 你如果要出門 , 記得帶不鏽鋼瓶 , 讓它灌滿水 , 或者濾過水 , 而不要購買塑膠瓶裝水 。	it's easy to choose to use stainless steel bottles and glass bottles , and if you go out and you take stainless steel bottles and fill it up , or filter water , instead of buying plastic bottles .
我猜我想要告訴大家的是我知道你們大家關於此塑膠汙染知道得很多漂在大海上的塑膠是個嚴重的問題 , 但這是我們做為消費者自身產生的問題 , 我們也能自身解決這問題 。	i guess what i'd like to tell you is that i know you know a lot about this plastic pollution that's a serious problem floating in the ocean , but it's a problem that we're generating as consumers , and we can solve it ourselves .
我們透過提高這問題的意識 , 教導人們選擇可替換性產品 , 能夠解決這問題 。	we're teaching people to choose alternative products by raising the awareness of this problem .
所以無論何時 , 請選擇使用可替換性產品 , 拒絕使用一次性使用塑膠和即丟塑膠 。	so whenever you want to use replaceable products , you refuse to use oneoff plastic and disposable plastic .
我們可以切斷源頭 , 阻止這塑膠汙染到我們的海洋裡 , 透過如上4r行動 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的家園 , 拯救我們自己 。	we can cut the source and stop this plastic pollution into our oceans by saving our oceans by 4rs , by saving our homes , by saving ourselves .
這個演示--來自pattiemaes在麻省理工的實驗室 , 由pranavmistry演示--在ted大受好評 。 這是一個可佩帶的帶有一個投影儀的裝置 , 為我們與周圍環境的互動帶來了新的啟發 。 想象一下《少數派報告》吧 。	this is a demonstration from pattie maes' lab at mit , demonstrated by pranavmistry very well reviewed at ted . it's a pepper belt with a projector that inspires us to interact with the environment around us . think about " minority report . demo , design , interfacedesign , technology	demo , matters , interfacedesign .
pattiemaes演示 " 第六感 " , 劃時代的科技飾品	pattie maes demonstrates " the sixth sense , " the technical jewelry of the age .
有一個問題我思考了很久 , 就是我們能否進化出一種第六感官 。 這種感官可以讓我們快速的便捷的獲得元資訊 , 或者是其他的一些資訊 , 在我們需要做出一些決定的時候 , 這些資訊能幫助我們做出正確的選擇 。	one of the questions that i've been thinking about for a long time is whether we evolved to have a sixth sense that allows us to get metadata quickly , or some of the information that we need to make decisions that will help us make the right choices .
你們可能會說 , 當今的手機不正是如此嗎 ?	and you might say , isn't it the case with mobile phones today ?
但是 , 我不認同 。	but i disagree .
假設 , 當你在ted遇到某人 , ted , 毫無疑問 , 是每年最佳的社交場所 。 難道你會不跟人家握手 , 然後說: " 你能等一會嗎 ? 我要用手機google一下你 。 "	let's say that when you meet someone at ted , ted , certainly the best social space a year , you don't shake hands with people's hands and say , " can you wait ? i google you on my phone . "
或者 , 當你在超市裡 , 站在一排巨大的貨架前 , 面對著各種各樣的廁紙 , 難道你會拿出手機 , 開啟瀏覽器登入一個網站 , 嘗試去決定到底哪一種廁紙才是最環保的 , 最應該買的 ?	or , when you're standing in a supermarket and you're standing in front of a huge array of shelves , facing all kinds of toilet paper , are you pulling out your phone and opening the browser into a website and trying to decide which bathroom paper is the most ecological ?
所以說 , 我們並沒有一個便捷的渠道去獲取這些資訊 , 這些能幫助我們做出應該要幹什麼的最佳決定的資訊 。	so we don't have a convenient channel to get this information that helps us make the best decisions that we should do .
因此 , 我的實驗室的研發團隊完成了一系列的發明 , 在不改變使用者行為的條件下 , 幫助使用者快速簡單的獲取這些資訊 。	so my lab's r&amp ; d team finished a series of innovations that helped user quick access to this information without changing the user behavior .
現在 , 我將這個裝置展示給大家 。 這是我們至今最成功的版本 , 仍然在不斷改進 。	now , i'm going to show you the device . this is the most successful version of our time , and it's still improving .
我現在正佩戴著我們其實是把市面上常見的一些元件組裝在了一起 。 順便提一下 , 目前這個裝置的成本是350美元 。	now i'm wearing something that we're actually putting together some common components on the market , and by the way , the cost of this device is 350 dollars .
我佩戴著一個相機 , 就是一個簡單的網路攝像頭 , 一個便攜的用電池供電的投影儀和一個小鏡子 。	i'm wearing a camera , a simple webcam , a portable battery projector and a small mirror .
這些元件跟我口袋中的手機進行通訊 , 手機作為一個通訊和計算的裝置 。	these components communicate with my phone in my pocket as a communications and computational device .
畫面中 , 是我的天才學生pranavmistry , 他設計並製造了這整套系統 。	in this case , my genius student , pranavmistry , designed and built this entire system .
我們可以看到 , 當他靠近任何表面時 , 資訊就會被投影到表面上 , 他就用雙手來進行操作 。	we can see that when he gets closer to any surface , the information gets projected onto the surface , and he operates with his hands .
系統會跟蹤四個主要的手指 。	the system tracks four major fingers .
在這裡 , 你可以看到他戴著用於標示的指套 。	and here , you can see him wearing advice that he's used for .
如果你想要更美觀 , 可以把你的指甲染成不同的顏色 。	if you want to be more beautiful , you can dye your nails into different colors .
攝像頭會跟蹤這四個手指 , 識別他的任何手勢 , 例如 , 他可以開啟longbeach的地圖 , 進行放大或者縮小等等操作 。	the camera is tracking these four fingers , identifying any gestures , for example , and he can open up a map of long beach to do amplification or shrinking and so on .
這個系統也能識別 " 象徵性手勢 " , 比如 , 當你做出這個 " 拍照手勢 " , 系統就會拍照 , 把你面前的東西拍下來 。	the system also recognizes symbolic gestures , such as when you make this " snapshot gesture , " the system takes pictures and takes pictures of what's in front of you .
當他回到medialab實驗室之後 , 他可以走近任何一面牆 , 投影出他拍的所有照片 , 用各種自然手勢 , 進行整理 , 歸類 , 改變大小等各種操作 。 所有操作都用手勢來完成 。	when he got back to the medaliab lab , he could walk up to any wall and project all the photos that he took , using various natural gestures , organizing them , categorizing them , changing all kinds of operations , all gestures with gestures .
你們當中有些人兩年前在這裡應該看過jeffhan演示微軟的surface系統 , 你們可能覺得:這套系統跟surface看起來很像 。	some of you may have seen jeff han playing a microsoft surface system two years ago , which you might think is very similar to surface .
沒錯 , 這兩套系統都是用自然手勢 , 用雙手來操作 。	yes , both of these systems are manipulated using natural hand gestures , using both hands .

為了尋找健康長壽的秘訣 , 丹•比諾與他的研究團隊研究了世界上被稱為 " 藍區 " 的地方 。 在這些特殊地方 , 老年人能活到創紀錄的年齡並且仍然保持活力四射 。 丹比諾在ted分享了九種使得這些老年人年過一百的普通的飲食和生活習慣 。	to find the secret to healthy longevity , dan bino and his research team studied the world's referred to as blue zone , where older people live to the age of creation records and still remain active , nine of these elderly people shared ages 100 ordinary diet and habits at ted .
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	it's biology , it's time for us to live , it's the life of us .
丹•比諾:如何健康長壽	db: how to live long lives .
一個叫 " 丹麥雙胞胎 " 的研究表明 , 普通人在生物學允許的限度內的壽命 , 僅僅有百分之十是由我們的基因決定的 。	a study called the denmark twins showed that only 10 percent of the time in biology allowed is determined by our genes .
另外的百分之九十則取決於我們的生活方式 。	the other 90 percent depends on our lifestyle .
因此 , 對藍區研究的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就可以得出一個實際的長壽公式 。	so the premise for the blue zone is that if we can find the best way to live long , we can come up with an actual longevity formula .

我們找到健康長壽秘訣的研究方法是與《國家地理》雜誌和國家老齡化研究院的研究人員合作©找出四個人口統計學資訊確切的並且有明確的地理界線的地區tm	we found a way to work with national geographic and national aging researchers at the national aging research institute , and we looked at four demographic information specific and specific geographical boundaries tm .

但首先 , 我想戳穿一些常見的關於長壽的謠言 。	but first , i want to poke some common rumors about longevity .

第二個謠言是 , 擁有能夠幫助我們減緩倒轉甚至阻止衰老的方法	the second rumor is that there are ways in which we can slow down and even stop aging .

過度打網球會損害膝蓋的軟骨你的軟骨永遠不再復原 。	playing tennis balls damage the cartilage of your knee , your cartilage never recovered .

以指數性規律成長 。	grow exponentially .
有點像是那段時間裡我們都有披頭士和老鷹樂隊的相簿一樣我們會複製盒式磁帶並讓朋友們也複製很快 , 代代相傳磁帶現在聽起來過時了	it's kind of like during that time we all had beatles and eagle bands albums , and we copyed box tapes and we let our friends copy them very quickly , modern communications tapes , and now they sound like they're obsolete .

這就是為什麼一個65歲的老人的老化速度是一個12歲孩子的125倍	that's why a 65yearold aging rate is 125 times the rate of a 12yearold .
所以如果沒有什麼能夠減緩或停止老齡化我為何還站在這裡	so if there's nothing to slow down or stop aging , why am i standing here ?

從弗雷明翰研究中我們得知如果你有三個好朋友都肥胖你也有一半肥胖的可能 。	we know from the fremingham studies that if you have three good friends , you're half obese .
所以如果你和不健康的人在一起隨時間推移會受到很大影響 。	so if you're with unhealthy people , the migration is going to be significant over time .
如果你朋友娛樂的主意是體力活動 , 打保齡球或打曲棍球腳踏車或園藝工作 , 他們飲酒適量飲食適度 , 他們投入工作值得信任 , 最後就會對你產生最大影響 。	if your friend's entertainment idea is physical activity , bowling or playing hockey bikes or gardening , they drink alcohol appropriately enough to eat , and they work trustworthy , and they end up having the biggest impact on you .
食物沒有什麼用 , 歷史上沒有一種食物能養活2%的人口 。	there's nothing to use for food , there's no food in history that feeds two percent of the population .
練習專案通常在一月開始十月結束 。	practice projects often end in january .
至於長壽 , 沒有藥片或其他什麼東西能在短期內奏效 。	as for longevity , there's no pill or anything that can be done in the short term .
但當你想到你的朋友是長期的冒險活動時 , 因此 , 它是你為增加壽命和讓生命生機勃勃能夠做的最重要的事情謝謝	but when you think about your friends as the longterm adventures , it's the most important thing you can do to increase your lifespan and make life alive .
能導電的墨水、一<unk>開關就由透明變不透明的窗戶、能播放音樂的果凍--這些東西確實存在 。 catarinamota說:現在是時候嘗試他們了 。 mota將帶領我們認識這些新穎和神奇的材料 , 她說 , 弄清楚這些材料的神奇之處的最好方式就是用它們來做實驗 , 不斷嘗試並樂在其中 。	the transparency windows , the freezing of music that we can conduct electricity , the freezing of transparency — these things actually exist . catari mota says now it's time to try them . mota will lead us to understand these novel and magical materials , and she says , the best way to make sense of these materials is to try and experiment with them and try and experiment with them and try and experiment with them .
creativity , design , technology	it's ivity , it's serious .
catarinamota:玩轉智慧材料	catarina mota: play with smart materials .
我有一位葡萄牙朋友 , 其祖父用一輛腳踏車和一臺洗衣機改裝成一輛汽車供家人乘用 。	i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather used a bicycle and a washing machine to convert into a car for multiplication .
他這樣做 , 一是因為他買不起車 , 但更重要的是因為他知道如何改裝汽車 。	he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but more importantly because he knew how to modify it .
曾經 , 我們都懂得一些機械的工作原理 , 也知道它們是怎麼製造出來的 , 所以我們能夠自己製作和維修它們.或者至少基於我們的瞭解作出明智的購買決定 。	once upon a time , we've all understood some mechanical work principles , and we know how they're made , so we can make them and fix them ourselves , or at least based on our understanding of making wise purchases .
但我們很多這些diy的實用性技能在20世紀的下半葉就流失了 。	but a lot of these diy practical skills were lost in the second half of the 20th century .
但是現在 , 製作者社群和開放資源模式正在把這些物品的工作原理和製造材料的知識帶回到我們的生活中 。 而且我相信我們需要把這些知識帶到下一個層面 , 也就是了解構成這些物品的元件 。	but now , the maker community and the open source model are bringing the principles and the knowledge of the objects back into our lives , and i believe we need to take that knowledge to the next level , the components that understand these things .
我們很多人都知道 , 像紙和織物這樣的傳統材料是什麼做成的 , 以及它們是如何生產的 。	many of us know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of , and how they're produced .
但是現在我們有了一些令人驚歎的未來複合材料-如可以變形的塑膠、可以導電的油漆、可以變色的顏料和可以發光的織物 。	but now we have some remarkable future composite materials such as deformable plastic , conductive paint , variable pigments and glowing fabrics .
下面讓我們來看一些新材料 。	so let's look at some new materials .
這種導電墨水可讓我們 , 拋棄傳統的印刷電路板或電線的方法而直接用導電墨水來畫電路板 。	this conductive ink allows us to discard conventional printed circuit boards or wires directly draw circuit boards using conductive inks .
比如我手裡拿著的這個小裝置 , 是我們用導電墨水做成一個觸控性的感測器 , 一旦接觸人的皮膚 , 這個小燈就會亮起 。	this little device that i'm holding in my hand is we're using conductive inks to make a touch sensor , and once exposed to the skin , this little light will light up .
導電墨水已經被藝術家們應用到創作中了 , 最新的進展表明我們很快就能把它應用在鐳射印表機和鐳射筆中.	conductive inks have been applied to artists , and the latest progress has been shown that we will soon be able to apply them to a laser printer and a laser laser .
這是一張泡浸過無色光漫顆粒丙烯酸的紙.	this is a paper that's bathed in bright colorless pellets of acrylic .
只浸過普通丙烯酸的紙只在其邊緣周圍有漫光現象 , 而這張浸過無色光漫顆粒丙烯酸的紙 , 當我們開燈時漫光會照亮整張紙.	there's only a phenomenon around the edge of the regular acrylic acid that immerses the colorless pellets of acrylicine , and as we turn on the light , it lights up the entire piece of paper .
就目前所知 , 這種材料已經被應用到室內設計和多點觸控系統兩個領域中了 。	as far as we know , this material has been applied to both interior design and multitouch systems .
而熱變色顏料在特定的溫度下會改變顏色 。	and thermodynamic pigment changes color in particular temperatures .
我先把這張東西放到一個電熱板上溫度設定比外界溫度稍高一點然後你可以看到發生了什麼.	i'm going to put this thing on a board a little hotter than the outside world , and you can see what's going on .
除了其它用途 , 這種材料主要用作嬰兒奶瓶的製造 。 它能告訴你什麼時候瓶裡的東西涼到可飲用的溫度 。	except for other purposes , this material is mostly made of baby bottles , and it tells you when things are cool enough to drink .
這些就是我們通常所說的 " 智慧材料 " 的幾個例子 。	these are just a few examples of what we usually call smart materials .
幾年內 , 它們將被應用到很多我們日常使用的物件和科技產品上 。	within a few years , they will be applied to a lot of the objects and technological products that we use every day .
我們也許還不會有科幻小說向我們保證的飛行汽車 , 但是我們能擁有隨溫度變色的牆 , 可以捲起來的鍵盤 , 和一<unk>開關就變不透明的窗戶 。	we may not yet have science fiction flying vehicles to our guarantee , but we can have walls that change temperature , keyboards that curl up , and computers that change transparency .
我是科班出身的社會科學家 , 為什麼今天我在這裡講智慧材料 ?	i'm a social scientist from the kuban , and why am i talking about smart materials today ?
首先 , 我是個製造者 。	first of all , i'm a maker .
我對於東西如何運轉和怎樣製作有好奇心 , 我也相信我們應該對我們這個世界的組成材料有更深的瞭解 , 並且現在 , 我們對於這些構成我們未來的高科技材料瞭解不多 。	i have a curiosity about how things work and how they make , and i also believe that we should know a lot more about the materials that make up our world , and we don't know very much about these hightech materials that make up our future .
要獲得少量的智慧材料是很難的 。	it's hard to get a small amount of smart material .
有關如何使用這些材料的資訊也很少 , 它們是如何製作的資訊就更加少得可憐 。	there's very little information about how to use these materials , and there's less information about how to make them .
目前 , 它們絕大多數都存在於貿易機密和專利中 , 只有大學和大公司才能得到 。	currently , the overwhelming majority of them are in trade secrets and patents that only universities and large companies can acquire .
所以三年多以前 , 我和kirstyboyle發起了一個叫做openmaterials的專案 。	so over three years ago , i started a project called open maternals with kirstyboyle .
在那個網站上 , 我們和想要加入我們的任何人 , 分享實驗 , 釋出資訊 , 鼓勵其他人為此作出力所能及的貢獻 , 並且收集像研究論文和像我們一樣的製造者所製作的教程一類的資源 。	on that website , we're sharing experiments with anyone who wants to join us , releasing information , encouraging others to make the contributions that they can and collect curriculum like research papers and like us make .
我們希望把這一網站做成一個大規模的、集體生成的資料庫 , 蒐集用智慧材料diy的資訊 。	we want to make this website a database of massive , collectively generated data collection that uses information about smart materials , diy .
但是我們為什麼要關心智慧材料是如何工作和它們是用什麼來製造的呢 ?	but why should we care about how smart materials work and what they build ?
首先 , 因為我們無法影響我們不理解的東西 , 我們不理解和不會用的東西還會反過來影響我們 。	first , because we can't influence things that we don't understand , things that we don't understand and don't use are going to influence us .
我們使用的東西 , 我們穿的衣服 , 我們住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活質量上產生深遠的影響 。	the things that we use , the clothes that we we wear , the house that we live in , have a profound impact on our behavior , our health and our quality of life .
所以如果我們將要生活在一個由智慧材料構成的世界中 , 我們就應該知道並瞭解它們 。	so if we're going to live in a world made up of smart materials , we should know and understand them .
第二 , 同樣重要地 , 創新總是來源於修補匠 。	secondly , just as importantly , innovation always comes from craftsmanship .
很多時候 , 是業餘愛好者而非專家 , 發明和改進了諸如山地車、半導體、個人電腦、甚至飛機 。	oftentimes , amateur lovers , not experts , have invented and improved things like mountain vehicles , semiconductors , personal computers , even airplanes .
材料科學的最大挑戰是它的複雜性 , 以及對昂貴的儀器的需求 。	the biggest challenge of material science is its complexity and its need for expensive devices .
但事實並非總如此 。	but that's not always the case .
伊利諾伊大學的兩名科學家在他們發表一篇關於用更簡便的方法制作導電墨水的論文時就明白了這個道理 。	two scientists at the university of illinois published a paper on making conductive inks in a simpler way .
jordanbunker在這一實驗之前是一個沒有任何化學經驗的人 。 他讀了這篇論文後在他的工作間裡用現成的物質和工具重複了這個實驗 。	jordan bunker , before this experiment , was a person with no chemistry experience , and he read this article and repeated this experiment with the offtheshelf substances and tools that he was working on .
他用了一個烤箱 , 而且他甚至在另一個科學家/製造者的教程的基礎上自制了旋渦混合器 。	he used an oven , and he even organized a vortex mixer on the basis of another scientist/maker’s teaching .
後來 , jordan在網上發表了他的實驗結果 , 包括所有他試過的沒成功的東西 , 這樣其他人可以學習然後複製這一實驗 。	later , jordan published his experiments online , including all the unsuccessful things he tried so that others could learn and replicate the experiment .
所以jordan主要創新方式是拿一個在設施齊全的大學實驗室裡創造的實驗 , 然後在芝加哥的一個車庫裡用便宜材料和自制的工具來重複實驗 。	so jordan's main innovation was to take an experiment that was created in a university garage , and then repeat it in a garage in chicago with cheap materials and autonomy tools .
在他發表的實驗結果基礎上 , 其他人可以接著做下去並且設計甚至更簡單的步驟和改進實驗 。	and based on the results that he published , others could go on and design even simpler steps and improvements .
我想分享的另外一個例子她專案的目標是在突出材料富有表現力的特質的同時專注於製造者的創造力和製造技巧 。	another example i'd like to share with you is that her project aims to emerge materials that are expressive and focus on the creativity and the manufacturing skills of makers .
電子工具在教我們東西如何運轉這方面非常有力 , 但是它們設計中傳承下來的約束影響我們學習的方式 。	electronic tools are very powerful in teaching us how things work , but the constraints that they inherit in their designs affect the way that we learn .
所以hannah的方法 , 在另一方面 , 就是創制一系列的技術 , 來創造非常規的東西 , 透過教給我們材料本身的知識 , 把我們從事先設計好的約束中解放出來 。	so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to create a series of technologies to create very regular things by teaching us materials , to liberate us from predetermined constraints .
在hannah眾多令人欽佩的試驗中 , 這個是我的最愛之一 。	this is one of my favorite experiments in hannah's many admirable experiments .
[ " 會說話的紙 " ]我們在這裡看到的只不過是一張紙上面的銅帶連線著一個mp3播放器和一塊磁鐵 。	[ " speech paper " ] what we're seeing here is just a copper belt on a piece of paper with an mp3 player and a magnet .
在麻省理工學院教授marcelocoelho研究的基礎上 , hannah使用各種材料創造了一系列紙質揚聲器 。 從普通的銅帶到導電的織物和墨水 ,	at mit , professor marcelo coelho studies , hannah uses various materials to create a series of paper speakers , from ordinary copper to conductive fabrics and inks .
就像jordan和其他很多製造者一樣 , hannah發表了她的配方並且允許任何人來重複這些實驗 。	like jordan , like so many other makers , hannah released her recipe and allowed anyone to come and repeat these experiments .
但是紙上電子是材料科學中最有前景的分支之一 , 因為它讓我們能創造出便宜又靈活的電子產品 。	but electrons on paper are one of the most promising branches of material science , because it allows us to create cheap , flexible electronics .
所以hannah的手工作品 , 和她分享了她的發現這個事實 , 打開了一扇門 , 通向兼具美學和創新的一系列新的可能 。	so hannah's hand job shared her discovery with her , opening a door to a new series of possibilities that are both aesthetic and innovative .
製造者的有趣之處在於我們創造是出於熱情和好奇 , 並且我們不害怕失敗 。	what's interesting about makers is that we create passion and curiosity , and we're not afraid to fail .
我們通常從非傳統的角度處理問題 , 並且 , 在這個過程中 , 最終發現其他方案或者更好的方法 。	we typically deal with problems from an unconventional perspective , and in the process , we ultimately discover other solutions or better ways .
所以當更多的人願意用新材料做試驗的時候 , 更多的研究者就會願意分享他們的研究成果 ; 有更多的製造商分享他們的知識 , 我們就會有更好的機會來創造造福我們所有人的科技 。	so when more people are willing to do experiments with new materials , more researchers will be willing to share their work ; more manufacturers will share their knowledge , and we will have a better chance to create technology that will benefit all of us .
我的感覺有一點像tednelson在70年代初期的感覺一樣 , 他寫道 , " 你們現在必需懂電腦 。 "	i felt a little bit like tednelson's feeling in the early '70s , and he wrote , " you need to understand computers now . "
那個時候 , 電腦是這些只有科學家關心的大型機 , 沒有人會夢想到放一臺在家裡 。	at that time , computers were these big machines that scientists cared about , and nobody would dream of putting in a home .
所以我今天站在這裡說 " 你們現在必需懂智慧材料 " 有一點奇怪 。	so i stand here today and i say , " you need to understand smart materials a little bit strange .
請記住對於新興科技擁有先發制人的知識是確保我們在對未來的創造中有發言權的最好方式 。	remember that the primary knowledge of emerging technologies is to ensure that our best way to speak upon our future creations .
當我們開車是 , 我們就坐進了一個玻璃氣泡中 , 鎖上門 , 踩下油門 , 依靠眼睛為我們自己導航 。 即使我們僅僅只能看見車前車後的幾輛車 。 但是假如汽車能互換關於位置、速度的資料 , 並運用預測模型來為每一位司機測算最安全的線路呢 ? 詹妮佛海麗構想了一個零車禍的世界 。	when we drive , we sit in a glass bubble , and we lock the door , and we step down the gas gate and navigate ourselves , even though we only see a few cars behind the car , but if the car exchanges data about position , speed and use predictive models to make the safest route for every driver , jennifery seafree's idea of an accident .
詹妮弗海麗:汽車若能交流車禍或可避免	jennifer hay: car accidents , or inevitably .
讓我們來面對一樁事實吧開車是一件危險的事	let's face it: driving is a dangerous thing .
它是我們不願意去想的事物之一但事實上那些神像和平安符世界各地都有人把它們擺在儀表盤的上方這就無意中透露出一個我們都心知肚明的事實	it's one of the things that we don't want to think about , but in fact , those gods , peace and security around the world , are placed above the dashboard , which inadvertently reveals a fact that we all care about .
車禍是死亡的主因尤其在美國16到19歲的美國人群中死亡的主因並且百分之七十五的車禍都與毒品和酒精無關	car accidents are the leading cause of death , especially in the united states between the ages of 16 and 19 , and 75 percent of all car accidents have nothing to do with drugs and alcohol .
沒人能給出確切答案但我記得我第一次出車禍	no one could give the exact answer , but i remember my first time out of a car accident .
我當時還是個開車的新手 , 當時正在外面高速路上開著車 。 我突然看見我前面汽車的剎車燈亮了	i was a new driver , and i was driving outside on the highway , and all of a sudden i saw the brake lights in front of me .
我當時想好吧他減速了那我也減速好了	and i thought , well , he's slowing down , and i'm slowing down .
我踩了剎車	i stepped on the brakes .
但是我前面那個人並不是在減速	but the person in front of me is not slowing down .
他停車了突然停車在高速路上突然停車	he stopped and suddenly stopped on the highway and suddenly stopped cars .
速度從65邁瞬降到0	the speed goes from 65 to zero .
我猛踩剎車	i flashed on the brakes .
我當時感覺到我的車的防抱死系統啟動了但車還在行駛並沒停下來的意思我也知道我的車停不了了安全氣囊也鼓了起來車報廢了但幸運的是沒有人受傷	i felt like my car's defense was initiated , but the car was still running and didn't stop , and i knew that my car stopped , and the airbags were inspired , and fortunately nobody was injured .
但我根本不知道我前面那輛車要停而且我想我們可以比那做得更好	but i had no idea that the car was going to stop in front of me , and i thought we could do better than that .
我想我們透過實現 " 讓汽車之間對話 " 來改變我們的駕駛體驗	i think we can change our driver's experience by making car conversations .
我希望你們能思考片刻思考一下現在的駕駛體驗是怎麼樣的	i want you to think about what the experience of driving is like in a moment .
坐進車裡關上車門你就已經置身在一個玻璃氣泡中	you're sitting in your car , closed the door , and you're already in a glass bubble .
你不能直接感受到你周圍的世界	you can't just feel the world around you .
因為你坐在車這樣一個不小的空間裡	because you're sitting in a car that's a very small space .
你的任務就是導航你只能看見道路的一部分並且以超人類的速度行駛在其他的 " 金屬巨人 " 間	your mission is to navigate , and you can only see part of the road , and drive at the speed of superhumanity in the other metal giants .
對吧 ? 你只能靠雙眼來導航	right ? you can navigate by your eyes .
對你別無他法眼睛並非是用來幹著活兒的但是有些事情你就必須得做 , 比方說 , 你想換個車道那你第一件要做的事是什麼	there's no other way for you to do it , but there's something you have to do , like , you want to change lanes and what you do first .
將眼睛從車道上移開對	remove the eyes from the lane .
將目光從你前進的方向移開轉彎檢查一下盲點然後就一直開根本不注意自己在往哪裡開	turn your eyes from the direction you're moving in , check the blind spot , and keep pausing and noticing where you're going .
所有人都這麼做這是安全的駕駛方式	everybody does that . it's a safe way of driving .

當今的學生常常處在一種環境中這裡 , 他們所學的科目中包含了真與美 , 但是他們所被教授的方法卻是被分割的這種方法使得真和美並不總是那麼明顯 。	students today are constantly in an environment where the subjects they've learned contain truth and beauty , but the way they've been taught is by partition that make truth and beauty not always so obvious .
就像是一道古老的雞湯菜譜 , 烹煮雞肉直到香味通通散去	it's like an ancient chicken soup , cooked chicken until the flavor goes off .
我們並不想對我們學生也這麼做 。	we don't want to do that to our students .
所以我們有機會可以真正開啟教育 。	so we have the opportunity to really open up education .
數年前 , 我接到哈佛大學 , 分子與細胞生物學系robertlue的電話 。 他問我 , 我和我的團隊是否有興趣和願望來真正改變哈佛大學裡的醫學和科學教育方式 。	a few years ago , i got a call from harvard , from the molecular and cellular biology department robert lue , and he asked me if my team and i were interested and wished to really change the way medical and scientific education was done at harvard .
所以我們開始了進行細胞探索的一個計劃 , 這將展示分子細胞生物學中內在的真和美由此學生會有更全面的印像能把所有事情聯絡在一起	so we're starting a program for cellular exploration , which will show the truth and beauty within the molecular cellular biology , where students will have a more holistic impression , where they can connect everything together .

而這些微型機器卻是生命的中心 。	and these micromachines are the center of life .
這些微型機器 , 能讓當今全球奈米工程師嫉妒 , 它們是能自我引導、功能強大且精密嚴謹的裝置它們是由氨基酸鏈所構成的 。	these micromachines allow today's global nanoengineer jealousy , and they are selfdirected , powerful and rigorous devices that are made up of amino acid chains .

所以我們開始研究這些分子到底是如何整合在一起的 。	so we started looking at exactly how these molecules were integrated .
我們想出了一個劇情大綱 , 那就是 , 巨噬細胞正在流過一個毛細血管它們不時接觸著毛細血管管壁它們收集來自細胞散佈在毛細血管管壁上的訊號 , 這個訊號是:在外側 , 有炎症發生 , 巨噬細胞本來是無從得知 。	we came up with a plot , and that is , macrophages are flowing through a capillary blood vessel wall that is constantly exposed to the capillary walls that are collecting signals from the cells spreading across the walls of capillary capillaries , and that signal is: inflammation happens in the outside , and macrophages don't know .

並想出一個辦法 , 能夠真實的表現裡面正在發生的事情 , 但又不是那麼地真實 , 因為實際上細胞中緊密擁擠使這種景象變得不可能 。	and figure out a way to be able to show what's happening in real life , but it's not that real , because it's actually impossible to crowd the imagery in a cell .
我將給您展示的是一段3分鐘的影片這是我們做的影片第一部分的《讀者文摘》版這個計劃尚未完成 , 還需要4 , 5年時間	so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute video , and this is the first part of the video that we did , the " reader's version , " which is not done yet , and it's going to take four or five years .
我請您看這個並看看這些細胞造的路這些小的正在走動的機器 , 是驅動蛋白--它們負載而行在大小比例關係上 , 可以和螞蟻一決雌雄 。	i'd like you to look at this and look at the roads that these small walking machines are driven proteins they're loaded in proportions of size , they're malefemale .
請播放動畫	please play an animation .
但這些賦予細胞內部生機的機器實在令人驚奇 , 他們真的是所有生命的基礎 。 因為所有這些機器都在互相交流 。	but these machines that are giving the inside of the cell are really amazing , and they're really the basis of all life , because all these machines are communicating .
他們互相傳遞資訊	they communicate information to each other .
他們決定細胞裡不同的事件發生 。	they decide that different things happen in the cell .
在空間裡 , 細胞透過利用能讀懂基因的分子從細胞核中帶來資訊 , 從而正確生產出它所需要的部分 。	in space , the cells bring information through the molecules that can read the genes to the nucleus , to properly produce the parts it needs .
沒有任何生命 , 從最小的生命到在坐的各位 , 如果沒有這些小型機器 , 可以存在 。	no life , from the smallest life to the people who are sitting , without these small machines , can exist .
事實上 , 沒有這些機器的話 , chris , 今天的出席狀況將非常慘烈 。	in fact , without these machines , chris , attendance today is going to be incredibly terrible .
這是細胞中fedex快遞人員:	this is the fedex deliveryman in the cell .
這個小傢伙叫驅動蛋白他拉著一大袋新合成的蛋白質 , 到細胞所需要的任何地方--不論它是細胞膜 , 還是一個細胞器也不管是用來搭建什麼 , 還是修復什麼	this little guy's called driving protein , and he's pulling a bag of newly synthetic proteins , anywhere in the cell whether it's a membrane , or a cellular device , whatever it's used for , or what it's repairing .
我們體內每個細胞 , 大約有10萬個這樣的小傢伙此時此刻 , 正在跑來跑去而我們大約有100萬億個細胞 。	we have about 100 , 000 of these cells in our bodies , and right now , we're running around , and we have about 10 trillion cells .
所以無論你覺得自己有多懶本質上 , 你並不是什麼都沒做 。	so no matter how lazy you feel , you don't do anything .
當你回家時 , 我希望你們能夠思考這個問題 , 想想我們的細胞是多麼地強大	and when you go home , i want you to think about this question of how powerful our cells are .
想想我們正在學的細胞機器的種種事情 。	think about all kinds of things that we're learning about cellular machines .
一旦我們全盤瞭解細胞內發生的所有事情相信我 , 我們大概才知道1%而已--一旦我們瞭解細胞內的狀況 , 我們將能更好地控制我們的健康 , 我們的下一代 , 我們的壽命 。	and once we fully understand what's going on inside the cells , believe me , we probably know one percent if we understand what's going on inside the cells , we're going to be able to control our health better , our children , our lives .
並且 , 希望我們可以藉此去發現更多的真和美 。	and hopefully , we can discover more truth and beauty in this way .
這些細胞 , 這些微型機器 , 真的不可思議 , 它們能過意識到細胞需要它們為其做些什麼事情	these cells , these micromachines , are really incredible , and they're aware of what the cell needs to do for them .
他們同心協力 , 它們使細胞能夠完成需要做的事情	they work together , and they make the cells do what they need to do .
他們通力合作才使我們身體--這個他們永遠看不見的巨大整體能夠正常工作 。	they're working together to make our bodies this enormous , invisible whole that they're never going to see , working properly .

貝基布蘭頓計劃在一年裡就在他的小貨車裡住並且遊歷全國 , 但是當沮喪加劇而且自由作家的工作泡湯的時候 , 他的旅營就變成了無家可歸了 。 在這個溫馨的演講中 , 她描述了她作為美國無家可歸的工作者之一的獨特經歷 。	baki branton was planning to live and travel throughout the country for a year , but when depressed and free writers worked bubbles , his travel camp became homeless , and in this beautiful speech , she described her as one of the unique experiences of being homeless workers of america .
adventure , happiness , life , personalgrowth , poverty , socialchange , society , storytelling	" adventure , " " happiness , " " alternately " , " " " life , " " " all of you , " all of you , " all of you , " all of you , " all of you . "
貝基布蘭頓:我無家可歸的一年	bjk: one year i'm homeless .
我是一個作家 , 一個新聞記者 , 我也是一位具有強烈求知慾的人 。 所以在做新聞記者的22年裡 , 我知道了很多新奇的事物 。	i'm a writer , i'm a journalist , i'm also a person with a strong courtship , so for 22 years , i learned a lot about novelty .
而三年前 , 我學會做的一件事就是變成隱形人 。	and one of the things i learned three years ago was that i became invisible .
我成了一個無家可歸的工作者 。	i became a homeless worker .
我辭掉了報紙編輯的工作在我父親那年二月去世之後我決定去旅行	i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died that february , and i decided to travel .
他的去世對我打擊非常大 。	his death struck me very much .
當時這麼做 , 是因為有很多我想去感知和處理的事 。	and this was because there were so many things that i wanted to perceive and deal with .
旅遊時我天天都在露營 。 並且決定在休旅車裡住一年就當作是一段長期野營旅行 。	i was on a road trip every day , and decided to live in a suv for a year as a longterm camp trip .
所以 , 我就帶上我的貓 , 我的羅特威爾犬和露營的裝備裝載到1975產的雪佛萊旅遊車上 , 開車去看日落但當時完全沒想過三件嚴重的事	so i took my cat , my rotwell dog and camping equipment , down to the 1975 chevy ride in 1975 , and i drove to the sunset , but i had no idea of three serious things .
一:社會將住房即使是很小的房間 , 和人的價值等同起來 。	one: social housing is equal to human value .
二:我沒有意識到其他人的負面言語對我們本身的影響是多麼嚴重 , 假如我們放任不管 。	two: i didn't realize how severe the negative effects of other people are on us if we let go .
三:我沒有意識到無家可歸是一種生活態度而不是一種生活方式 。	three: i didn't realize homelessness was a lifestyle , not a lifestyle .
一開始 , 住在車裡是很不錯的 。	at first , living in a car was pretty good .
我在露天洗澡 , 正常的去外面吃東西 。	i was bathing in the open , normally eating outside .
而且有時間去抒發情感 。	and there's time for that to come out of emotion .
但是後來 , 因我父親去世而帶來的悲憤和痛沮開始加劇 。	but then the anger and the frustration that my father died .
我自由作家的工作結束了 。 我就需要去找一件全職工作來支付我的賬單 。	my free author's job ended , and i needed to find a fulltime job to pay my bill .
從一個非常溫和的春天變到一個極其炎熱的夏天會怎樣呢 。	from a very gentle spring to a hot summer .
不管車停在哪都是難以忍受的不用說也很明顯我帶著一隻貓和一隻狗 , 而且非常的熱 。	regardless of where the car parks are unbearable , obviously , i carry a cat and a dog with a dog and i'm very hot .
貓從車窗來回的跑 。	cats running back and forth from their windows .
狗跑到了狗狗護理中心 。	the dog runs to the dog nurse center .
不管什麼時候 , 只要可以 , 我就會去用在辦公大樓和卡車車站裡員工用的淋浴 。	whenever i could , i would go to the showers for office buildings and truck stations .
或者在公共衛生間裡洗洗 。	or wash them in public health .
在夜裡車裡的溫度很少會降到華氏80度以下 , 這使我幾乎無法入睡 。	at night , i rarely get below 80 degrees fahrenheit , which makes me literally impossible to sleep .
食物在高溫下腐壞 。	food rotted in temperature .
冷藏櫃裡的冰幾個小時就化完了 , 非常苦悶的時期 。	the ice in the refrigerator cabinet is finished for a few hours , a very boring period .
我沒錢找公寓 , 或者找不到讓我可以養狗和貓的地方 。	i had no money to find apartments , or i couldn't find a place where i could raise dogs and cats .
我不想把它們拋棄 。 所以我繼續待在旅行車裡 。	i didn't want to throw them away . so i kept on staying in the van .
但炎熱的天氣使我飽受折磨以至於在夜裡走50英尺到車外面的公共衛生間都懶的動 。 我用桶和垃圾袋當廁所 。	but the hot weather made me so afflict that 50 feet into the middle of the night beyond public health , i used buckets and garbage bags as toilets .
當冬天來臨的時候 , 溫度驟降到零度以下 。 然後就一直這麼冷 。	when the winter came , the temperature dropped below zero degrees , and it stayed cold .
我又遇到了一堆新問題 ,	and i had a bunch of new questions .
每晚我的車都停在不同的地方 。 這樣才可以不讓警察發現以至於和警察爭吵 。	every night , my car parks in different places , so that the police can't see any more than arguing with the police .
當然 , 並不是每次都成功 。	of course , not succeeding all the time .
但是 , 我覺得我已無力掌控自己的生活了 。	but i felt like i had no control over my life .
我也不知道什麼時候或者是如何發生的 , 我這麼快就從一個有才的寫手 , 新聞從業者變成一個無家可歸 , 住在車裡的女人這簡直是快的難以置信 。	i didn't know when or how it happened , soon i went from being a talented writer to being an homeless woman living in a car , incredibly fast .
我並沒有變 。 我的智商沒有降低 。	i didn't change . my iq didn't decline .
我的才能 , 我的正直 , 我的價值 , 所有關於我的這些東西都還是一樣 。	my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me is still the same .
但是從某種程度上 , 我還是改變了 ,	but in a way , i changed .
我越來越沮喪 , 像一個漩渦一樣不斷地往下沉 。	i became more and more depressed , and i sinked like a swirl of eddies .
後來有人介紹我去一個專為無家可歸之人開的健康診所 。	and then someone introduced me to a health clinic that was specifically homeless .
我去了 。 我有三天都沒有洗澡了 ,	i went . i didn't have a bath for three days .
我和其他那些排隊的人一樣沮喪 , 身上的味道也很難聞 。	i was as depressed as anybody else in line , and it was very difficult to smell .
我只是沒有喝醉或者興奮 。	i just wasn't drunk or excited .
當一些無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括一個以前在大學任教的教授 , 他們說: " 你不是無家可歸 , 你真正在這裡的原因是什麼 ? "	when some homeless people realized that , including a professor who used to teach at university , they said , " you're not homeless , what's the reason you're really here ? "
其他的無家可歸的人不把我當作是無家可歸的人看待 。 但是我自己是這麼認為的 。	other homeless people don't see me as homeless people , but i do .
後來 , 教授聽了我的故事後他說 , " 你有工作 , 有希望 。	and after the professor listened to my story , he said , " you have a job , you have hope .
真正無家可歸的人並沒有希望可言 。 "	there is no hope for a real homeless person . "
診所針對我沮喪開的藥物的副作用讓我有點自殺的傾向 。 我還記得當時想 , " 如果我自殺了 , 可能沒人會發現的 "	the doctor's side effects of the despairing medication made me a little bit suicidal , and i remember thinking , " if i kill myself , no one's going to find it . "
在那不久後 , 我的一個朋友就告訴我 , 她聽說提姆路塞特 , 一個全國知名的記者在全國播放的電視節目上談論到了我 。	not long after that , a friend of mine told me that she had heard about tim luther , a nationally renowned journalist about me on national television shows .
一篇我寫的關於我父親的短文 , 在他去世前一年寫的 , 被收錄到了提姆的新書裡 。	an essay i wrote about my father , a year before he died , was received in a new book about tim .
他那時在做巡迴演講 , 提到我的寫作 。	he was giving a tour and talking about my writing .
當我發現提姆路塞特 , 前meetthepress節目的調解員 , 在談論我的寫作 。 而我卻生活在停在沃爾瑪停車場裡的旅行車裡面 , 我開始笑了 ,	when i found tim luther , former meetthe press , talking about my writing , i was living in a van in walmart parking lot , and i started laughing .
我開始笑 , 因為這正是問題根結 , 我是一位作家呢 , 還是一位無家可歸的女人 ?	and i started laughing , because that's the question: am i a writer , or is it a homeless woman ?
於是我走進一家書店 。 找到提姆的書 。	so i went into a bookstore . i found tim's book .
我站在那 , 又重新讀了一遍我寫的短文 。	and i stood there and i reread the text that i've written .
因為我是一位作家 ,	because i'm a writer .
是一位作家 。	it's a writer .
在那之後 , 我很快就搬回了田納西 。	since then , i quickly moved back to tennessee .
有時住在車裡 , 有時會去朋友家睡沙發 。	sometimes living in a car , sometimes going to a friend's house and sleeping on a couch .
我又重新開始寫作了 。	i started writing again .
在接踵而來的夏天裡 , 我又成為了一名新聞記者 。	in the summer of the following summer , i became a journalist .
我得了獎 , 住在我自己的公寓裡 。	i got a prize to live in my own apartment .
我不再無家可歸 。	i was no longer homeless .
我也不再被無視 。	i was no longer being blinded .
無數的人在從事著全職和兼職的工作 , 而且住在他們的車裡 。	countless people are engaged in fulltime and parttime jobs and living in their cars .
但是社會還繼續汙衊他們並視住在交通工具裡或者睡在街上為犯罪 。	but society continued to arouse them and watch them live in vehicles or sleep in the streets for crime .
所以那些無家可歸 , 有工作但是無家可歸的人 , 大部分還是隱藏著的 。	so the homeless , the workforce but homeless , most of them are still hidden .
但是如果你見到了 , 僱用他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 並給予他們希望 。	but if you see them , hire them , encourage them and give them hope .

聯合國的資料顯示 , 艾滋病的新增病例降低了百分之九十 。 世界銀行的報告顯示 , 我們的行動拯救了770萬人的生命 。	data from the united nations showed that new augmented cases of aids decreased by 90 percent , and the world bank report showed that our actions saved 7 . 7 million lives .
