我認為現在時機已經成熟可以根本性地改變我們的文明	i think it's time to mature , to fundamentally change our civilization .
不過若要真正改變 , 就需要讓婦女的力量參與到世界當中	but in order to really change , we need to engage women's forces in the world .
我們需要讓足夠的婦女擁有權力並且培養男人心中的婦女力量	we need to have enough women own power and cultivate women's strength in men .
這裡當然是指年輕男人了	this is , of course , young men .
老男人們都沒求了 , 只能等著他們死光	older men don't get it , but they're going to die .

不過若是可以選擇 , 我寧願擁有勇敢的心像旺加里.馬塔伊 , 蘇曼麗.馬恩 , 珍妮和羅斯.馬培德那樣的	but if i had a choice , i would rather have the courageous hearts like wangari maathai , somali maran , jennie and ross mabed .
我想讓世界變得更好	i wanted to make the world a better place .
不僅僅是消極地等待改變 , 而是參與改變	not just negatively , waiting for change , but engaging in change .
為什麼不這樣 ? 這是能夠做得到的 。 看看這裡 , 充滿了知識 , 活力 , 才華和科技	why not ? it's possible . look here , it's full of knowledge , dynamic , talent and technology .
讓我們走出冷氣房 , 捲起袖子開始行動 , 帶著我們的熱情創造一個近乎完美的世界	let's get out of the cold room , roll up our sleeves , start acting , and take our passion to create a nearly perfect world .
在一個倫敦那麼大的城市裡 , 每天都要消耗掉三千萬噸糧食 。 但是 , 這些食物都從何而來 ? 建築師carolynsteel探討每天餵養一個城市的神話 , 介紹古代的食物運輸如何影響城市的形成和發展 。	in a city that's that big in london , they consume 30 million tons of food every day , but where does it come from , and architect carolyn steel has looked at the myth of feeding a city every day , introducing how food transportation affects the formation and development of the city .
cities , culture , food , globalissues	you know , it's the world's humble , right ?
carolynsteel:食物如何塑造我們的城市	carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities .
如何餵養一個城市 ?	how do you feed a city ?
這是我們這個時代的一個重大問題之一 。	this is one of the big questions of our time .
然而很少人會問這個問題 。	however , very few people ask this question .
我們習以為常了 , 我們走進商店的時候走進餐廳的時候 , 或是一個小時後我們進入這個劇院的門廳總會有食物等著我們它們很神奇地從某個地方冒出來	we used to think that when we walked into the shop , when we walked into the restaurant , an hour later , we entered the theater's door , there was always food , and they waited for us , and magically emerged somewhere .
然而 , 當你想像每一天 , 在一個倫敦那麼大的城市 , 要生產足夠的食物運輸、交易這些食物 , 烹飪 , 食用 , 最後扔棄它們而且類似的事情每天都發生著在地球上的每一個城市都如此每個城市都有食物供應 , 這件事很不可思議	however , when you imagine that every single day in a city the size of london , there's enough food transportation , trading these foods , cooking , cooking , eating , throwing them out , and things like that happen every day every day , every city on this planet , so it's incredible .
我們住在每天有食物供應的城市 , 彷彿這是世界上最自然的事情 , 我們忘記了我們也是動物 , 所以我們需要進食 , 事實上我們要依賴自然界就如同我們的祖先要依賴自然界一樣 。	we live in a city that has food supplies every day , as if it's the most natural thing in the world , and we forgot that we are animals , so we need to eat , and we actually depend on nature as our ancestors depend on nature .
隨著我們越來越多人到城市生活 , 越來越多的自然界正在變成我身後的這些特別的景象這是巴西matagrosso的大豆田用來種食物養活我們	as more and more of us go to cities , the natural world is becoming a very special scene behind me , and this is the soybean field of brazil matagrosso in order to grow our food .
這些特別的景象我們很少人親眼目睹過	these particular scenes are very few of us have seen .
越來越多的這些地貌不只是生產食物養活我們	more and more of these landscapes aren't just producing food to feed us .
隨著我們越來越多人移居城市越來越多人吃肉所以每年全球有三分之一的糧食現在是用來餵動物而不是餵養我們人類	as more and more of us move into cities , more and more people eat meat , so a third of the world's food is now feeding animals rather than feeding us humans .
雖然說需要3倍的糧食事實上卻是10倍的食物來餵養一個人 , 如果從餵養動物的糧食也計算在內這並不是一個很有效率的餵養方式	even though it takes three times as much food , it's actually 10 times as much food to feed a person , and if you feed an animal , it's not a very efficient way to feed an animal .
這是一個越來越重要的問題	it's an increasingly important question .
到2050年 , 預測有兩倍的人口將在城市居住	by 2050 , it's predicted that twice as many people will live in cities .
預測到也將需要兩倍的肉和奶類製品的消耗	it's predicted that we're going to need twice as much meat and milk production as we know .
所以肉的消耗和城市化是共同發展的	so meat consumption and urbanization are coevolving .

這是個大問題.如果我們還像我們現在這麼發展 , 我們很可能沒法在2050年解決這個問題	it's a big problem . if we're still as evolving as we are now , we probably wouldn't be able to solve this problem by 2050 .
每年有1900萬公頃的雨林消失它們用作開墾新的耕地	every year , 19 million hectares of rainforest disappear , and they use it to cultivate new arable land .
儘管與此同時我們也失去等量的現有耕地 , 因為鹽鹼化或水土流失	and yet , at the same time , we're losing an equal amount of arable land because of saltification or water land loss .
我們也急需化石燃料	we desperately need fossil fuels .
在歐洲 , 我們需要10卡路里的能量來生產1卡路里為我們消耗的食物	in europe , we need 10 calories of energy to produce one calories of food for us .
儘管這些食物我們都是花了很多功夫才生產出來事實上我們卻不珍惜它們	despite all this food , it took a lot of work to produce , and in fact we don't appreciate them .
在美國有一半食物被扔棄	half of the food is discarded in the united states .
最終 , 在這漫長過程的最後我們將沒法養活我們這個地球	ultimately , at the end of this long process , we will not be able to feed our planet .
我們中10億人肥胖 , 還有多於10億的人處於飢餓中	one billion of us are obese , and more than one billion people are hungry .
這些都沒有道理	none of this makes any sense .
當你發現現在80%的全球食物貿易僅由五家跨國公司控制 , 這是挺可怕的	when you find out that 80 percent of the world's global food trade is controlled by just five multinational companies , it's terrifying .
隨著我們搬進城市 , 世界正在接受西方的飲食	as we move into cities , the world is accepting western diet .
如果我們展望未來這不是個可持續的飲食方式	if we look at the future , it's not a sustainable way of eating .

先回答那個較簡單的問題 , 首先我想說 , 在大概1萬年前是這個過程的開始在古代的中東地區也就是廣大的新月狀的地區	well , the simpler question i'd like to begin with is , first of all , about 10 , 000 years ago , the beginning of this process in the middle east , the vast area of new moonshaped areas .
因為你可以看到它是新月形的	because you can see it's the new moon .
同時它也是廣大的	it's also enormous .
就在這裡 , 大概1萬年前2大偉大的發明農業和城市化在此發生幾乎在同時 , 同一地點	right here , about 10 , 000 years ago , the great inventions of agriculture and urbanization happened almost at the same time , at the same time .
這並不是偶然因為農業和城市是緊密聯絡的.它們需要彼此	it's not accidentally because agriculture and cities are intimate , and they need each other .
因為糧食的發現我們的遠古祖先 , 第一次第一次生產出足夠的糧食並且產量穩地 , 這幫助他們長期居住下來	the discovery of food was that our distant ancestors , for the first time , produced enough food and yielded steadily , helped them live longtermly .
如果我們看一下當時那些居住地我們可以看到他們是緊密的	if we look at the places where they lived at the time , we can see that they were intimate .
他們被農田圍繞並由一些大的廟宇統領著例如這一個在烏爾的神殿事實上 , 他們是很有效的精神統領 , 食物分發中心 , 兩者結合	they're surrounded by farms , and they're led by large temples , like this one in ur , and in fact , they're very effective psychiatry , food distribution centers , combinations .
因為這些神殿組織耕作收集這些糧食 , 供奉給諸神然後把諸神沒吃的食物發還給人們	because these temple tissues are gathering these foods , serving them to the gods , and then giving them back the food that the gods don't eat .
所以這些城市的精神和物質生活都用糧食和收成掌控並維持城市的生活	so the spirit and the physical life of these cities is used to eat and control and maintain the city's lives .
事實上 , 過去的每個城市都是如此	in fact , every city in the past has been like this .
當然 , 並不是每個都是那麼小的城市	and of course , not every city is that small .

這樣是在古代能實現的唯一的方法因為陸上運輸相當困難鑑於路況不好	it's the only way that ancients can achieve this , because shipping is very difficult on land , given bad circumstances .

所以羅馬常常發動戰爭攻打像迦太基和埃及那樣的國家僅僅是為了得到他們的糧食儲備	so rome regularly launched war attacks in countries like ghachi and egypt just to get their food reserves .

事實上 , 我喜歡這個事實 。 我不得不指出的是羅馬在一個時期 。 我認為這非常特別	in fact , i love that fact . i have to refer to rome in a period . i think that's very special .

如果我們看看十七世紀倫敦的地圖我們可以看見作物從泰晤士河畔出產的位於地圖的底部	if we look at maps of london in the 17th century , we can see crops coming out of the thames river banks , at the bottom of the map .

魚當然是從河裡面打撈出來的	the fish , of course , came out of the river .
billlingsgate是倫敦有名的賣魚市場在1980年之前	billynsgate was a famous selling fish market in london before 1980 .

肉是一個非常不同的故事了因為 , 動物自己走向城市	meat is a very different story , because animals go to cities themselves .
因此 , 倫敦消費的大量肉類是從西北方過來的從蘇格蘭和威爾士	so london consumed a lot of meat from the northwest , from scotland and wales .
當他們過來 , 抵達城市的西北方這就說明了為什麼smithfield倫敦一個非常有名的肉類市場 , 在這裡產生	when they came , they arrived in the northwest , which illustrates why smithfield london was a very famous market for meat .
家禽從anglia的東部來 , 去往東北部	domestic avian comes from the eastern part of ananglia to the northeast .
我感覺這有點像一個天氣播報員然後鳥兒都飛過來了它們的腳被小帆布鞋包裹著	i felt like a weather announcer , and the birds flew over , and their feet were wrapped around little canvas shoes .
然後當它們在東部降落的時候具體說來是在戚普塞街 , 也就是它們被賣掉的地方這也就是戚普塞街被稱為 " 家禽 " 街的原因	and when they landed in the east , they specifically described what they were selling , which is why they called " domestic street . "
事實上 , 如果你看看任何一個城市的地圖在工業化時代之前你能夠發現食物是如何進入城市的	in fact , if you look at any map of any city before the industrial era , you can see how food enters the city .
事實上 , 你可以看出食物是如何塑造一個城市的透過閱讀街道的名稱 , 你就會發現很多線索	in fact , you can see how food shapes a city by reading the names of the streets , and you can see a lot of clues .
星期五街 , 在過去的日子中是一個在星期五買魚的地方	friday street , in the past , was a place to buy fish on friday .
但是 , 你同時也必須想象那裡到處都是食物	but you also have to imagine that there's food everywhere .
因為街道和公共區域是食物買賣的唯一地點	because the streets and the public areas are the only places where food buys and sells .
如果你想象一下1830年的smithfield你會發現很難在這樣一個城市裡面生活下去並且不留意食物的來源	if you think about smithfield in 1830 , it's very difficult to live in a city like this and not pay attention to the source of food .
事實上 , 當你在星期日吃午飯的時候你將很有可能聽到窗外的牛羊的叫聲在三年以前	in fact , when you're eating lunch on sunday , you're likely to hear that goat out the window , three years ago .
因此 , 顯然他是一個有機城市屬於有機迴圈中的一個部分	so , apparently , he's part of an organic city that's part of an organic loop .
但是 , 10年後 , 一切都改變了	but after 10 years , everything changed .
這是大西鐵路在1840的照片	this is a picture of the great western railroad in 1840 .
你可以看見 , 一些早期的鐵路乘客們是豬和羊群	as you can see , some early railroad passengers were pigs and sheep .
一夕之間 , 這些動物不再走進市場	all of a sudden , these animals stopped walking into the market .
他們被屠宰了在鄉村的某個地方	they're slaughtered somewhere in the country .
然後他們透過鐵路來到了城市	and they came to the city through the railroad .
這些改變了一切	and that changed everything .
首先 , 他第一次使城市成長變成了可能不論地點、成為什麼規模和形狀的城市	first of all , he had the first growth of cities , the possible , no matter what the scale and shape of the city was .
城市發展過去受到地理的限制城市需要透過很艱難的方式獲得食物	cities have developed past constraints in geography , and cities have to get food in a tough way .
突然 , 他們從地理限制中解放了出來	all of a sudden , they liberated from geography .
你可以看看倫敦的地圖在鐵路建成後的90年它從容易餵飽的一小點透過動物步行到市場等方式成長成為大型的奢侈的大都市步行運輸再也不能餵飽每個人不論是對人還是對動物	you can see the map of london in the 90 years after the railroad was made , it went from a small dot that was easy to feed , through animal walks to markets , to a large , luxury metropolitan walk , to transportation , to no longer feed everybody , whether it's right or animal .
當然 , 這僅僅是開始 。 當汽車代替了火車這真正標誌這個過程的結束	and of course , it's just the beginning . when the automobiles replaced the train , the real sign of the process is over .
這是城市的最終解放從自然的束縛中完全的解放了	this is the ultimate liberation of the city from the constraints of nature , completely liberated .
這樣型別的城市沒有了原來城市的味道亂糟糟的市容 , 當然也缺少了人因為沒有人想要在這麼大的一塊地方步行	it doesn't have the smell of the original city , and of course it's missing because nobody wants to walk in such a big place .
事實上 , 他們都開小汽車去購買食物了開車去郊外的超級市場買回來一週需要的食物然後考慮到底如何規劃這些食品	in fact , they're all driving cars to buy food , driving to the supermarkets outside of the suburbs , buying food that they need for a week , and thinking about how to plan these foods .
這時刻 , 食物和城市的關係 , 完全的改變了	at this point , food and cities have changed completely .
過去買食物是在市中心在城市的最核心地帶	it used to be buying food in the central part of the city .
買賣食物曾經是一種社會性的活動 ,	buying food used to be a social activity .
我們原來還需要烹飪 , 現在我們只需要加水或者是一些雞蛋 , 當我們在做蛋糕或者其他東西的時候	it turns out we need to cook . we need to add water or some eggs when we're making cake or something .
我們不會在去聞聞食物來確認它是否可以吃了	we're not going to smell food to make sure it's going to eat .
我們只是閱讀包裝袋上的使用說明就好	we're just reading the instructions on the package .
我們沒有發現食物的價值 , 我們也不信賴它	we don't have the value of discovering food , and we don't trust it .
我們甚至擔心它	we worry about it .
從體會它的價值變成浪費	from recognizing its value to wasting .
當今食品工業最最諷刺的是他們讓生活極致地便利卻也使得一切更為複雜	the irony of today's food industry is that they've made it extremely convenient , but they've made it even more complicated .
因為可以自由的建立新城市但是他們卻疏遠了人可貴的聯絡也就是人與自然的聯絡	because they're free to build a new city , but they're alienated from the expensive contact of human beings and nature .
同時 , 他們也讓我們依賴這個系統這個系統 , 在我們看來 , 是不可持續的	at the same time , they also rely on this system , which is unsustainable , in our opinion .
所以 , 我們應該做點什麼呢 ?	so what should we do ?
這不是一個新的問題	this is not a new question .
500年前 , 湯馬斯摩爾曾經問過自己	500 years ago , thomas more asked himself .
這是他的書《烏托邦》的主旨	this is the essence of his book , " utopia . "
它是一個半獨立的城邦如果這麼說聽上去還比較熟悉的話一天的行走你會看見所有人農場都在瘋狂的種植或者在自己的後院種植蔬菜然後一起享用鄉鎮的共有食物 , 等等	it's a semiindependent city , and if that sounds like it's more familiar , walking on a day , you'll see all the farms growing in crazy , or growing vegetables in their own backyard , and sharing shared food with the town , and so on .

有時從正面說 , 那就是- " 推己及人 。 "	sometimes from a positive point of view , that's , " selfmotivate . "

審視你的內心 。 探尋究竟是什麼讓你痛苦 。 然後在任何情況下 , 都拒絕將這種痛苦施加於別人 。	scrutinize your heart , seek out what causes you to suffer , and in any case , refuse to apply that pain to others .
人們之所以重視仁愛 , 不僅僅是因為它聽起來很棒 , 更是因為它行得通 。	people value compassion , not just because it sounds great , but because it works .

非常感謝 。	thank you very much .
mit研究人員斯凱拉•蒂比茨從事自我裝配的研究一個取代建造東西的主意 , 我們能創建制作自己的材料 , 很像dna鏈打包的方式 。 目前還是一個巨大概念的早期階段 ; 蒂比茨向我們展示了三個還在實驗中的專案 , 我們可以一窺一個自我裝配的未來可能的樣子 。	the mit researcher , skyla tibiz , who works on selfassembly a project where we can create our own materials , much like the dna chain packing , and we're still at the earliest stages of an enormous concept , where tibiz shows us three projects that are still in the experiment where we can peer into the future of selfassembly .
斯凱拉•蒂比茨:我們能製作可以製作自己的東西麼 ?	sk: can we make things that we can make ourselves ?
今天我想向各位展示未來我們製作東西的方式 。	i want to show you today how we make things in the future .
我相信很快我們的建築和機器將能自我組裝 , 自我複製和自我修復 。	i believe soon our buildings and machines will selfassemble , selfreplicating and selfrepairing .
因此我要向各位展示我所認為的製造業的當前狀況 , 接著再將其與一些自然系統比較 。	so i'm going to show you what i think is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare it to some natural systems .
那麼在當前的製造業中 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的時間 , 50萬至上百萬個部分 , 非常複雜 , 使用了在鋼鐵 , 混凝土和玻璃方面的新技術 。	so in the current manufacturing industry , we have skyscrapers two and a half years , 500 , 000 to million parts , very complex , using new technologies for steel , concrete and glass .
我們有令人激動的機器 , 可以帶我們進入太空五年時間 , 兩百五十萬個部分 。	we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years , 2 . 5 million parts .
但另一方面 , 如果看看自然系統 , 我們有擁有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 能在一萬納秒內摺疊起來 , 我們能在大約一小時內對帶有三十億鹼基對的dna進行復制 。	but on the other hand , if we look at the natural system , we have two million types of proteins that fold up in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , and we can reconstruct that with about three billion base pairs of dna in about one hour .
這就是我們自然系統的複雜性 , 但它們非常高效 , 比我們建造的任何東西都要高效 , 比我們能建造的任何東西都要複雜 。	that's the complexity of our natural systems , but they're very efficient , much more efficient than anything we build , much more complicated than anything we can build .
它們在能源方面更加高效 。	they're more efficient in energy .
它們很少犯錯 。	they rarely make mistakes .
他們能自我修復保持長壽 。	they can selfrepair longevity .
關於自然系統有件超級有意思的事情 。	it's a fascinating thing about natural systems .
如果我們能將其轉換為我們的建築環境 , 那麼我們構建事物的方式就會有很大的潛力 。	if we can turn it into our building environment , then there's a huge potential for how we construct things .
我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。	i think the key is selfassembly .
如果我們想要在自身的身體環境中利用自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。	if we want to use selfassembly in our own bodies , i think there are four key factors .
第一個是 , 我們需要解碼我們所要建造的東西的所有的複雜度也就是我們的建築和機器 。	the first is that we need to decode all the complexity that we want to build , our buildings and machines .
我們需要把它們解碼成簡單的序列基本上就是我們的建築運作的dna 。	we need to decode them into simple sequences basically the dna that our buildings function .
接著我們需要可程式設計的部分這部分能接受這一序列並用於摺疊或是重塑 。	and then we need parts of programmable programmable parts that can accept this sequence and fold or reshape .
我們需要一些能量來進行啟用 , 使我們的這些部分能夠依照程式摺疊起來 。	we need some energy to start , so that our parts can fold up on the code .
我們需要一些型別的糾錯冗餘以保證我們成功建造的就是我們想要的 。	we need some kind of error redundancy to guarantee that what we've succeeded in building is what we want .
因此 , 我要向各位展示一些我和我的同事正在進行的要實現這種自我組裝的未來的專案 。	so i'm going to show you some projects that my colleagues and i are working on to realize this selfassembly future .
頭兩個專案是macrobot和decibot 。	the first two projects are macrobot and decibot .
這些專案都是大規模可重構機器人8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。	these projects are all eightfoot , 12footlong proteins .
它們嵌入機電裝置 , 感測器 。	they're embedded in mechanical appliances , sensors .
你需要把想要摺疊的方式解碼成 , 解碼成一系列角度負120度 , 負120度 , 0度 , 0度 , 120度 , 負120度 , 這類的東西 ; 一系列角度 , 或轉向 , 可以用電線把這個次序傳過去 。	you need to decode the way you want to fold it into a series of angles that are 120 degrees minus 120 degrees minus 120 degrees , zero degrees , 120 degrees , minus 120 degrees , a series of things , a series of angles , or shifts , to get this sequence through .
每個單元獲取自己的訊息比如負120.它進行旋轉 , 檢查是否旋轉到位然後把序列傳給它的鄰居 。	each unit takes its own message such as minus 120 . it rotates , checks if it spins to its neighbor .
有許多傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師為這個專案工作 。	there are many brilliant scientists , engineers , designers working on this project .
我認為這一專案真的揭示出:這真的可擴充套件麼 ?	and i think this project really reveals: is this really scalable ?
我是說 , 花費數千美元許多人時來製造這個八英尺的機器人 。	i mean , it cost thousands of dollars to build this eightfoot robot .
我們真的能擴大它麼 ? 我們真的能在每個部分中都嵌入機器人麼 ?	can we really expand it ? can we really embed robots in all parts ?
下一個問題是看看被動性 , 或被動地嘗試讓重組具有可程式設計性 。	the next problem is looking at passiveity , or passively trying to make recombinations programmable .
但它更進了一步 , 它嘗試進行實際計算 。	but it goes a little further , and it tries to do actual computation .
基本上嵌入了多數計算的基礎構建模組 , 數字邏輯閘 , 直接進入各個部分 。	basically embedded in most computational building modules , digital gates , directly into all parts .
這是與非門 。	it's not a gate .
每個要用於計算的門上都有一個四面體 , 有兩個輸入四面體 。	each of these doors has a tetrahedron on the door of computation , with two inputs .
其中一個是來自使用者的輸入 , 就像你在構建磚塊 。	one is input from the user , just like you're building blocks .
另一個是來之前前放好的一塊磚的輸入 。	the other is a brick input that was previously introduced .
接著它會給出三維空間的輸出 。	and then it exports threedimensional output .
這意味著使用者以他們想要的方式堆砌磚塊 。	it means that the user builds bricks in the way they want .
它依據之前所做的和你的指令進行計算 。	it calculates based on previous instructions and your commands .
現在它開始在三維空間內移動上或者下 。	now it starts moving up or down in three dimensions .
看左面 , [1 , 1]的輸入等於0輸出 , 表示向下 。	look at the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , represents the downwards .
在右邊 , [0 , 0]的輸入是1輸出 , 表示向上 。	on the right , [0 , 0] input is one output , expressing upwards .
因此這真正的的意味是我們的結構中現在包含了我們想要構建的藍圖 。	so what this really means is that our structures now contain blueprints that we want to construct .
因此關於想要構建的事物的資訊已經全部嵌入其中 。	so information about the things that want to construct is embedded .
這意味著我們有了某種形式的自我複製 。	that means we have some form of selfreplication .
對這種情況 , 我稱之為自我導向複製 , 因為你的結構中包含了精確的藍圖 。	in this case , i call this selfdirected copying , because your structure contains accurate blueprints .
如果遇到錯誤 , 你可以替換一個部分 。	if there's a mistake , you can replace a part .
所有的本地資訊都嵌入其中 , 告訴你如何修復它 。	local information is embedded in , telling you how to repair it .
因此你有個可以攀爬的東西 , 能讀出它並一個一個的輸出 。	so you have something that can climb and read it and output one by one .
它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有外部指令輸入 。	it's directly embedded ; there's no external input .
我要展示的最後一個專案名為偏心鏈條 , 它可能是我們現在看到的被動自我裝配系統中最令人激動的例子 。	the last project i'm going to show you is called the biased chain , and it's probably the most exciting example of the passive selfassembly system that we're seeing right now .
它具有可重構性和可程式設計性使它成了為了一個完全地被動系統 。	it has reconstructability and programmability that makes it a system for completely passive systems .
基本上就是你有了一連串的元素 。	basically you have a series of elements .
每個元素都是完全相同的 , 且它們是偏心的 。	each element is completely identical , and they are preferred .
每個鏈條 , 或每個元素想要向右轉或是向左轉 。	each strand , or every element wants to turn right or left .
如果你要裝配鏈條 , 需要為它程式設計 。	if you want to assemble a chain , you need to program it .
要告訴每個單元是要左轉還是右轉 。	tell each unit to turn left or right .
當你搖動這個鏈條時 , 它就摺疊起來程式設計你所為它編碼的任何結構因此這種情況下 , 一個螺旋體 , 火這種情況 , 兩個相連的立方體 。	when you shake this chain , it folds up , and it programs whatever structure you code for it , so in this case , a spiral , fire , in this case , two cubes connected .
基本上你可以在三維空間內程式設計或是一維、二維這鏈條是完全被動的 。	basically , you can program it in three dimensions or onedimensional or twodimensional strands that are completely passive .
這向我們預示了怎樣的未來呢 ?	what does this tell us about the future ?
我認為這告訴我們這些在我們的身體結構、我們的建築和機器中這種自我裝配、自我複製和自我修復的可能性 。	i think what this tells us is the possibility of selfassembly , selfreplication and selfrepairing in our bodies , our buildings and machines .
在這些部分中有新的可程式設計性 。	there's new programmability in those parts .
從中你能獲得計算的新可能性 。	you can get the new possibilities of computation .
我們將有空間計算 。	we'll have spatial computing .
想象一下我們的建築、橋樑、機器 , 所有的磚塊都能進行實際計算 。	imagine our buildings , our bridges , our machines , all of these bricks can actually compute .
多麼令人驚奇的平行計算和分散式計算能力和新的設計可能性啊 。	what an amazing parallel computing and distributed computing power and new design possibilities .
這是項令人激動的潛力 。	it's an exciting potential .
我認為這些我向各位展示的專案僅僅是邁向未來的一小步 , 如果我們為一個新的自我組裝的世界實現了這些新技術的話 。	and i think these projects that i've shown you are just a tiny step towards the future , if we assemble a new selfassembly world .
我們已踏上過月球 , 我們已測繪了大陸 , 我們甚至已去過海底最深處--兩次 。 還剩下什麼值得我們的下一代去探索 ? 生物學家和內森•沃爾夫提出了這樣的答案:幾乎所有事物 。 " 我們可以從那小到看不見的世界開始 " , 他說 。	we've stepped on the moon , we've mapped the continent , we've even been to the deepest of the sea twice . what's left worth exploring ? biologists and nathan wolf asks the answer: almost everything . "
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	bioversity , biology , is what happens to you .
內森•沃爾夫:還有什麼值得探索 ?	nathan wolf: what else is it worth exploring ?
最近我去了威斯康星州的伯洛伊特市 。	i recently went to berroet , wisconsin .
我去那裡是為了紀念一名20世紀的探險家 , 羅伊•查普曼•安德魯斯 。	i went there to honor a 20thcentury explorer , roy chapman andrews .
當他在美國自然歷史博物館的時候 , 安德魯斯領導了一系列對未知領域的探險 , 比如說在這裡的戈壁灘 。	when he was at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a series of expeditions for the unknown , like the gobi beaches here .
他是個了不起的人物 。	he's an amazing figure .
他後來據說是印第安娜瓊斯角色的原型 。	he was later told to be the prototype of indiana jones role .
當我在威斯康星州的伯洛伊特市的時候 , 我給一群中學學生上了一堂公開課 。	when i was in burroyt , wisconsin , i gave a group of middle school students a public class .
我現在想告訴你們 , 如果真的有什麼比在ted做演講還難的話 , 那就是嘗試保持他們的注意力一群上千個12歲的孩子 , 並保持45分鐘 。	i want to tell you right now that if there's something harder than giving a talk at ted , it's trying to keep their attention a thousand 12yearolds and stay for 45 minutes .
在我講完之後 , 他們問了很多問題 , 但有一個讓我自始至終難以忘記 。	after my talk , they asked a lot of questions , but one of them made me never forget .
有個小女孩站起來 , 問了一個問題: " 我們該去哪裡探索呢 ? "	a little girl stood up and asked a question: " where should we explore ? "
我想我們中的絕大多數有種觀念 , 那就是 , 地球上的大探索時代已經結束 , 我們的下一代人應該去外太空或者海洋最深處從而去尋找值得探索的東西 。	i think the vast majority of our notions , that the age of exploration on earth is over , that our next generation should go to outer space or the deepest of the ocean and find things worth exploring .
但真的是這樣嗎 ?	but is that true ?
真的沒有重要的地方留給我們探索了嗎 ? 整個地球上都沒有 ?	isn't it really important for us to explore ?
這讓我回憶起我最喜歡的生物領域的探險家之一 。	it reminds me of one of my favorite explorers in biological fields .
他是位未知世界的探索家 , 馬丁努斯•威廉•拜耶林克 。	he's an explorer of the unknown world , martinus william william bellelink .
拜葉林克當初想找出引起菸草花葉病的原因 。	and byelink , who was initially trying to figure out why tobacco caused leaf disease .
他提取了受過感染的菸草汁液 , 然後讓這些汁液經過一層比一層更細的過濾 。	he took the tobacco sap of infected sap , and he let it go through a layer of filters that are tinier than a layer of infection .
他得出一個結論 , 剩下的裡面一定有什麼東西它們比那時最小的已知的生命形態--細菌 , 還要小 。	and he came to the conclusion that there must be something left out there that is smaller than the smallest known life form of bacteria , bacteria .
他給這個神秘的東西起了個名字	he gave this mysterious thing a name .
叫它們 , 病毒在拉丁文裡是 " 毒藥 " 的意思 。	call them , the virus in latin means " poison . "
在發現病毒之後 , 拜耶林克為我們打開了一個全新的世界 。	after discovering the virus , jeerlink opened a whole new world for us .
我們現在知道病毒構成我們星球上絕大部分的遺傳資訊超過所有其他生命的遺傳資訊的總和 。	we now know that viruses make up most of the genetic information on our planet more than the sum of all other life .
而且顯然已經出現了無數有關病毒的切實應用在這個世界上--像天花的根除 , 子宮癌的疫苗的降臨--我們現在知道它大部分是由乳頭瘤病毒引起的 。	and it's clear that there's been a tremendous application for viruses such as the eradication of smallpox , the decline of vaccines in cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by mammogram viruses .
而且拜耶林克的發現可不是500年前的事情 。	and byeller's findings were not 500 years ago .
拜耶林克發現病毒這件事也就發生於100多年前 。	this happened more than 100 years ago byeller .
也就是說當汽車都已經出現在世的時候 , 我們還不知道這種構成了我們星球上大部分的遺傳資訊的生物 。	that means that when the cars are already out there , we don't yet know that this is the genetic information that constructs most of the genetic information on our planet .
我們現在有些很了不起的工具來幫助我們探索未知世界 , 像基因深度測序 , 可以讓我們不只是停留在表面來看自某個特定物種的獨立基因組 , 而是研究整個基因組--我們身體裡面和周邊無處不在的微生物群落 , 並且記錄下這些物種的遺傳資訊 。	we now have some amazing tools to help us explore the unknown world , like the genetic deep sequencing , that allow us not just to remain on the surface to look at the independent genomes of a particular species , but to study the entire genome the microbial community that is everywhere in our bodies and around us , and to document the genetic information of these species .
我們可以應用這些技術來研究從土壤到皮膚和它們中間的一切 。	we can use these technologies to study everything from soil to skin and everything in between .
在我所在的機構裡面 , 我們現在經常這麼做 , 來尋找暴發的原因 , 那些我們還不清楚的原因.	in my institution , we're doing this all the time to find the causes of outbreaks that we don't know yet .
稍微給你們講下這是怎麼做的 , 想象下從你們每個人那裡取一個鼻腔分泌物標本	just to give you a little bit of how this works , imagine taking a nasal secretion specimen from each of you .
像這種事是我們經常做的 , 為了尋找呼吸道病毒 , 像流行性感冒病毒 。	things like this are things we do all the time to find respiratory viruses like flu .
我們首先看到的是海量的遺傳資訊 。	so the first thing we're looking at is the amount of genetic information .
如果我們開始仔細看看這些遺傳資訊 , 我們會看到一些常見的資訊當然了 , 有很多人類的遺傳資訊 , 但也有很多細菌和病毒的資訊 , 大部分是你鼻子裡面完全無害的東西 。	if we start looking at these genetic information , we're going to see some common information , of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also a lot of bacteria and viruses , mostly harmless things in your nose .
但我們也會看到一些非常非常讓人吃驚的東西 。	but we'll also see some very , very surprising things .
當我們開始研究這些資訊 , 我們會發現你鼻子裡面20%的遺傳資訊跟我們所見過的東西--任何植物 , 動物 , 真菌或者細菌 , 都對不上號 。	and when we started looking at this information , we found that 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose was not going to be the same as anything we've seen any plant , animal , fungi or bacteria .
我們基本上對這些一無所知 。	we basically don't know anything about that .
我們這裡的一小部分研究這些資料的人們 , 稱呼這些資訊為生物暗物質 。	a small portion of the people that we're working on this data are called biological dark matter .
我們知道以前從未見過這些生物暗物質 ; 這似乎可以被稱之為我們自己遺傳資訊裡的未知大陸 。	we know we've never seen these biological dark matters ; it seems to be called the unknown continents of our own genetic information .
而且數量非常之多 。	and that's a lot .
如果你認為你鼻子裡面20%的遺傳資訊有很多生物暗物質 , 那當我們看你內臟的時候 , 那有將近40%到50%的生物暗物質 。	if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , then when we look at your internal organs , it's nearly 40 to 50 percent biological dark matter .
即使在相對無菌的血液裡 , 也有1%到2%的資訊是暗物質--無法被歸類 , 無法被判別類別 , 跟我們所見過的東西都不同 。	even in relatively sterile bloodstreams , one to two percent of the information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be categorized , is different from anything we've seen .
開始我們以為這是人為的東西 。	we start thinking it's manmade .
這些基因深度測序工具相當比較新 。	these genetic deep sequencing tools are quite new .
但當它們變得越來越來精確 , 我們認為這些資訊是一種新的生命 , 或者至少某一部分是種生命 。	but as they get more and more accurate , we think that information is a new life , or at least some part is life .
即使這些關於解釋生物暗物質的存在的假設還處於嬰兒期 , 一個讓人非常非常激動的可能性存在著:那就是藏在這個生命裡面 , 在這些遺傳資訊裡 , 有一種沒有被識別的生命的標識 。	even though these assumptions about explaining the existence of biological dark matter are still in the infancy , a very , very exciting possibility exists: that hidden in this life , there's an unrecognizable sign of life that has not been recognized .
當我們探索這些一串串a/t/c/g嘌呤的時候 , 我們也許會發現全新的生命 , 就像拜耶林克 , 從根本上改變我們對生物學特性的理解 。	when we explore these cascades of a/t/ghour purineineine , we may find entirely new life , like bayeringk , fundamentally changing our understanding of biology .
這也許會讓我識別出困擾我們的某種癌症的原因 , 或者識別出我們不熟悉的疾病暴發的根源 , 或者創造出一種分子生物學的新工具 。	this may recognize the causes of some type of cancer that troubles us , or the root causes of a disease atrocity that we're not familiar with or create a new tool in molecular biology .
我很高興的宣佈 , 和我的斯坦福、加州理工和舊金山加利福尼亞大學的同事們一起 , 我們正在開始開始一個新的行動去探索生物暗物質來尋找新生命的存在 。	i'm happy to announce that with my fellow stanford and caltech and colleagues at the university of san francisco california , we're starting a new movement to explore the existence of biological dark matter .
100多年前 , 人們還不知道病毒的存在 , 這些包含我們星球上大部分遺傳資訊的生命形態 。	more than a century ago , people didn't know that viruses existed , which included most of the genetic information on our planet .
一百年以後 , 人類可能為我們以前完全不瞭解的新的生命形態而感到驚訝而它們就在我們眼皮底下 。	a hundred years from now , humans may be surprised by a new form of life that we didn't even know before , and they're under our eyes .
沒錯 , 我們或許已經繪製這個星球上所有大陸板塊的地圖 , 我們或許已經發現了當前所有的哺乳動物 , 但這並不代表地球上沒什麼好探索的了 。	yes , we may have mapped all of the continental plates on this planet , and we may have discovered all the mammals that we're currently in , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing to explore on this planet .
拜耶林克和像他一樣的人們給下一代探索者上了重要的一課----給那些像那個在伯洛伊特市的女孩一樣的人們 。	byelink and people like him gave the next generation of explorers a very important lesson to the girls like the city of berroet .
我想如果總結一下他給我們上的這一課 , 大概是:不要假設我們現在想到的東西是一個完整的故事 。	i think if you summarize the lesson that he gave us , it's like , don't assume that what we're thinking about is a complete story .
在不管你選擇的任何領域裡去探索那些暗物質吧 。	explore those dark matters whether you choose to .
未知的事物在我們身邊無處不在它們只是在等待人類的探索 。	the unknown things are everywhere around us , they're just waiting for human discovery .
著名科學家daviddeutsh將理論物理擱置一旁 , 而對一個更為急迫的話題展開論述:人類的存續 。 他表示 , 解決全球暖化的第一步是承認我們有問題需要解決 。	david deutsh , the famous scientist , puts theoretical physics aside , and starts the argument on a more urgent topic: human survival , and he says , the first step towards solving global warming is to acknowledge that we have a problem .
climatechange , cosmos , culture , environment , globalissues , physics , science , technology , universe	you know , the person who's there , the person who's doing it , the world issues , the physics , the person who's there , the person who's there , the person who's there .
daviddeutsch講述我們在宇宙中的位置	david deutsch tells us where we are in the universe .
主辦方要求我們大膽陳述 , 做到語不驚人死不休 。	the organizers asked us to speak boldly , to speak incredibly dead .
因此我會努力達到這一點 。 但是我想先從大家都知道的兩件事說起 。	so i'm going to try to do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone knows .
第一件事 , 事實上這是從有記錄的歷史以來就眾所周知的事 。	the first thing , in fact , is that it's something that has been known since recorded history .
這就是地球 , 或者太陽系 , 或者說我們的環境 , 或諸如此類 , 獨一無二地適合維持我們的進化 , 或者說創造 , 正如我們之前所理解的一樣--適合我們當下的生存 , 最重要的是我們未來的生存 。	this is the earth , or the solar system , or our environment , or whatever , uniquely suitable for our evolution , or creation , as we've all understood earlier for our present survival , and most importantly for our future survival .
今天這個概念有一個戲劇化的名字:太空船地球 。	today , this concept has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .
在這個概念裡 , 太空船之外宇宙不可調和地充滿敵意 , 而其內部是我們所賴以生存的一切 。	in this concept , the universe beyond the spacecraft is filled with hostility , and inside is everything we depend on .
我們只有一次機會:如果我們將我們的太空船折騰壞了 , 我們將無處可去 。	we only have one chance: if we fold our spaceship up , we're going to be everywhere .
第二件大家都知道的事是與我們在人類歷史中大部分時間所堅信的相反人類事實上並不是存在的中心 。	the second thing that everyone knows is that , contrary to what we believe in most of human history , humans are actually not at the center of existence .
大家都知道stephenhawking說過我們只是存在於一個典型星球表面的一些化學汙垢這個典型星球環繞著一個典型恆星繞行太空 , 而這個典型恆星位於一個典型銀河系的邊緣 , 以此類推 。	you know , stephen hawking said that we are just a few chemical scums on the surface of a typical planet that orbits a typical star that orbits a typical star , and this typical star is on the edge of a typical galaxy , and so on .
大家都知道的兩件事當中的第一件大概是說我們存在於一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的適合性等 , 而第二件事卻說我們存在於一個典型的地方 。	the first of these two things that everyone knows is probably to say that we're in a very untypical place , unique fitness and so on , and the second is that we're in a typical place .
尤其是當你將這兩件事當作生命中深刻的真理並以此作為你人生決策的依據 , 那麼他們似乎彼此有些衝突 。	and especially if you think of these two things as deep truths in life and based on your life decisions , then they seem to have some conflict with each other .
但是這也沒法改變他們都是徹底錯誤的這一事實 。	but it doesn't change the fact that they're completely wrong .
他們就是錯誤的 。 讓我從第二件事說起:典型 。 讓我們看一下--這是一個典型的地方嗎 ? 讓我們看一下四周 , 如你所見 , 隨便超哪個方向望去 , 我們會看到一堵牆 , 還有一些化學汙垢----而這在宇宙中一點也不典型 。	they're just wrong . let me start with the second thing: typical . let's see if this is a typical place ? let's look around , as you can see , anywhere in the world , we'll see a wall , some chemical scum and it's not typical in the universe .
你所要做得是 , 朝著同一個方向前行數百英里然後往回看 , 你將根本不會看到任何牆或者化學汙垢--你所能看到是一個藍色星球 。 如果你繼續前行 , 你會看到太陽 , 太陽系 , 以及恆星等等 。	what you're doing is , you're walking hundreds of miles in the same direction and looking backwards , and you won't even see any walls or chemical scum what you can see is a blue planet . if you keep going , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .
然而這在宇宙中仍然不算典型 , 因為恆星存在於星系中 。	but it's still not typical of the universe , because stars exist in galaxies .
宇宙中的大部分地方 , 或者說宇宙中一個典型的地方 , 不是任何靠近星系的地方 。	most places in the universe , or a typical place in the universe , are not anywhere near galaxies .
因此我們繼續前行 , 直到我們走出星系 , 然後再往回看 , 是的 , 你會看到巨大的星系 , 它螺旋形的觸手展現在我們面前 。	so we keep going , until we get out of the galaxy and we look back , yes , you see a huge galaxy , and its spiraling tentacles are in front of us now .
而到達此地 , 我們已經跨越了十萬光年 。	and at this point , we've crossed 100 , 000 lightyears .
但是我們仍然一點也沒有靠近宇宙中的典型地方 。	but we still don't have a typical place to be in the universe .
要到達典型地方 , 你需要跨越此距離的1000倍 , 直到你到達星系與星系中間的地方 。	to get to a typical place , you need to cross over 1 , 000 times the distance until you get to the middle of the galaxy and the middle of the galaxy .
那裡看上去是什麼樣子呢 ? 典型的 。	what does it look like ? typical .
那麼宇宙中一個典型的地方看上去是怎樣的呢 ?	so what does a typical place in the universe look like ?
在這裡 , ted不惜代價 , 給大家安排了一次高畫質晰的模擬的星系間空間的真實體驗--星系間空間的景觀 。	here , at ted price , i'm going to arrange a very highquality simulation of the intergalactic space of galaxies the landscape of intergalactic space .
請將電燈關閉 , 我們就可以看到了 。	please turn the lights off , and we can see that .
不太準確 , 不是非常完美--看到了嗎 ? 星系間的空間--星系間的空間是徹底黑暗的 , 極端地黑暗 。 ♪	not very accurate , not very perfect see ? intergalactic intergalactic space is radically dark , extremely dark .
這個空間是如此的黑暗 , 假使你正盯著離你最近的恆星 , 這顆恆星正好發生超新星爆炸 , 當光線射到你的時候 , 假使你正直勾勾地盯著它看 , 你甚至連微弱的閃光都無法看到 。	this space is so dark , that if you're staring at the nearest star to you , this star happens to be a supernova explosion , and when the light hits you , if you're staring directly at it , you can't even see it even flashing .
宇宙就是如此的巨大和如此的黑暗 。	the universe is so enormous and so dark .
這還沒有考慮超新星爆炸的光線是如此強烈和明亮 , 你在距離它數光年的地方會立馬斃命 。	it's not considered the light that supernova explosions are so intense and bright , that you will kill horses at a few lightyears away .
但是在星系間的空間 , 它是如此的遙遠 , 你甚至無法看見 。	but in intergalactic space , it's so far away you can't even see it .
那裡也非常寒冷--不超過絕對零度三度 。	it's also very cold not more than three degrees above absolute zero .
什麼都沒有 。 那裡真空的濃度比目前地球上最好的技術可以產生的真空濃度的100萬分之一還要小 。 所以這就是宇宙裡一個典型的地方與這兒如何地不同 。	there's nothing . there's a vacuum concentration that's smaller than one millionth the concentrations of vacuum that the best technology on earth can produce . so that's how a typical place in the universe is different than how it is .
也就是說我們現在所處的這個地方是如此地不典型 。	that's how untypical this place is .
請開燈 , 謝謝 。	please turn on the lights . thank you .
那麼我們如何瞭解距離我們如此遙遠的一個環境呢 ? 與我們所熟悉的一切相比 , 它是如此不同 , 如此陌生 。	so how do we make sense of an environment that's so far away compared to everything we're used to , so different and so foreign .
地球--我們的環境 , 以我們這一形式存在--創造知識 。	the earth our environment , in our form , creates knowledge .
這又意味著什麼呢 ? 向我們剛去過的地方的更遠處望去--我的意思是從這裡開始 , 利用望遠鏡--你會看到類似恆星的東西 。	what does that mean ? look at the further above where we've been i mean from here , using telescopes you'll see things like stars .
他們叫做類星體 。 類星體原意是指類似恆星的物體 。	they're called quasars . quasars originally meant objects like stars .
也就是說是指看上去有點像恆星的物體 。 但是他們不是恆星 。	in other words , it looks a little bit like stars , but they're not stars .
我們已經知道他們是什麼了 。 數十億年前 , 數十億光年之外 , 一個星系中心的物質朝著一個超級巨大的黑洞塌陷 。	we already know what they are . billions of years ago , billions of years ago , a matter at the center of the galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .
隨後密集的磁場對重力塌陷中的一些能量產生了導向作用 。 其中一些物質 , 以巨大的噴射流的形式逃離 , 照亮了宏偉的太空 , --我認為相當於一千億個太陽的光亮 。	intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy in some of the gravitational collapses , and some of the matter escaped in the form of giant jets , illuminating the brightness of space i think it's the equivalent of 100 billion suns .
然而 , 與這樣一個噴射流的物理相比 , 我們人類大腦的物理大相徑庭到極點 。	however , compared to the physics of a jet like this , the physics of our human brain is extremely different .
在這樣的環境裡 , 我們連一瞬間都無法生存 。 當我們試著描述那樣的噴射流中的狀況 , 語言變得無法表達 。	in such environments , we don't survive instantaneously , when we try to describe what's going on in that jet , language becomes impossible to express .
這可能有點像經歷一次超新星爆炸 , 但是是在零距離接觸並且將數百萬年的能量集中到同一時間爆發 。	it might be a bit like going through a supernova explosion , but at zero distance and concentrating millions of years of energy at the same time .
但是 , 這個噴射流發生得如此地精確 , 以至於數十億年後在宇宙的另一端 , 一些化學汙垢可以準確地描述 , 建立模型 , 並預測和解釋 , 最重要的是--你可以找得到參考--現實中曾經發生過的事 。	but this jet occurs so precisely that billions of years later on the other side of the universe , some chemical scum can accurately describe and predict and explain , and most importantly you can find the reference what has happened in real life .
一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含了另外一個物理系統的準確工作模型--類星體 。	one physics system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of another physics system , quasars .
不僅僅是一個粗淺的影象 , 雖然也包含影象 , 而且還包含解釋性的模型 , 表達同樣的數學關係和一樣的因果結構 。	not only is it a shallow image , but it also contains an explanatory model that expresses the same mathematical relations and the same causal structures .
這就是知識 。 如果這還不夠讓你驚訝的話 , 一個結構表達另外一個的準確性正隨著時間不斷提高 。 這就是知識的增長 。	this is knowledge . if it's not surprising enough , one structure expresses another accuracy over time . that's the growth of knowledge .
因此 , 物理規律擁有這樣一個特殊的性質 。	so physics has this special property .
物體 , 不管他們彼此多麼相異 , 卻仍然能夠表現同樣的數學和因果結構 , 而且隨著時間增長表現得越來越多 。	objects , no matter how different they are , can still express the same mathematical and causal structure , and can perform more and more over time .
因此我們是與眾不同的化學汙垢 。 這一化學汙垢擁有普適性 。	so we're remarkably different chemical scums .
它的結構準確度越來越高地包容著 , 世界萬物的結構 。 這個地方 , 不是宇宙中任何其他地方 , 在它自身內部 , 成為一個包容了其他一切宇宙萬物結構性和因果性精髓的中心 。 因此 , 意義深遠的是 , 物理規律允許這一現象 , 抑或甚至主導了它的發生這一事實是關於物理世界的最重要的事情之一 。	its structure is getting more accurate , more accurate , more accurate , more accurately , the structure of the world , not anywhere else in the universe , becoming at the center of all the rest of the universe's structural and causal essence , and therefore , the fact that physics allows this physics , or inhibits its dominance , is one of the most important things about the physical world .
那麼太陽系--我們的環境 , 以我們的形式--是如何獲取這樣一個與宇宙其他部分的特殊關係的呢 ?	so how does the solar system how does our environment , in our form , get a special relationship with the rest of the universe ?
stephenhawking觀點中其中一個正確面--我的意思是 , 這是正確的 , 但是著重點是錯的 。 其中一個正確面是它並沒有倚賴任何特殊的物理學 。 沒有特殊的放寬 , 沒有奇蹟發生 。 它的發生只依賴於我們現在富有的三種東西 。	stephen hawking , one of the correct aspects of the stephen hawking i mean , it's true , but it's wrong . one of the accurate aspects of it is that it doesn't rely on any special physics . there's no special release , no miracles . it just depends on the three things that we're wealthing now .
其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是一種資訊處理的形式 。 資訊處理需要計算 , 計算需要電腦--現有的知識下不可能不需要物質來製造電腦 。	one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing , information processing requires computation , computing requires computers the existing knowledge cannot be made without matter .
我們還需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 要使得用來記錄我們所發現知識的媒介工作 。	we also need energy to make computers , and most importantly , to make media out of the knowledge we've discovered .
第三種東西 , 較難感觸得到 , 但是在開放式的知識和解釋的開發中同樣關鍵的是證據 。	the third thing is harder to touch , but evidence is just as critical in openended knowledge and explanation .
我們的環境中充滿了證據 。	our environment is filled with evidence .
但是我們常常忽略了測試--比如 , 牛頓的地球引力定律--大約是在300年前提出的 。	but we often ignore tests things like newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .
但是我們習以為常的證據 , 從數十億年前就在地球上的每個角落裡不斷墜落 , 也會在接下來的數十億年裡繼續墜落 。 其他科學也同樣如此 。	but the evidence that we're used to , that we've been falling down everywhere on earth billions of years ago , and will continue to fall for billions of years , and so on .
就我們所知 , 發掘所有科學大部分基本真理的證據就在我們的星球上等待我們獲取 。	as far as we know , the evidence to discover most of the fundamental truths of all science is just waiting for us on our planet .
我們所在的地方充滿了證據 , 還有物質和能量 。	where we live is full of evidence , and also matter and energy .
而在星系間的空間中 , 這三個創造開放式知識的前提條件存在的可能性極端之小 。	and in intergalactic space , these three premises for creating openended knowledge are less likely .
正如我所說 , 那裡空無一物 , 寒冷 , 黑暗 。 抑或不是如此 ?	as i said , it's empty , it's cold , it's dark , it's not ?
事實上 , 這只是另外一個狹隘的誤解 。	in fact , this is just another narrow misunderstanding .
假想在星系間空間有一個立方體存在 , 與我們的房屋般大小 , 太陽系 。 以我們的標準來看 , 這個立方體非常空 , 但是它事實上仍然包含著超過百萬噸的物質 。	imagine a cube that exists in intergalactic space the size of our house , the solar system , and in our standards , that cube is very empty , but it actually contains more than a million tons of material .
一百萬噸足夠建造一個 , 比方說 , 自給自足的空間站 , 在這個空間站內聚居著一群科學家 , 他們致力於不斷創造開放式的知識 , 等等 。	one million tons is enough to build one , for example , selfsufficient space stations , a bunch of scientists who are working on creating openended knowledge , etc .
然而 , 現在的科技甚至連從星系間空間收集氫氣和將其轉化成別的元素等都遠不能做到 。	however , even the technologies that gather hydrogen from intergalactic space and translate it into other elements are far from being able to do that .
但問題是 , 在一個可理解的宇宙中 , 如果某事是物理定律所允許的 , 那麼在我們知道如何運作的情況下 , 什麼會妨礙我們去實踐它呢 ?	but the question is , in an understandable universe , if something is permitted by the laws of physics , then what would prevent us from doing it ?
換句話說 , 這是一個關於知識的問題 , 而不是關於資源 。	in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .
同樣 , 如果我們可以做到的話 , 那麼我們將自動獲得能源供給 , 因為這裡的變化將是核反應堆--證據 ?	and if we can do that , then we'll automatically get energy supply , because what's going to change here is the nuclear reaction evidence ?
還是一樣 , 對人類的感官來說那裡漆黑一片 。 但是你所需要做的是拿起一個望遠鏡 , 甚至是今天的技術設計 , 往外看去 , 你會看到我們從這兒看到的同樣的星系 。	again , it's dark for human senses , but all you have to do is pick up a telescope , even today's technology , and look out , and you'll see the same galaxies that we see from here .
如果你有一個更強大的望遠鏡 , 你將能看到恆星和行星 。	if you have a more powerful telescope , you'll see stars and planets .
在那些星系裡 , 你可以進行天體物理學研究 , 瞭解物理定律 。	in those galaxies , you can do astrophysics and learn the laws of physics .
在你所處的位置 , 你可以製造粒子加速器 , 研究初級粒子物理學 , 化學等 。	in your position , you can make particle accelerators , you can study primary particle physics , chemistry , etc .
也許最難做的科學研究是生物學實地考察 , 因為需要花費數百萬年才能往返最近的有生命的星球 。	perhaps the hardest science to do is biology field trips , because it takes millions of years to return to the nearest living planet .
但是我必須告訴你--對不起 , richard--但是我從來都不是那麼喜歡生物學實地考察 , 我想我們可以每數百萬年才進行一次 。	but i have to tell you sorry , richard but i never really liked biology field expeditions so much , i think we can do it every million years .
因此事實上 , 星系間空間並不具備創造開放式知識的前提條件 。 任何一個這樣的立方體 , 在宇宙中任何地方 , 都可以成為跟我們一樣的中心 , 如果履行這一計劃的知識確實存在的話 。	so in fact , intergalactic space doesn't have the premise of creating an openended knowledge , and any cube like this , anywhere in the universe , can be a center like ours if the knowledge of this project exists .
因此我們並不是唯一熱情好客的地方 。	so we're not the only places to be passionate .
如果星系間空間可以創造出一串開放式的解說 , 那麼幾乎其它所有的環境都是可以的 。 地球也一樣 。 被汙染的地球也是一樣 。	if intergalactic spaces can create an openended list , then pretty much every other environment is ok , the earth is the same .
而限制性因素 , 這裡和那裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充沛 , 而是知識 , 非常匱乏 。	and the limiting factor here and there , not resources , because resources are plentiful , but knowledge , very scarce .
這樣一個知識型的宇宙觀也許--我認為應該--讓我們感覺非常不平凡 。 但同時也讓我們感覺到自己的脆弱 , 因為這也意味著如果沒有那些必需的具體的知識來幫助我們應對宇宙中源源不斷地挑戰 , 我們將無法生存 。	such a cosmic view of knowledge that maybe i think should make us feel very extraordinary , but it also makes us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that necessary to help us deal with the challenges of the universe , we will not survive .
僅僅是幾光年外的一個超新星爆炸 , 我們都將必死無疑 。	just a supernova explosion just a few lightyears away , and we're all going to die .
martinrees最近剛寫了一本關於我們人類對於所有事物的脆弱性的書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗事故 , 還有最重要的擁有大規模殺傷性武器的恐怖主義 。	martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all things , from astrophysics to scientific experiments , and most importantly , terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .
他認為人類文明只有50%的機率可以存活過這個世紀 。	he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .
我想他晚些時候會在這個會上給大家講述 。	i think he'll tell you a little bit later in this conference .
但是我認為這一問題並不適合用機率來描述 。	but i don't think the odds of this problem are good for describing it .
但是我同意他就此的看法 。 我們可以生存下去 , 我們也可能不會存續 。	but i agree with him that we can survive , that we may not survive .
但是這並不取決於機率 , 而是我們是否可以及時創造出相關的知識 。	but it doesn't depend on probability , it's whether we're going to be able to create knowledge in time .
這種危險肯定不是前所未有的 。 物種一直都在滅絕 。	this danger is certainly not unprecedented . species are always extinct .
文明也會終止 。 絕大多數存在過的物種和文明都以成歷史 。	civilizations will end . the vast majority of species and civilizations exist as history .
如果我們想成為例外的話 , 邏輯上來看我們唯一的希望是利用將我們這個種群和文明與其他物種區別開的這個特徵 , 與其他一切都區別開的這個特徵 。 也就是 , 我們與物理定律得特殊關係 。 我們創造新的解釋和知識的能力--成為存在的中心 。	if we want to be an exception , logically , our only hope is to use the feature that distinguishes our species from civilization and other species , and that is , we have a special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations and knowledge becomes the center of existence .
讓我將此運用到當前的一個論戰中 , 不是因為我想提議任何特定的解決方法 , 而只是用來闡明我所要講述的一些事 。	let me apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to propose any particular solution , but just to illustrate some of the things that i'm going to talk about .
這個論戰就是全球暖化 。	this argument is global warming .
我是一個物理學家 , 但我並不是此領域的物理學家 。 就全球暖化來說 , 我只是個門外漢 。 對一個門外漢來說理智的做法是嚴肅對待權威的科學理論 。 而根據這一理論 , 已經太晚了 , 災難在所難免 。	i'm a physicist , but i'm not a physicist in this field , and as global warming , i'm just an outsider , and for an outsider , reason is a serious scientific theory of authority , and based on that theory , disaster is too late .
因為 , 如果我們目前最好的選擇是阻止二氧化碳排放的話 , 例如透過東京議定書之類的 , 限制經濟活動 , 以及花費千億美元等巨大的代價 , 那麼不管如何衡量 , 這就已經是一個災難了 。	because if our best options at the moment are to stop co2 emissions , like through tokyo protocols and things like , limiting economic activity and tens of billions of dollars and so on , then it's already a disaster no matter what the measurements are .
倡議的行動甚至都不是為解決問題 , 而只是稍微推遲災難的到來 。 因此災難在所難免 , 一切都已晚 , 或在所有人意識到這個危險之前就已經太晚了 。	the actions that are advocated are not even solving problems , they're just a little bit late for disaster arrival , and so catastrophe is inevitable , and it's all too late or it's too late to be aware of that danger .
上世紀70年代的時候也許就已經太晚了 , 那時候最先進的科學理論告訴我們工業排放將促成一個新的冰河世紀 , 數十億的人類將從此滅亡 。	it may have been too late in the 1970s , when the stateoftheart scientific theory tells us that industrial emissions will fuel a new ice age , billions of humans will die .
這一教訓對我來說清晰可見 , 我不明白為什麼它沒有傳達至公眾辯論 。	this lesson was clear to me , and i didn't understand why it didn't communicate to public debate .
事實是我們不可能永遠知道 。 當我們知道有一個災難將要降臨 , 應對這個災難的成本要比災難本身小 , 那麼就真的沒有什麼好爭論的 。	the fact is that we can never know . when we know that a disaster is coming , there's going to be a disaster response to the cost of this disaster less than the cost of the disaster itself , there's really no argument .
但是沒有任何預防措施 , 或者預防原則可以幫助我們避免我們還沒有預測到的問題 。	but no precaution or precautionary principle can help us avoid problems that we haven't anticipated yet .
因此我們需要準備好去解決問題 , 而不僅僅是避免問題 。	so we need to be prepared to solve problems , not just to avoid problems .
一盎司的預防等於一盎司的解決 , 這是事實 , 但是這只是在我們知道預防什麼的情況下 。	an ounce of prevention equals an ounce of solutions , and that's true , but it's only in case we know what prevention is .
如果你的鼻子被打了一拳 , 醫學不會教你如何閃躲拳頭 。	if your nose gets punched , medicine doesn't teach you how to hide your fists .
如果醫學不再研究治病的方法 , 而是僅僅研究預防 , 那麼它將幾乎一事無成 。	if medicine stops studying treatment , instead of studying prevention , it's almost impossible .
目前整個世界都在不計成本地忙著計劃來促成氣體排放量的減少 。	the whole world is now busy planning to promote a decrease in gas emissions .
而它應該趕緊計劃如何降低溫度 , 以及計劃如何在溫度升高之後如何生存 。 不是不計成本 , 而是有效地、廉價的計劃 。 而這樣的一些計劃已經存在了 , 比如在太空中放置大批鏡子來將太陽光反射出去 , 以及刺激海洋生物消費更多的二氧化碳 。	and it's supposed to survive temperature planning how to reduce the temperature and plan how to survive after it gets hotter , not costeffective , inexpensive programs already exist , such as putting big mirrors in space to reflect the sunlight and stimulate more carbon dioxide .
而目前 , 這些都只是邊緣研究 。	and so far these are just marginal studies .
人類在應對這個問題或者廣義上來說這些問題的時候 , 它們起不到核心作用 。	when humans cope with this problem or with broad arguments , they don't have a core effect .
對於我們並未知覺的問題 , 糾錯的能力--不是無限期的躲過期發生的絕對好運--是我們唯一的希望 , 不僅僅是為解決問題 , 而是為生存 。	the ability to tackle the unconscious , the ability to tackle wrong not the infinite luck of avoidance it's our only hope , not just for problemsolving , but for survival .
我們應該拿起兩塊石碑 , 在上邊刻上銘文 。	we should pick up two stones and have an inscription up there .
其中一塊刻上 " 問題是可以解決的 " 。	one of them is: " problems are soluble . "
另外一塊刻上 " 問題是不可避免的 " 。	the other one is , " the problem is inevitable . "
被困在不健全的制度下 , 一個國家怎麼可能脫貧呢 ? 經濟學家paulromer提出全新見解: " 特別市 " , 由多國聯合政府管理的、城市規模的管理區域 。	how could a country be out of poverty under unhealthy institutions , the economist paul romer raised an entirely new insight: special markets , governed by multinational united nations , regions of urban scale .

這些非洲學生在做功課在首都機場的街燈下因為他們家裡沒有電 。	these african students are doing homework under the streetlights of the capital airport because they don't have electricity at home .

拿那個穿綠襯衫的學生做例子 ,	take that student in green shirt .
假設他的名字叫做nelson 。	let's say his name is nelson .
我猜他肯定有個手機	i guess he's got a phone .
有趣的是 ,	and here's what's interesting .
為什麼nelson有機會享用像手機這樣的前沿科技成果但卻不能在家用上電力 ? 人們早在100年前就已經發明瞭這一科技啊 ?	why did nelson have the opportunity to enjoy the technologies of a mobile phone without having electricity at home that people had invented 100 years ago ?
答案是 " 制度 " 。	the answer is institutions .
不健全的制度會妨礙這種雙贏節決辦法的產生人們在一定的制度之下就不會將科技帶給像nelson這樣的人	unhealthy institutions can prevent the creation of winwin resolutions , and people don't institutionally bring technology to people like nelson .
什麼樣的制度呢 ?	what's the system ?
這個國家的電力公司需要遵守一條制度這個制度要求它在政府補貼的條件下從使用者收取極其低價電費事實上 , 電費便宜到另電力公司虧損的地步	the power company in this country needs to follow an institution that requires it to charge extremely low electricity prices from the user's subsidies , and in fact , electricity is cheap to the loss of an alternative company .
所以 , 電力公司既沒有資源 , 也沒有動機去給使用者接通電源	so , the power company has no resources , no motivation to the user to connect electricity .
總統想要改變這個局面	the president wanted to change it .
他已經覺察到更換體制是具可能性的 。 能讓商家盈利的體制才能使有動機爭取更多使用者	he has noticed that replacement is possible , and that the systems that make business profitable are motivated to get more users .
賣nelson的手機的那個廠家也正式在制度下經營著	the facility that sold nelson's cell phone was operating institutions .
總統已經領會到制度執行良好	the president has led to a great institutional implementation .
所以他嘗試著改變現行的電價制度但來自商人以及消費者的反對的聲音四起他們想保留現行的補貼電費制度	so he's trying to change the current electricity price system , but it comes from businesspeople and consumer opposing sounds all the way around , and they want to retain the current patchwork system .
總統無能為力 , 只能任由現行制度阻止雙贏局面產生 , 任由它妨礙改善國家	the president couldn't do anything about it , but it could just apply the current system to stop the winwin situation from improving the country .

香港其實是中國很小的一塊地方在二十世紀的絕大部分時期都在非常不同的體制下治理著與大陸其它地方都不同體制是從當時有效的市場經濟複製出來的並由英國治理	hong kong is actually a very small piece of china in the vast majority of the 20th century , governing institutions very different than any other continent , copied from the market economy at the time , and british governance .
於19世紀五十年代 , 香港是百萬大陸人去找像縫紉 , 製作玩具之類工作的地方	in the 1950s , hong kong was a million continental people looking for places like sewing and making toys or something .
但要想提高收入提高技術促進飛速增長	but to raise income , we need to increase the speed of flight .

但鄧小平本能地理解給予人民自由的重要性	but deng xiaoping understood the importance of giving people freedom .

二:在恰當的規模下操作	two: operate at the right scale .
如果你想在一個村莊改變體制 , 可以 , 但一個村的規模太小了不能帶給你如同讓百萬人一樣的效應在優質體制的治理下	if you want to change the system in a village , yes , but the scale of a village is too small to give you the same effect that millions of people have in the governance system .
另一方面 , 一下子改變全國的體制又太大了	on the other hand , the systems that change the country are too large .

所以我提議我們設想一種叫做 " 特別市 " 的東西	so i propose that we think of something called special markets .

城市才能建立起來	cities can build them .

要想成功 , 我們需要完善地體制 。 我們已經討論過了	in order to succeed , we need to have perfect systems . we've talked about them .

是真正融入了這個模型如果我們允許在無人居住的土地上建設城市的話	it's really integrated into the model if we allow cities to be built on uninhabited land .

最後 , 我們需要給領導者自由去選擇	finally , we need to give leaders the freedom to choose .
要做到給領導者自由我們需要允許國家間的合作讓不同的國家可以合作事實上像中國和英國合作一樣來首先建設一個市場經濟的飛地然後擴大至整個中國	to achieve freedom for leaders , we need to allow countries to collaborate between countries , to actually collaborate , like china and the u . k . , to first build a market economy and scale up to china .
或多或少 , 英國 , 不經意地在上個世紀它治理香港期間對削減世界貧困上做出了比任何支援專案都更為卓越的貢獻	more or less , britain , inadvertently , in the last century , managed hong kong to make a more extraordinary contribution to reducing world poverty than any support program .
所以只要我們允許這樣的合作重演我們可以將這個效應擴大的整個世界的規模	so if we allow this kind of collaboration to reproduce , we can scale this across the world .

從艱苦漫長的環球探險中 , 基因組學先驅克雷格•文特忙裡偷閒 , 為我們講述其團隊描繪海洋生物多樣性的歷程 。 到目前為止 , 他們已經發現了數百萬的基因 。	from a long , long global adventure , genomics pioneered craig venter's busy talking about the journey of marine biodiversity for us , and so far , they've found millions of genes .

克雷格•文特:dna和海洋	craig venter: dna and the ocean .
休息的時候 , 有幾個人過來問我對老齡化問題怎麼看	at rest , a couple of people came to ask me what i thought about aging .
我的唯一看法是	my only opinion is this .
我認為樂觀主義者比悲觀主義者活得久得多	i think optimists live a lot longer than pessimists .
在這18分鐘裡我將告訴你們的是我們是如何做到從最初的閱讀遺傳編碼發展到我們自己開始編寫遺傳編碼	what i'm going to tell you about in those 18 minutes is how we've gone from reading genetic code to reading our own genetic code .
僅僅十年之前的這個月我們發表了第一個來自自由活動生命體的基因序列即流感嗜血桿菌的序列	this month just a decade ago , we published the first gene sequence of living organisms , the sequence of haemophilus .
由此我們將基因組專案完成的時間從13年降到4個月	so we've gone from 13 years to four months by doing the genome project .
現在 , 同樣的基因組專案只需要2到8個小時	now , the same genome project only takes two to eight hours .
因此過去十年 , 我們完成了大量的基因組測序大部分的人類病原體幾種植物多種昆蟲和哺乳動物包括人類基因組	so over the last 10 years , we've done a lot of sequencing genomes , most of the pathogens of the human pathogen , and a few plants , many species of insects and mammals
約在十年前我們對基因組學發展的設想是到今年年底的時候我們或許能完成3到5個基因組的測序而事實上已經完成了數百個	about a decade ago , our assumptions about genomics were that by the end of this year , we might be able to sequence three to five genomes , and in fact , hundreds of them have been completed .
我們剛剛從戈登-貝蒂•摩爾基金會獲得一筆資助作為環境有機體專案的副專案我們將在今年完成130個基因組的測序	we just got a funding project from gordon betty moore foundation as a side project of environmental organisms projects , and we're going to sequence 130 genomes this year .
閱讀遺傳編碼的速率已然改變	the rate of reading genetic code has changed .
但我們看到 , 未來的路還很長我們僅僅探索了這個星球表面上淺淺的一層	but we see that the future is long , and we've only explored its shallow surface .
大多數人沒有意識到這些肉眼看不到的生物微生物構成了地球約一半的生物量而所有的動物加起來也才佔地球生物量的千分之一	most people don't realize that these invisible microbes make up about half of the biomass on earth , and all animals add up to a thousandth of the biomass of the earth .
跑到海邊喝上一口海水或許不是牛津人經常做的事但請記住每一毫升的海水裡有大約一百萬個的細菌其中的病毒更是以千萬計	go to the beach and drink a bite of seawater that maybe not oxford people do regularly , but keep in mind that every milliliter of seawater has about a million bacteria , and that virus is hundreds of millions of viruses .
兩年前只有不到五千種的微生物被鑑定歸類於是我們決定做些這方面的事情	less than 5 , 000 microbes were identified two years ago , so we decided to do something about it .
我們啟動了巫師二號考察和其他大型的海洋考察活動一樣我們嘗試每200英里採一次樣	we launched a shaman ii expedition , like any other big ocean expedition , and we tried to take a sample every 200 miles .
考察伊始 , 我們在百慕大進行了測試專案然後前往哈利法克斯接著到美國東海岸加勒比海、巴拿馬運河穿過加拉帕哥斯群島 , 然後橫跨太平洋現在我們正在穿越印度洋的過程中	we tested it in bermuda , and then we went to halifax , and then we went to the east coast of the united states , the caribbean , the panama canal , and we went across the galapagos , and now we're in the process of going across the indian ocean .
工作很艱難 , 我們乘著一艘帆船某種程度上我們想透過它激起年輕人投身科學的興趣	it's hard work . we're in a sailing boat , and in a way we're interested in getting young people into science .
實驗其實非常簡單	it's a very simple experiment .
採集海水 , 過濾用不同的過濾器採集不同大小的生物然後把它們的dna帶回羅克韋爾的實驗室在那裡我們可以每24小時測完一億字元的遺傳編碼	we take seawater , we take different filters , we take different size organisms , and we take their dna back to rokwell's lab , where we can actually measure 100 million cross genetic code every 24 hours .
透過這些我們已經有了一些驚人的發現	and through that , we've made some surprising discoveries .
比如我們眼睛裡的視色素之前認為自然界中只有一到兩種生物擁有和我們一樣的視色素	for instance , pigments in our eyes thought that only one or two organisms in nature had the same pigments as us .
但後來發現在溫暖海區的上層海水中幾乎每個物種都擁有這類光受體並利用陽光作為能量來源和交流工具	but it turns out that in the upper region of the warm sea , almost every species has this light receptor that uses sunlight as a source and communication tool .
僅僅一個採集點 , 從一桶水中我們就能發現1300萬個新基因相當於5萬個新種	just one collection point , and from a barrel of water , we can see that 13 million new genes are equivalent to 50 , 000 new ones .
藉助來自斯隆基金會的資助我們已經將研究擴充套件到空氣中	by funding from the sloan foundation , we've expanded our research into the air .
我們正在測算 , 在我們每天呼吸的空氣中漂浮著多少病毒和細菌特別是在飛機和禮堂等封閉環境中	we're calculating how many viruses and bacteria are floating in the air we breathe every day , particularly in closed environments like airplanes and auditoriums .
我們透過一些簡單的儀器進行過濾在紐約市某棟建築的頂上僅用一天我們就過濾出數十億計的微生物	we filtered billions of microbes on the top of a building in new york city , just a day , and we filtered billions of microbes .
目前我們正在對它們進行測序	we're currently sequencing them .
單純從資料蒐集方面僅僅在加拉帕戈斯群島我們就發現幾乎每200英里我們都能從採集的樣品中看到巨大的多樣性	just from the dataset , just from the galapagos islands alone , we found that almost every 200 miles we could see a huge diversity in the sample collection .
不同的溫度梯度或許可以部分解釋這種多樣性	different temperature gradients may well be explaining a little bit about this diversity .
這是一張基於溫度的衛星圖片紅色表示溫暖區域藍色表示冷的區域我們發現 , 在溫暖海水中獲得樣品與冷海水中的樣品在物種的豐富程度上具有極大的差異	this is a satellite based on temperature , showing warm areas in red , cool areas in blue , and what we found was that samples and samples in the warm seas are very different in the richness of the species .
另一個讓我們感到驚奇的事情是這些光受體能探測到不同波長的光而我們能透過它們的氨基酸序列來推測這一過程	another surprising thing for us is that these receptors can detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that through their amino acid sequences .
不同區域之間 , 它們也差別巨大	different regions , they're very different .
或許不是很讓人驚奇在幾乎是幽藍的深海里光受體傾向於 " 看 " 到藍光	it's probably not surprising that nearly ufosome , deep ocean receptors tend to see , to blue light .
而當週圍存在大量葉綠素的時候它們則 " 看 " 到許多綠光	and when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .
在向較極端的紅外和紫外波段移動時光受體的差別可能更大	the difference between the extreme infrared and the ultraviolet period is probably even larger .
為了對我們採集的所有基因進行評估我們彙總了所有資料包括到目前為止考察所得的所有資料代表了地球上超過一半的基因資料總共約2900萬個基因	to assess all of the genes that we've collected , we've collected all the data , including all of the data from the expeditions so far represents more than half of the genetic data on the planet , about 29 million genetic data .
我們把這些基因放入基因家族中試圖回答:我們是發現了已知基因家族中的新成員還是發現了新的基因家族 ?	we put these genes into gene families , trying to answer: are we finding new members of the known genome family , or are we discovering new gene family members ?
結果表明我們找到了大約5萬個主要的基因家族但我們從環境中獲得的每個新樣品都只是對這些新基因家族的線性補充	it turns out that we've found about 50 , 000 major gene family members , but every new sample we've obtained from the environment is simply linear to these new genomic families .
因此我們正處在發現地球生命及其組成部分和基因基礎的最初階段	so we're in the earliest stages of discovering life on earth and its component parts and genetic basis .
我們來看下所謂的進化樹我們人類就在右上角 , 和動物們在一起	we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , and we humans are in the upper righthand corner with animals .
在動物界約2900萬個基因中我們的基因組才僅僅擁有24000個基因	we only have about 29 million genes in the animal kingdom , and we only have 2 , 400 genes .
如果把所有的動物算在一起我們與之分享著不到30000可能在1.2萬或再多數千的不同的基因家族	if we calculate all the animals together , we share less than 3 , 000 animals , possibly 12 , 000 , or more , thousands of different gene family .
現在我不僅僅將這些基因視為進化的設計元件	now , i don't just think of these genes as evolutionary design components .
而且我們要從 " 基因中心觀點 " 或許要追溯到理查德•道金斯的理論而非 " 基因組中心觀點 " 來思考它們對這些基因元件的構造方式是不同的	and we're going to go back to richard dawkins' theory of genomecentric view , rather than genomecentric views , to think about how they're made of these genetic components differently .
合成dna , 即人工合成dna的能力在過去的十年或二十年裡與dna測序的能力在某種程度上是同步發展的而且都變得越來越快速和廉價	synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has been in sync with dna sequencing over the last 10 or 20 years , in some ways in sync with dna sequencing , and it's getting faster and cheaper .
有關合成基因組的想法是在1995年我們對第二個基因組即生殖道支原體測序的時候想到的	the idea for the synthetic genome was in 1995 , and we thought about the second genitalia , the genitalia sequencing .
我們還製作了相當不錯的t恤寫著 , " 我愛惜我的生殖器 "	we also made a pretty good tshirt that said , " i love my genitalia . "
這其實只不過是個微小的生物	it's just a tiny creature .
卻擁有近500個基因	it has nearly 500 genes .
嗜血桿菌擁有1800個基因	haemophilus has 1 , 800 genes .
我們提出疑問如果某物種需要800個基因 , 另一種需要500個是否能用一套更小的基因組成一個微小的可運作生命系統	we asked if one species needed 800 genes , the other 500 genes , could be made out of a smaller set of genomes , a tiny , tiny , operating system .
於是我們開始做轉座子的突變發生	so we started mutating the seat .
轉座子是隨機插入遺傳編碼之中的短的dna片段	the transmitter is short pieces of dna that randomly insert into the genetic code .
如果轉座子插入到基因中間 , 就會擾亂基因的功能	if you insert a seat in the middle of the gene , it disrupts the function of the gene .
因此我們找出所有能夠接受轉座子插入的基因併為這些 " 非必需基因 " 製作了 " 地圖 "	so we looked at all the genes that could be inserted into the transfer and made the map not necessarily by necessary .
但結果我們發現環境對此的影響非常關鍵我們只能根據環境中確實存在的條件來定義必需和非必需基因	but it turns out that the environment is critical to this , and we can only define the need and nonnecessary genes according to the conditions that exist in the environment .
我們還試圖做一個更直觀的研究對13個有親緣關係的生物我們試圖比較它們的基因組 , 看它們是否有相同之處	we also tried to do a more intuitive study of 13 animals with relationships , and we tried to compare their genomes to see if they had the same things .
於是我們得到了這些重疊的圓圈 , 我們發現只有173個基因在這所有13種生物中是相同的	so we got these overlapping circles , and we found out that only 173 genes are the same in all 13 species .
如果忽略掉一個細胞內寄生物的話這個基因庫還能擴充套件一點當我們審視核心的一組約310個基因時基因庫擴大更多	if we ignore a parasite in a cell , this gene pool can expand a little bit more when we look at a core set of 310 genes , and the gene pool expands even more .
因此我們認為可以從最少500個基因擴充套件或縮小取決你怎麼看這個問題到約300到400個基因	so we thought we could go from the minimum 500 gene extension kits or minimum genes , and determine how you think about this problem , to something like 300 or 400 genes .
證明這些理論的唯一方法是以這些基因人工構建一個染色體而且我們必須用基於表達框的方式來達到這一目的	the only way to prove these theories is to build a chromosome out of these genes , and we have to do it based on the framework .
我們發現大片段精確合成dna是非常非常困難的	and what we found was that large pieces of synthetic dna were very , very difficult .
我的同事漢姆•史密斯和克萊德•哈欽森發明了一個讓人振奮的新方法能讓我們在短短兩週時間內合成一個擁有5000個鹼基對的病毒而且在基因序列和生物學特性上都百分百精確	my colleague han smith and clay hutchinson have invented an exciting new way to synthesize a virus with 5 , 000 base pairs in just two weeks , and 100 percent accurate in gene sequencing and biology .
那是個相當讓人興奮的實驗:我們僅僅把合成的dna片段注進細菌中 , 突然之間dna就開始引導病毒顆粒的合成而病毒反過來殺死了細菌	it was a very exciting experiment: we just injected synthetic pieces of dna into bacteria , and all of a sudden , dna starts to guide the synthesis of virus particles , and viruses come and kill bacteria .
這並非第一個合成的病毒一年前已有某種脊髓灰質炎病毒被製造了出來但這卻是唯一達到百分之一活性的病毒耗時三年才合成成功	it's not the first synthetic virus that was made a year ago , but it was the only virus that got to one percent of active it took three years to synthesize .
這是phix-174結構的一個動畫	this is an animation of the structure of phix174 .
這是軟體為自己構建硬體的活例子也為我們的生物學提供了新想法	this is a living example of software that builds hardware for ourselves and provides new ideas for our biology .
有人立即開始擔心生物武器的威脅不久前我也在參議院委員會和另一個由美國政府成立旨在評價這一領域的特殊委員會上作證	immediately , i was worried about the threat of biological weapons , and not long ago , i was at the senate committee and another special committee that the u . s . government was aiming for .
我認為最重要的是將事實牢記在心而非人們對事情發生的想象	i think the most important thing is to remember the facts , not the kinds of things that people think about them .
基本上 , 任何現在已經被測序的病毒其基因組都可以被合成	basically , any virus that has been sequenced now can be synthesized .
人們立馬被埃博拉病毒或天花病毒之類等嚇壞了但從這些生物體中提取的dna並不具有感染力	people were horrified by things like the ebola virus or smallpox , but the dna extracted from these organisms was not contagious .
因此即使有人制成了天花病毒基因組其dna本身並不會引發感染	so even if somebody made the smallpox virus genome , its dna itself wouldn't cause the infection .
安全部門真正需要擔心的是 " 設計者病毒 "	the security department really needs to worry about designer viruses .
只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯曾經花大力氣致力於生物武器的研製	only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union have spent an effort on biological weapons .
如果這些研究真的已經終止那麼在未來人為製造出設計者病毒的機率微乎其微	if these studies have really stopped , the odds of making designer viruses in the future are significant .
我想兩年內製造出單細胞生物是可能的	i think it's possible in two years to make singlecelled organisms .
而真核細胞我們自己擁有的這種細胞也可能在十年內製造出來	and the real nuclear cells that we have can be made in a decade .
我們可以區分開進入這個人工基因組的不同表達框和不同基因使得我們能構建數十種不同的結構	we can separate into different expressive boxes and different genes of this artificial genome , allowing us to construct dozens of different structures .
關鍵是 , 如何把所有其他的放進來 ?	the key is , how do you put all the other in ?
我們從這些片段開始然後透過一個同源重組系統將其組合到染色體中	we start with these clips , and then we combine them together through a homologous recombination system to a chromosome .
這來自一種名為耐輻射奇異球菌的生物能在三百萬拉德的輻射劑量下保持活力	this comes from a creature called deinococcus radiodurans that remains alive in three million radical doses .
在暴露輻射約12到24小時其染色體幾乎完全破碎的情況下它還能將自身的染色體重新組裝起來	in exposure radiation for about 12 to 24 hours , the chromosome is almost completely broken , and it can also reassemble its own chromosomes .
這種生物在地球上幾乎無處不在甚至由於人類的活動它們還可能在外太空活動	these organisms are almost everywhere on earth , and even because of human activity , they may be active in outer space .
這是玻璃燒杯在約50萬拉德輻射下的情形	this is a burning glass of about half a million radical radiation .
玻璃開始燃燒 , 爆裂而位於底部的微生物則似乎越來越開心	glass starts to burn , burns , and microbes at the bottom seem to be getting happier and happier .
這是實際的情形上面是經過170萬拉德輻射之後的染色體	this is a practical scenario of a chromosome after 17 million rads of radiation .
幾乎已經支離破碎	it's almost broken .
下面是24小時之後同樣的dna自動重組的結果	and here's what happens with the same dna automatically recombined 24 hours later .
這些生物能做到的真是歎為觀止 。 如果不是數以萬計的話也許我們還能找到數以千計的物種也同樣能夠做到	these organisms are truly extraordinary , and if not tens of thousands , maybe we'll be able to find thousands and thousands of other species , too .
這些基因組合成之後第一步就是將它們移植到另一個沒有基因組的細胞中	the first step after these genomes are to transplant them into cells with no genomes .
因此我們認為合成細胞將具有巨大的前景不僅僅在生物學基礎的理解上而且很可能幫我們應對環境和社會問題	so we think that synthetic cells are going to have huge promise not just for biologybased understanding , but potentially for environmental and social problems .
例如 , 從我們測序的第三種生物詹氏甲烷球菌 , 生活在相當於水沸點的高溫中以氫作為能量來源並依靠捕獲環境中的二氧化碳為自己提供所需的碳	for instance , from the third species we sequenced , methane bacteria lived at the equivalent of hydrogen boiling at high temperatures , using hydrogen as a source of energy , and relying on carbon dioxide in the environment to provide
由此可知 , 透過大量不同的途徑數以千計的生物能夠捕獲並依賴二氧化碳生存	and it turns out that thousands of organisms can capture and depend on carbon dioxide .
因此我們可以透過捕獲大氣中的碳製造生物高聚物或其他產品來替代從石油中工業合成的碳製品	so we can replace carbon products that are synthesized from the oil industrial oil by capturing carbon in the atmosphere , or other products .
有種依賴一氧化碳的生物我們利用其還原能力使水分子破裂 , 製造出氫和氧	there's a creature that depends on carbon dioxide , and we're using its ability to crack the water molecules and make hyd
同樣 , 還有許多途徑能夠用來轉化甲烷	similarly , there are many ways to translate methane .
杜邦公司和挪威石油公司有一大型專案就是把挪威油氣田中的甲烷轉化為有用的產品	the largest project for dupont and norwegian oil is to convert methane into useful products in norway's oil fields .
我突然想到 , 將有一個新的領域 " 組合基因組學 " 很快就要誕生因為有了這些新的合成方法有了這麼龐大的基因序列和同源重組我們可以設計出一個能夠每天生產近百萬個染色體的機器人	and it struck me that there was a new field called combinatoric genomics that was going to be born very quickly , because with these new synthesis methods , there was this huge genome sequence and homologous recombination , we could design a robot that could produce almost a million chromosomes a day .
因此 , 所有的生物學特徵都能透過螢幕來選擇無論是製造氫化學合成 , 或者僅僅是生存能力	so all the biology features can be selected through screens , either by making hydrogen chemicals , or simply by making survival .
理解這些基因的功能將變得觸手可及	understanding what these genes are going to do will become a tentacle .
我們正嘗試改進光合作用以直接在陽光下製造出氫	we're trying to improve photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly in the sun .
光合作用受氧調節而我們使用的對氧不敏感的氫化酶將完全改變這一過程	photosynthesis is oxygenregulated , and the hydrogenins that we're using are completely changing this process .
我們還整合了多種纖維素酶這些酶可以把複雜的糖類分解為簡單的糖類並在同一個細胞內發酵產生酒精	we also integrate cellulose enzymes , which enzymes can break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentate in the same cell to produce alcohol .
在一些大型的實驗室裡已經開始利用微生物進行藥品生產	in some large laboratories , we're starting to use microbes to make drugs .
環境中化合物的化學比我們最好的化學家制造出來的化合物還要複雜很多	the chemical compounds in the environment are much more complicated than our best chemists make up compounds .
也許未來的工程物種將成為我們的食物來源能量來源環境補救手段甚至取代石化行業	perhaps the future engineering species will be our food source energy sources , environmental remedies , and even replace the fossil industry .
最後讓我以道德和政策上的研究結束吧	let me end with morality and policy research .
我們推遲了1999年開始的實驗直到對是否應該嘗試製造人工物種這一問題進行了一年半的生物倫理學討論後實驗才繼續進行	we late to the 1999 experiment , until the question of whether we should try to make artificial species , which took a year and a half of our bioethical discussions to continue .
每個主要宗教都參與其中	every major religion is involved .
真是一項奇怪的研究因為許多宗教領袖都以他們的教義、經文作為法律而且不能從中找出禁止製造生命的條文所以這應該沒什麼問題最根本的擔憂來自生物武器方面但只有開始進行這些實驗之後我們才能找出從事這一切的原因	it's a strange study , because many religious leaders are using their creed , their scriptures , and they can't find the doctrines that prohibit life , so there's nothing wrong with this very fundamental concern that comes from biological weapons , but only after doing these experiments can we figure out what's going on .
目前斯隆基金會已經資助了一個相關的多機構參與的研究以確定這些實驗給社會帶來的風險和益處同時也為像我們這樣的科學團隊在這一領域開展研究制定規則在前進的同時我們也努力成為一個良好的榜樣	now the sloan foundation has funded a multiinstitutional study to identify the risks and benefits of these experiments for social groups like us , and to build the rules forward , and we're also trying to be a good example .
有許多複雜的議題	there's a lot of complex issues .
除了生物恐怖主義它們其實都很簡單:我們能否設計出生產清潔能源的工具透過各種不同的簡單步驟或能徹底改變發展中國家的能源生產模式	besides bioterrorism , they're very simple: can we design tools to produce clean energy through various simple steps , or can we fundamentally change the way energy production is in the developing world ?
心理學家philipzimbardo說我們大部分人都忽略了幸福和成功的來源:那就是我們觀望過去、面向現在和展望未來 。 要想改善生活質量 , 他建議我們首先要調整時間觀念 。	the psychologist philipzimbardo suggests that most of us overlook the source of happiness and success: that's what we see in the past , in the present and in the present and in the future , and to improve the quality of life , he suggests that we first have to adjust our time .
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	happiness , mind , psychology .
philipzimbardo健康的時間觀念	philip zimbardo's health time perspective .
我想跟你們分享一些對時間的神秘力量的看法當然是在很短的時間內	i want to share with you some of the mysterious powers of time , of course , in a very short period of time .

快 , 亞當 , 別磨磨<unk>的 , 就咬一口 , 我已咬過了	fast , adam , don't mill , just bite , i've bitten .
