生活中充滿了誘惑 。 而且到處都是:屈服或反抗是、不是、現在、隨後、衝動、沉穩專注現在和展望未來	life is full of temptations , and it's everywhere: submission or resistance , yes , now , impulsive , steady focus on the present and the future .
激情時刻一旦到來 , 道德束縛將皆被打破	when the passions come , the moral constraints will be broken .
那些承諾婚前無性行為的女孩–這裡感謝下小布什總統大多數 , 大概百分之六十的人在一年之內就違背了自己的承諾	those girls who committed prior to sexual activity thanks to president george bush , the majority , about 60 percent of them , defeated their commitment within a year .
而這些人幾乎沒采取任何 " 安全措施 "	and these people have barely accepted any safety measures .
多麼多的承諾啊	what a promise .
現在我們來試試引誘4歲的孩子 , 拿他們來做個試驗	now let's try this with a fouryearold . let's do an experiment with them .
他們現在有一個棉花糖 , 如果他們能夠等到實驗員回來再吃的話 , 就可以得到2個棉花糖	they now have a marshmallow , and if they wait for the experimenter to come back , they'll get two marshmallows .
這當然是需要付出的 , 如果你真喜歡吃棉花糖的話 , 那就等著	of course it's necessary to pay if you really like eating marshmallows , that's waiting .
但結果是3分之2的孩子屈服於誘惑	but it turns out that twothirds of children submit to temptation .
他們等不了 。 當然 , 其它的孩子都得到了第二個棉花糖	they couldn't wait . and of course , all the other kids got the second marshmallow .
因為他們抵抗了誘惑 。 他們甘於先苦後甜 。	because they resist temptation . they sweet .
沃特米塞奇 , 是我在斯坦福大學的同事他在14年後重新找到這些孩子並去勘察他們現時的情況	wat mitcher , my colleague at stanford university , who , 14 years later , reclaimed these children and explored what was happening to them .
結果發現這兩組孩子在各個方面都有著巨大的差異	and it turns out that these two groups have enormous differences in all sorts of ways .
那些等到了第二個棉花糖的孩子在sat中比另一組得分平均高250分	the kids who waited for the second marshmallow were 250 points higher than the other group in sat .
這是多麼大的差異啊 ! 這根本就是兩組智商水平不同的孩子啊	it's a huge difference . it's a different set of i . q . kids .
他們都沒有任何問題 , 都是好學生	they don't have any problems . they're good students .
他們自信而且果斷 。 那麼今天我所要說的關鍵是同樣也是你們的關鍵點就是由 " 面向現在 " 轉變為 " 展望未來 "	they're selfconfident and decisive . so the key point i'm going to talk about today is that it's also your critical point , which is to turn from " the present " to " the future . "
那什麼是時間洞察力呢 ? 這將是我下面要講的	so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about .
時間洞察力是研究個人包括我們在內 , 如何以時間區域或時間類別為單位劃分自身的經歷體驗 。	time perspective is the study of individuals , including us , how to divide our experiences in time zones or time categories .
其實我們一直都在自然而然地做著	we've been doing it all the time .
而影響我們劃分方式的因素有很多 , 包括不同的文化背景、國家個人、社會階層以及不同的教育背景	and there are many factors that influence the way we divide , including different cultural backgrounds , nations , individuals , social classes , and different
問題是由於這些因素的存在 , 最終導致時間洞察力都具是片面的因為你學會經常使用其中的一些 , 而其他的則被很少使用	the problem is that these factors exist , and they ultimately lead to time perspective , because you learn to use some of them all the time , and others are rarely used .
是什麼促使你做出那些選擇 ?	what makes you make those choices ?
你所做的決定是基於你怎麼採取行動的	the decision you make is based on how you act .
對一些人來說 , 這個決定只是基於現狀另一些人是基於他們的直覺 。	for some people , this decision is only based on the status quo and the other based on their intuition .
對於那些基於現狀而做決定的人我們稱呼他們為: " 面向現在 " 因為他們專注於現正發生的事情	for those who make the decisions based on the status quo , we call them " face to the present , " because they focus on what's happening right now .
對於另一些人來說 , 現正發生什麼並不重要	it doesn't matter what's happening to other people .
就好像是說: " 我以前好像經歷過類似的事情 " 一樣	it's like , " i've been through something like this before . "
所以 , 他們基於過去的經驗來做決定	so they're making decisions based on their experiences .
我們稱呼這些人為: " 觀望過去 " , 因為他們專注於過去	we call these people " the looking of the past , " because they focus on the past .
還有一部分人 , 他們的考慮不是基於現在 , 也不是過去而是未來	and some of them , not based on the present , not the past , but the future .
他們專注於預期的結果	they focus on the expected results .
我們稱呼這些人為:展望未來 。 因為他們專注於將來會是怎麼樣的	we call these people the future , because they're focused on what's going to happen in the future .
那麼 , 時間悖論 , 這裡我要討論的是:時間洞察力的悖論會不會有某個因素影響你做出的每一個決定而你又完全不知 ?	so here's the paradox of time: is there a paradox of time perception that affects every single decision you make that you don't know at all ?
那你就具有某種程度上的片面的時間洞察力	so you have a certain amount of time perspective .
實際上是有六種時間洞察力 , 其中兩個屬於 " 面向現在 "	there are actually six kinds of perspectives , two of which are now .
兩個屬於 " 觀望過去 " , 還有兩個屬於 " 展望未來 "	two of them are called " the past , " and two of them are " the future . "
你可以專注於 " 積極經歷 " 或 " 消極經歷 "	you can focus on active experience , or negative experience .
也可以專注於 " 享受現在 " 指的是你專注於生活中的快樂 , 或者自身宿命這些都無所謂 , 因為你的生活盡在掌握	it can also be focused on enjoying the present , meaning that you're focused on the pleasures of your life , or your own destiny , and that doesn't matter , because your life is in control .
當然 , 你也可以 " 展望未來 " , 設定一個目標	of course , you can also look at the future and set a goal .
或者超越未來指的是:生命在死後重新開始	or beyond the future , meaning that life begins again after death .
透過增強精神靈活性來順利地提升時間洞察力這有賴於環境的需求這就是你要學著去做的	by increasing flexibility , insight goes up smoothly , and that's dependent on the environment , and that's what you learn to do .
那麼 , 什麼是最佳的時間洞察力呢 ?	so what's the best time perspective ?
高度依賴於 " 積極經歷 " , 適度依賴於未來	high dependence on the positive experience , adaptability depends on the future .
適度依賴於 " 享受現在 "	adaptability depends on enjoying the present .
永遠不考慮 " 消極經歷 " 和 " 宿命論 "	never think about negative experiences and fatalism .
其實 , 最佳的時間洞察力是由你過去的經歷 " 積極經歷 " 奠定了基礎 , 你和你的家庭 , 獨立自主	in fact , the optimal insight is laid down by your past experience of activism , you and your family , independently .
從未來得到是值得奮鬥的目標 , 新的挑戰	receiving from the future is a fighting goal , a new challenge .
從 " 享受現在 " 中得到的是動力去探索自身世界、他人以及原始需求	what you get from enjoying the present is motivation to explore its own world , its other and its original needs .
任何時間洞察力中總是負性多於正性的	insight is always more negative than positive at any given time .
舉個例子:為了將來的成功我們需要犧牲些什麼呢 ?	for example: what do we need to sacrifice in the future of success ?
我們需要犧牲和家庭在一起的時光 , 需要犧牲和朋友在一起的時光	we need to sacrifice time with our family when we need to sacrifice time with our friends .
需要犧牲那些快樂的時光 , 需要犧牲個人嗜好	we need to sacrifice those happy times . we need to sacrifice personal hobbies .
需要犧牲業餘愛好 , 需要犧牲睡眠時間 。 因此會影響身體健康	we need to sacrifice hobby , we need to sacrifice our sleep , and therefore we can affect our health .
他們的生活中只有工作、成就和控制慾	they only live in jobs and accomplishments and control of desire .
我保證你們在座的一些人會對此引起共鳴	i'm sure some of you will resonate with this .
這些與我引起了共鳴 , 我出生於南布朗克斯貧民窟中的一個貧困的西西里島人的家庭中 。 每個人都是在沉<unk>過去和活在當下	and it resonated with me that i was born in a poor cysilian family in the south bronx slum in a ghetto in the south bronx .

現在我學會了 " 享受現在 " , 同時也學會了觀望 " 積極經歷 " 因此 , 在我76歲的時候 , 我感覺到從沒有過的精力、動力現在的我比以前任何時候都要快樂 !	now i've learned to enjoy the present , and i've learned to enjoy the present , and i've learned to enjoy the positive experience , so at the age of 76 , i feel that the energy that i've never been , the moment i'm happier than ever before .

道理是簡單且顯而易見的但結論是深奧的	the reason is simple and obvious , but the conclusion is profound .
今天的頭條有多少會影響100年 , 1000年 ? kirkcitron " 長遠新聞 " 專案收集那些不僅在今天有影響 , 而且還會影響幾十年甚至幾百年 。 在ted2010上 , 他指出最近的哪些頭條訊息對塑造未來具有潛在的影響	how many headlines are going to affect 100 years , 1 , 000 years ? kirkcitron collected projects that don't just affect today , but they're going to affect for hundreds of years . on ted2010 , he pointed out which headlines have a potential impact on shaping the future .

村民將失去40%的土地並被包圍起來失去從這裡進入約旦河西岸地區的自由	the villagers will lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , and they will lose freedom from here to the west bank .

我給大家播放影片的一些片斷讓你們大致瞭解實地發生的情況	i'm going to show you some clips from the video to give you a sense of what's actually happening .
巴勒斯坦女子:他們說那堵圍牆會將巴勒斯坦和以色列分隔開來	palestinian woman: they said the wall would separate palestine from israel .
在佈德魯斯我們意識到那堵牆會搶佔我們的土地	in berrus , we realized that the wall was going to take over our land .
以色列男子:這堵圍牆事實上是防止恐怖行動的一項解決方法	israeli man: the wall is actually a solution to preventing terrorism .
今天我號召大家加入一場和平的遊行	today , i'm calling for a peaceful march .
與你們並肩行動的是幾十位以色列兄弟姊妹	working side by side with you are dozens of israeli brothers and sisters .
以色列行動主義者:最令軍隊害怕的就是非暴力抵抗	israeli activist: what scares the army most is nonviolent resistance .
女子:我們看到男人們試圖推開那些士兵但是沒有人成功	woman: we saw men trying to release soldiers , but nobody succeededed .
而我認為姑娘們能夠做到	and i think girls can do it .
法塔赫組織成員:我們必須清空頭腦中傳統的觀念	fatah members: we need to empty the conventional wisdom in our heads .
哈馬斯組織成員:我們是完全和平的我們希望讓它遍及整個巴勒斯坦	hamas: we're completely peaceful , and we want it to go all over palestine .
口號聲:團結一致的民族	slogan: solidarity .
法塔赫哈馬斯人民陣線	the fatah hamas people's fronts .
新聞主播:圍牆附近的衝突仍在繼續	news anchor: conflicts around the wall continue .
記者:以色列邊警受命驅逐抗議人群	interviewer: israeli police are deported by protesters .
他們被允許採用一切必要的強制手段	they were allowed to adopt the mandatory means of everything necessary .
男子:他們正在開火	man: they're fired .
這裡就像費盧傑到處是槍聲	it's like ferluje is shooting everywhere .
以色列行動主義者:我知道我們是去送死	israeli activist: i know we're going to die .
但是我身邊的許多人沒有一絲畏懼	but a lot of people around me are not afraid .
以色列士兵:一場非暴力抗議無法阻止我們建立這堵牆	israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest can't stop us from building this wall .
抗議者:這是一場和平的示威遊行	protesters: this is a peaceful protest march .
我們不需要使用暴力	we don't need to use violence .
口號聲:我們必勝我們必勝	slogan: we must win .
朱莉婭•帕夏:當我第一次聽說佈德魯斯的這段故事我感到非常驚訝全球媒體居然沒有報道在2003年也就是七年以前所發生的這一系列了不起的事件	julia parcha: when i first heard this story from bedrus , it was very surprising to me that there was no newspaper in 2003 , which was this amazing series of events that happened seven years ago .
而更令人吃驚的是佈德魯斯最終取得了勝利	and what's even more surprising is that berros eventually won a victory .
經過長達10個月的和平抵抗運動那裡的居民說服了以色列政府將圍牆從他們的土地遷出轉而遷到綠線上也就是國際公認的巴以領土分界線上	after 10 months of peaceful resistance , the residents convinced the israeli government to migrate from their lands to the green line , the international recognition of baseline .
佈德魯斯的抵抗運動的影響從此遍及約旦河西岸的所有村莊以及耶路撒冷境內的巴勒斯坦人居住區	the effect of the bandrusian resistance movement has spread across all of the villages in the west bank and palestinian settlements in jerusalem .
然而媒體對這些事件幾乎隻字未提	but the media has very little to say about these events .
這種漠視給巴勒斯坦非暴力運動的成長甚至生存產生了沉重的打擊	this indifference gives the growth of nonviolent movements in palestine and even the survival of survival .
暴力抵抗和非暴力抵抗有一個非常重要的共同點兩者像一個劇院渴望吸引觀眾的青睞	violence resistance and nonviolent resistance have a very important common denominator: a desire to attract audiences .
如果暴力演員總是領銜主演將全球目光聚焦巴勒斯坦問題那麼非暴力領導人就很難向他們的民眾證明和平的反抗才是帶他們脫離苦海的可行方案	if violent actors are always leading titles to focus globally on palestinian problems , then nonviolent leaders are struggling to prove peaceful resistance to their citizens that it's possible to take them out of the sea .
在座為人父母的估計對關注的力量並不陌生	the estimates for a parent are not unfamiliar with the power of attention .
如果孩子第一次鬧脾氣就得到父母的注意那麼你的孩子以後肯定會鬧得更厲害	if your child ever gets a parent's notice for the first time , then your child's going to be even more awesome .
鬧脾氣就會成為兒童心理學家所說的功能性行為孩子學會用這種方式引起父母的注意	the tantrum becomes what children psychologists call functional behavior , and the child learns to catch the attention of their parents in this way .
父母可以透過關注或不予理睬來鼓勵或抑制此行為	parents can encourage or inhibit this behavior by ignoring or ignoring their attention .
而這也適用於成年人	and this applies to adults .
事實上社群和國家的行為是能夠受到影響而改變的而這取決於國際社會選擇關注的方面	in fact , the behavior of communities and countries can be affected and changed , depending on the international selection of the international community .
我相信解決中東地區的衝突給這裡帶來和平關鍵是我們要透過更多地關注當地的非暴力領袖來把非暴力行動轉變為一種功能性行為	i believe that the key to solving conflict in the middle east is to bring peace to this , and we need to focus more on local nonviolent leaders to transform nonviolent action into a functional behavior .
在約旦河西岸加沙地帶以及東耶路撒冷地區拍攝那裡的村莊時我親眼目睹了區區一部紀錄片對行為轉變所帶來的影響	in the west banks of jordan and in the villages of east jerusalem , i saw firsthand the impact of a documentary film on the transformation of behavior .
在離耶路撒冷很近的一個名叫瓦拉傑的村子那裡的村民面臨著與佈德魯斯相似的困境	in a village near jerusalem called varajeger , where the villagers face a plight similar to bradrus .
他們即將被包圍起來失去大片土地無法自由進入約旦河西岸或耶路撒冷	they're going to be surrounded , lose big patches of land , no freedom of access to the west bank or jerusalem .
在進行了長達兩年的非暴力抵抗之後他們最終心灰意冷因為他們沒有得到任何人的注意	after two years of nonviolent resistance , they eventually frustrated because they didn't get anybody's attention .
於是我們在那裡組織播放了紀錄片	so we showed the documentary film there .
一週之後他們組織了一場在當時參與人數最多最有紀律的遊行示威	a week later , they organized the most disciplined protest to participate at the time .
組織者們說當村民在紀錄片中看到佈德魯斯的故事他們感覺到確實有人與他們志同道合人們是在乎的	the organizers told us that when the villagers saw bedrus in the documentary , they felt that there was someone who really cared about it with them .
於是他們沒有放棄	so they didn't give up .
以色列有一個新的和平運動被稱為 " 索裡德拉爾特 " 在希伯來語中意為 " 團結一致 "	israel has a new peace movement called solidarity , which means " unity " in hebrew .
佈德魯斯的故事成為了這個運動的領導者招兵買馬的主要手段之一	the story of budrus became one of the leaders of the movement recruiting soldiers to buy horses .
他們反映說那些從未加入任何運動的以色列人看了紀錄片之後瞭解了非暴力抵抗的力量並開始加入他們行動	they reflected that israelis who had never joined any movement had seen a documentary , understood the power of nonviolent resistance and started joining them in action .
瓦拉傑和索裡德拉爾特運動的例子告訴我們即使是小成本的獨立電影也能夠幫助非暴力抵抗轉變為一種功能性行為	varajeger and solidart's campaign have shown us that even a smallscale independent film can help nonviolent resistance to a functional behavior .
想象一下主流媒體若是開始報道每週在貝拉因尼亞林瓦拉傑等村莊以及耶路撒冷境內的香克哈拉和西路萬巴勒斯坦居住區裡發生的非暴力示威活動這將產生多麼巨大的力量更多的人會關注非暴力運動領導者重視他們讓他們的工作更有成效	imagine the mainstream media , if you start reporting about villages like liniavaraj in bella , in jerusalem , and the nonviolent demonstrations that are happening in the neighborhood in okhara , palestine's neighborhood , this is going to be so powerful that people will pay attention to nonviolent leaders and make their work more effective .
我相信最重要的是我們要認識到如果我們不關注這些運動它們就是隱形的彷彿從來沒有發生過	i believe the most important thing to realize is that if we don't pay attention to these movements , they're invisible as if they've never happened .
但我以親身經歷為證如果我們關注這些運動就會得到發展	but i'm a testimony as a personal experience , and if we look at these movements , we're going to be achieved .
它們一旦發展其影響力就會遍及巴以衝突	and when they develop their influence , they're all over the palestinian conflict .
這種影響能夠最終將衝突化解	this ultimately resolves conflict .
這些領導者證明了非暴力運動在佈德魯斯這樣的地方是可行的	these leaders have shown that nonviolent movements work in places like dress .
我們一起來關注他們讓他們證明這在任何地方都是可行的	let's look at them , and let them show that it works anywhere .
西蒙•斯涅克用一個簡單但是震撼的模型來闡釋激勵人心的領袖力 , 這個模型的核心是一個 " 黃金 " 圓圈 , 意思是領袖素質的根本來源是回答 " 為什麼 ? " 。 他列舉了蘋果公司、馬丁•路德•金還有萊特兄弟成功的例子 , 同時以蒂沃數碼錄影機為失敗的典型 。 雖然蒂沃最近打贏一場官司 , 使得其股價上漲了3倍 , 但是它仍在掙扎中 。	simone snoneck illustrates the inspirational leadership in the heart of this model , a golden circle , meaning the fundamental source of leadership quality is " why ? " he listed apple , martin luther king and wright brothers successfully losing the typical typical of a digital video camera that recently won a threefold struggle .
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bull seye , for example , entrepreneur muine , sales , selling success .
西蒙•斯涅克:偉大的領袖如何激勵行動	simone snonek: how great leaders inspire movement .
當事情的發展出乎意料之外的時候 , 你怎麼解釋 ?	how do you explain when things are developing unexpectedly ?
換句話說 , 當別人似乎出乎意料地取得成功的時候 , 你怎麼解釋 ?	in other words , how do you explain when someone seems to be successful in an unexpected way ?
比如說 , 為什麼蘋果公司創新能力這麼強 ?	for example , why is apple so innovative ?
這麼多年來 , 年復一年 , 他們比所有競爭對手都更加具有創新性 。	for years , year after year , they were more innovative than all their competitors .
而其實他們只是一家電腦公司 。	and they're actually just a computer company .
他們跟其他公司沒有任何分別 ,	they have nothing to do with the other companies .
有同樣的途徑 , 接觸到同樣的人才 , 同樣的代理商 , 顧問 , 和媒體 。	there are the same pathways , exposure to the same talents , the same agents , the consultants , the media .
那為什麼他們就似乎有那麼一點不同尋常呢 ?	so why do they seem to be so remarkable ?
同樣的 , 為什麼是由馬丁•路德•金來領導民權運動 ?	similarly , why is it that martin luther king leads the civil rights movement ?
那個時候在美國 , 民權運動之前 , 不僅僅只有他一個人飽受歧視 。 他也決不是那個時代唯一的偉大演說家 。	at that time , before the civil rights movement , not only did he suffer discrimination , but he wasn't the only great orator of the time .
又為什麼懷特兄弟能夠造出動力控制的載人飛機 , 跟他們相比 , 當時的其他團隊似乎更有能力 , 更有資金 ,	and why is it that the white brothers were able to make a driver's plane , compared to them , that other teams at the time seemed to have more capacity , more funding ?
他們卻沒能製造出載人飛機 , 懷特兄弟打敗了他們 。	they didn't make a carrier airplane , and the white brothers beat them .
一定還有一些什麼別的因素在起作用 。	there must be something else that works .
大概三年半之前 , 我有了個新發現 ,	about three and a half years ago , i made a discovery .
這個發現完全改變了我對這個世界如何運作的看法 。 甚至從根本上改變了我的工作生活方式 。	this discovery completely changed my view of how the world worked , and even fundamentally changed the way i work .
那就是我發現了一種模式 ,	and that's how i discovered a pattern .
我發現世界上所有偉大的令人振奮的領袖和組織 , 無論是蘋果公司、馬丁•路德•金還是懷特兄弟 , 他們思考、行動、交流溝通的方式都完全一樣 ,	i find that all the great leaders and organizations in the world , whether it's apples or martin luther king or white brothers , they think , act , communicate , exactly the same way .
但是跟所有其他人的方式完全相反 。	but the opposite is true of everybody else .
我所做的僅僅是把它整理出來 。 這可能是世上最簡單的概念 。	all i'm doing is organizing it . it's probably the simplest concept in the world .
我稱它為黃金圓環 。	i call it the golden circle .
為什麼 ? 怎麼做 ? 是什麼 ?	why ? how ? what ?
這小小的模型就解釋了為什麼一些組織和領導者能夠在別人不能的地方激發出靈感和潛力 。	this little model explains why some organizations and leaders can inspire and potential where others cannot .
我來儘快地解釋一下這些術語 。	i'm going to explain these terms very quickly .
地球上的每個人 , 每個組織都明白自己做的是什麼 , 百分之百 。	everyone on this planet , every organization , understood what they were doing , 100 percent .
其中一些知道該怎麼做 , 你可以稱之為是你的差異價值 , 或是你的獨特工藝 , 或是你的獨特賣點也好 , 怎麼說都行 。	some of them know what to do , and you can call it your differences , or your unique craft , or your unique tradeoffs , or your unique selling points , or whatever .
但是非常 , 非常少的人和組織明白為什麼做 。	but very , very few people and organizations understand why .
這裡的 " 為什麼 " 和 " 為利潤 " 沒有關係 ,	there's nothing to do with why " for " profit . "
利潤只是一個結果 , 永遠只能是一個結果 。	profits are just one result , always one result .
我說的 " 為什麼 " 指的是:你的目的是什麼 ?	what i mean by " why " is: what is your purpose ?
你這樣做的原因是什麼 ? 你懷著什麼樣的信念 ?	what's the reason you do that ? what kind of beliefs do you hold ?
你的機構為什麼而存在 ?	why does your institution exist ?
你每天早上是為什麼而起床 ?	why did you get up every morning ?
為什麼別人要在乎你 ?	why should anyone care ?
結果是 , 我們思考的方式 , 行動的方式 , 交流的方式都是由外向內的 。	it turns out that the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is by extroverts .
很顯然的 , 我們所採用的方式是從清晰開始 , 然後到模糊的東西 。	apparently , what we're doing is starting with clarity and then blurry stuff .
但是激勵型領袖以及組織機構 , 無論他們的規模大小 , 所在領域 , 他們思考 , 行動和交流的方式都是從裡向外的 。	but inspiration leaders and organizations , no matter what size they are , they think , move and communicate from the inside out .
舉個例子吧 。	let's take an example .
我舉蘋果公司是因為這個例子簡單易懂 , 每個人都能理解 。	i'll give you an apple because it's a simple example , everybody understands it .
如果蘋果公司跟其他公司一樣 , 他們的市場營銷資訊就會是這個樣子: " 我們做最棒的電腦 ,	if apple had the same marketing information as any other company , it would have looked like this: " we make the best computers .
設計精美 , 使用簡單 , 介面友好 。	design beauty , with simplicity , with interfaces .
你想買一臺嗎 ? " 不怎麼樣吧 。	do you want to buy one ? "
這就是我們大多數人的交流方式 ,	this is how most of us communicate .
也是大多數市場推廣的方式 , 大部分銷售所採用的方式 , 也是我們大部分人互相交流的方式 。	it's also the way most markets push , most of the sales are adopted , and it's the way most of us interact with each other .
我們說我們的職業是幹什麼的 , 我們說我們是如何的與眾不同 , 或者我們怎麼比其他人更好 , 然後我們就期待著一些別人的反應 , 比如購買 , 比如投票 , 諸如此類 。	we say what our profession does , we say how we're different or how we're better than others , and then we expect other people's reactions , like purchasing , like voting , and so on .
這是我們新開的的律師事務所 , 我們擁有最棒的律師和最大的客戶 , 我們總是能滿足客戶的要求 。	this is our newly open law firm , and we have the best lawyers and the biggest clients , and we can always meet our clients' requests .
這是我們的新車型 , 非常省油 , 真皮座椅 。 買一輛吧 。	this is our new carshaped , very fuelefficient , dermatical seat . buy one .
這是蘋果公司實際上的溝通方式:	this is how apple actually communicates .
" 我們做的每一件事情 , 都是為了突破和創新 。	" everything we do is for breakthroughs and innovation .
我們堅信應該以不同的方式思考 。	we believe that we should think differently .
我們挑戰現狀的方式是透過把我們的產品設計得十分精美 , 使用簡單 , 和介面友好 。	the way we challenge the status quo is by designing our products very beautifully , using simplicity and interface friendly .
我們只是在這個過程中做出了最棒的電腦 。	we're just making the best computers in the process .
想買一臺嗎 ? "	would you like to buy one ? "
感覺完全不一樣 , 對吧 ? 你已經準備從我這裡買一臺了 。	it feels completely different , right ? you're ready to buy one from me .
我所做的只是將傳遞資訊的順序顛倒一下而已 。	all i've done is turn upside down the order of the information transmits .
事實已經向我們證明 , 人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念和宗旨 。	it's been shown to us that people don't buy products you make , people buy your beliefs and missions .
人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念 。	people don't buy products you make , they buy your beliefs .
這就解釋了為什麼這裡的每個人從蘋果公司買電腦時都覺得理所當然 。	this explains why everyone here takes it for granted when they buy a computer from an apple .
但是我們從蘋果公司買mp3播放器 , 手機 , 或者數碼攝像機時 , 也感覺很舒服 。	but when we buy mp3 players from apple , mobile phones , or digital cameras , it feels very comfortable .
而其實 , 我剛才已經說過 , 蘋果公司只是個電腦公司 。	and actually , as i said earlier , apple is a computer company .
沒有什麼能從結構上將蘋果公司同競爭對手區分開來 。	there's nothing to separate apple from structural competition .
競爭對手和蘋果公司有同樣的能力製造所有這些產品 。	competitors and apple have the same capacity to make all of these products .
實際上 , 他們也嘗試過 。	in fact , they tried .
幾年前 , 捷威公司推出了平板電視 。	a few years ago , the czech industry introduced flat tv .
他們製造平板電視的能力很強 ,	they're very capable of making flatscreen television .
因為他們做平板顯示器已經很多年了 。	because they've been working on a tablet display for years .
戴爾公司推出了mp3播放器和掌上電腦 , 他們產品的質量非常好 , 產品的設計也非常不錯 。 但是也沒有人買他們的這些產品 。	the company darre launched an mp3 player and a paddle computer , whose quality of their products was very good designed , and nobody bought them .
其實 , 說到這裡 , 我們無法想象會從戴爾公司買mp3播放器 。	actually , speaking of this , we couldn't imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .
你為什麼會從一家電腦公司買mp3播放器呢 ?	why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?
但是每天我們都這麼做 。	but we do it every day .
人們買的不是你做的產品 , 人們買的是你的信念 。	people don't buy products you make , they buy your beliefs .
做公司的目標不是要跟所有需要你的產品的人做生意 ,	the goal of the company is not to do business with everybody who needs your product .
而是跟與你有著相同理念的人做生意 。	it's a business with people who have the same ideas .
這是最精彩的部分 。 我說的這些沒有一個是我自己的觀點 。	that's the most amazing part . none of the things i'm talking about are my own perspective .
這些觀點都能從生物學裡面找到根源 。	all of these views can be found in biology .
不是心理學 , 是生物學 。	not psychology , but biology .
當你俯視看大腦的橫截面 , 你會發現人類大腦實際上分成三個主要部分 , 而這三個主要部分和黃金圓環匹配得非常好 。	when you look at the crosssection of the brain , you can see that the human brain is actually divided into three key parts , and those three main components are perfectly matched with golden circles
我們最新的腦部 , 管轄智力的腦部 , 或者說我們的大腦皮層 , 對應著 " 是什麼 " 這個圓環 。	our latest brain , our jurisdictional brain , or our cerebral cortex , corresponds to this circle .
大腦皮層負責我們所有的理性和邏輯的思考和語言功能 。	the cortex is responsible for all our rational and logical thinking and language function .
中間的兩個部分是我們的兩個邊腦 。 邊腦負責我們所有的情感 , 比如信任和忠誠 ,	the two parts in the middle are our brains , and the brain is responsible for all of our emotions , like trust and loyalty .
也負責所有的行為和決策 , 但這部分沒有語言功能 。	it's also responsible for all behaviors and decisionmaking , but this part doesn't have linguistic functions .
換句話說 , 當我們由外向內交流時 , 沒錯 , 人們可以理解大量的複雜資訊 , 比如特徵 , 優點 , 事實和圖表 。	in other words , when we communicate from extroverts , yes , people can understand a lot of complex information , like features , strength , facts and graphs .
但不足以激發行動 。	but it's not enough to inspire action .
當我們由內向外交流時 , 我們是在直接同控制行為的那一部分大腦對話 , 然後我們由人們理性地思考我們所說和做的事情 。	when we're diplomacying from the introverts , we're directly controlling part of the brain's behavior , and then we're rationally thinking about what we're talking about and doing .
這就是那些發自內心的決定的來源 。	and that's where those decisions come from .
你知道 , 有時候你展示給一些人所有的資料圖表 , 他們會說 " 我知道這些資料和圖表是什麼意思 , 但就是感覺不對 。 "	you know , sometimes you show people all the data graphs , and they say , " i know what the data and the graph means , but it just doesn't feel right . "
為什麼我們會用這個動詞 , " 感覺 " 不對 ?	why do we use that verb , " feeling " ?
因為控制決策的那一部分大腦並不支配語言 ,	because part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't dominate language .
我們只好說 " 我不知道為什麼 , 就是感覺不對 。 "	we just said , " i don't know why , it just doesn't feel right . "
或者有些時候 , 你說聽從心的召喚 , 或者說聽從靈魂 。	or sometimes you're listening to the call , or you're listening to the soul .
我不想把這些觀念分解得太徹底 , 但心和靈魂都不是控制行為的部分 。	i don't want to break these ideas down too thoroughly , but the heart and the soul are not the parts that control behavior .
所有這一切都發生在你的邊腦 , 控制決策行為而非語言的邊腦 。	all of this happens in your head , controlling decisionmaking behavior rather than linguistic brains .
如果你自己都不知道你為什麼幹你所做的事情 , 而別人要對你的動機作出反應 , 那麼你怎麼可能贏得大家對你的支援 , 從你這裡購買東西 , 或者 , 更重要的 , 對你忠誠並且想成為你正在做的事情的一分子呢 ?	if you don't know why you're doing what you're doing , and people are responding to your motivations , then how can you possibly win people's support from you , buying things from you , or , more importantly , loyal to you and want to be part of what you're doing ?
再說一次 , 目標不僅僅是將你有的東西賣給需要它們的人 ; 而是將東西賣給跟你有共同信念的人 。	and again , the goal is not just to sell things that you have to people that need them ; it's to sell them to people that share a common belief with you .
目標不僅僅是僱傭那些需要一份工作的人 ; 目標是僱傭那些同你有共同信念的人 。	the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; the goal is to employ people who share a common belief .
你知道嗎 , 我總是說 , 如果你僱傭某人只是因為他能做這份工作 , 他們就只是為你開的工資而工作 , 但是如果你僱傭跟你有共同信念的人 , 他們會為你付出熱血 , 汗水和淚水 。	you know , i always say , if you hire someone just to do this job , they're just going to work for you salary , but if you employ someone with you , they'll pay you hot blood , sweat and tears .
這一點 , 沒有比懷特兄弟的故事更恰當的例子了 。	now , no more appropriate example than the white brothers' stories .
大多數人都沒聽說過塞繆爾•蘭利這個人 。	most of you have never heard of this guy , samuel lanley .
20世紀初期 , 投入機動飛行器的熱情就像當今的網站熱 ,	in the early 20th century , the passion to invest in motorized aircraft was like the current website .
每個人都在做嘗試 。	everybody's trying .
塞繆爾•蘭利擁有所有大家認為是成功的要素 。	samuel lanley has all the elements of success .
我的意思是 , 即便是現在 , 你問別人 " 為什麼你的產品或者公司失敗了呢 ? "	i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or your company fail ? "
人們總是用同樣的三個東西以同樣的排列順序來回答你 , 缺乏資金 , 用人不善 , 形勢不好 。	people are always answering you in the same sequence as three things: lack of funding , bad people , bad posture .
總是那三種理由 , 所以讓我們來逐個分析一下 。	it's always those three reasons , so let's go through each analysis .
國防部給了塞繆爾•蘭利5萬美金作為研製飛行器的資金 。	the department of defense funded samuel lanley 50 , 000 dollars as a research robot .
所以說 , 資金不是問題 。	so funding is not a problem .
他在哈佛大學工作過 , 也在史密森尼學會工作過 , 人脈極其廣泛 。 他認識當時最優秀的人才 。	he worked at harvard university , and he worked at the smithsonian society , incredibly widespread , and he knew the best people at the time .
因此 , 他僱傭了用資金能吸引到的最優秀的人才 。 當時的市場形勢相當有利 。	so he hired domesticated talent with the best people he could attract , and the market conditions were quite profitable .
紐約時報對他做跟蹤報道 , 每個人都支援他 。	the new york times did a track record on him , and everyone supported him .
但是為什麼你們連聽都沒聽說過他呢 ?	but why haven't you even heard of him ?
與此同時 , 幾百公里之外的俄亥俄州代頓市有一對兄弟 , 奧維爾•萊特和維爾伯•萊特 , 他們倆沒有任何我們認為的成功的要素 。	meanwhile , hundreds of kilometers away in subton , ohio , orville wright and virgin wright , together with no elements of success .
他們沒有錢 。 他們用腳踏車店的收入來追求他們的夢想 。 萊特兄弟的團隊中沒有一個人上過大學 , 就連奧維爾和維爾伯也沒有 。 紐約時報更是不沾邊的 。	they didn't have money . they used the income of a bicycle shop to pursue their dreams . none of the wright brothers' team had gone to university , even oville and virgin . the new york times was more impressive .
不同的是 , 奧維爾和維爾伯追求的是一個事業 , 一個目標 , 一種信念 。	the difference is that what orville and vibel pursued was a career , a goal , a belief .
他們相信如果他們能研製出飛行器 , 將會改變全世界的發展程序 。	they believed that if they could build a robot , it would change the course of development around the world .
塞繆爾•蘭利就不同了 ,	samuel langley was different .
他想要發財 , 他想要成名 。	he wanted to give money , he wanted to be famous .
他追求的是最終結果 ,	he was looking for the end result .
是變得富有 。	it's becoming rich .
看吧 , 看接下來怎麼樣了 。	see , look what happens .
那些懷有和懷特兄弟一樣夢想的人跟他們一起熱血朝天地奮鬥著 。	those who had the same dreams as the white brothers struggled with them towards the heavens .
另一邊的人則是為了工資而工作 。	people on the other side are working for salary .
後來流傳的故事說 , 每次懷特兄弟出去實驗時 , 都必須帶著五組零件 , 因為那是在他們回來吃晚飯之前將要墜毀的次數 。	and the story goes on to tell me that every time the white brothers go out and experiment , they have to carry five pieces , because that's how many times they're going to crash before they come back to dinner .
最後 , 在1903年12月17日 , 懷特兄弟成功起飛 , 但是當時沒有任何其他人在場目睹 。	finally , on december 17 , 1903 , the white brothers took off , but nobody else was watching .
我們是在幾天後才知道的 。	we didn't know it until a few days later .
後來的事情進一步證實了蘭利動機不純 , 他在懷特兄弟成功的當天就辭職了 。	later things confirmed langley's innocence , and he quit the day the white brothers did successfully .
他本來應該可以說: " 夥計們 , 這真是一項偉大的發明 , 我可以改進你們的技術 。 " 但是他沒有 ,	he was supposed to be able to say , " guys , this is a great invention , and i can improve your technology . "
因為他不是第一個製造出飛機的人 , 他就不會變得富有 , 他也不會變得有名 , 所以他辭職了 。	because he wasn't the first person to make an airplane , he wouldn't be rich , and he wouldn't become famous , so he quit .
人們買的不是你的產品 ; 而是你的信念 。	it's not your product ; it's your belief .
如果你講述你的信念 , 你將吸引那些跟你擁有同樣信念的人 。	if you talk about your beliefs , you're going to attract people who share your beliefs .
但是為什麼吸引那些跟你擁有同樣信念的人非常重要呢 ?	but why is it so important to attract those who share the same beliefs ?
創新的傳播有一個規律 , 如果你不知道這個規律 , 你一定了解這個概念 。	there's a pattern for innovation , and if you don't know the pattern , you've got this idea .
我們的社會中 , 有2.5%的人是革新者 。	2 . 5 percent of our society is innovators .
13.5%的人是早期的少部分採納者 。	13 . 5 percent of people were early adopters .
接下來的34%是早期接受的大多數 , 然後是比較晚接受的大多數和最後行動的 。	the next 34 percent are most early acceptance , then most and last acts later .
這部分最後行動的人買按鍵電話的唯一原因是因為他們再也買不到轉盤電話了 。	the only reason that these guys ended up buying a call is because they couldn't buy a call anymore .
雖然我們在不同的時候會處在這個曲線上不同的位置 , 但是創新的傳播規律告訴我們如果你想在大眾市場上獲得成功 , 或者要大眾接納一個點子 , 你得等到獲得15%-18%的市場接受度這個轉折點之後才行 。 那時之後市場才真正開啟 。	although we're different at different times at different places on this curve , innovation is telling us that if you want to be successful in the public market , or you have to have an idea , you have to wait until you get 15 to 18 percent of the market receives that twist , and that's when markets really open .
我喜歡問公司: " 你的新生意怎麼樣呀 ? "	i like to ask companies , " what's your new business ? "
他們會很自豪地告訴你 " 哦 , 大概有10%吧 。 "	they're going to be proud to tell you , " oh , about 10 percent . "
是呀 , 你有可能就在10%的顧客群這裡過不去了 。	yeah , you're likely to be here in 10 percent of the customers .
我們都能讓10%的人 " 意會 " ,	we can all get 10 percent of the people .
對 , 我們一般這樣形容他們 。	yeah , we normally describe them this way .
就好比描述那種感覺: " 哦 , 他們有點心領神會了 " 。	it's like describing that feeling , " oh , they're kind of taking care of god . "
問題是:你怎麼在他們還沒有成為你的顧客之前就發現那些能意會的人 , 和那些不能意會的人 ?	the question is: how do you find people who will intentionally meet before they have become your customers ?
這就是問題的所在 , 就是這點間隙 , 你得把這個間隙給填上 , 正如傑弗裡穆爾所說的 , " 跨越鴻溝 " 。 因為早期的大多數不會嘗試新事物 , 除非有些人已經先嚐試過了 。	that's the problem , and that's the point where you have to fill this gap , as jeffrey moore said , " cross the gap , " because the early majority won't try something new unless some people have tried it first .
而這些人 , 創新者和早期的少數人 , 他們喜歡大膽的嘗試 。	and these guys , the innovators and the early few , they love the bold try .
他們更自然地憑直覺做事情 , 發自於他們的世界觀的直覺 , 而不僅僅是因為市場上有什麼樣的產品 。	they naturally do things intuitively , from their worldviews' intuitions , not just because of what products on the market .
這是一批在iphone上市的頭幾天去排隊等六個小時來購買的人 , 而其實只要等一個星期你就可以隨便走進店裡從貨架上買到 。	this is the first time a group of people came out on the iphone in line for six hours , and in fact , waiting for one week you can go to the store and buy it from the shelves .
這是一批在平板電視剛推出時會花4萬美金買一臺的人 , 儘管當時的技術還不成熟 。	this is a batch of 40 , 000 dollars spent on a flatscreen television , although the technologies didn't mature at the time .
補充說一下 , 他們並不是因為技術的先進而買那些產品 , 而是為了他們自己 。	and in addition , they're not buying those products because of technological advances , but for themselves .
因為他們想成為第一個體驗新產品的人 。	because they want to be the first person to experience a new product .
人們買的不是你的產品 ; 人們買的是你的信念 。 你的行動只是證明了你的信念 。	people don't buy your product ; people buy your beliefs ; your actions just prove your beliefs .
實際上 , 人們會去做能夠體現他們的信念的事情 。	in fact , people are doing things that reflect beliefs .
那些為了搶先在頭六個小時內買到iphone而排六個小時的隊的人 , 是出於他們的世界觀 , 出於他們想別人怎麼看自己 。 他們是第一批體驗者 。	the teams who were scheduling six hours in the first six hours were their worldviews , out of what they wanted other people to see themselves . they were the first group of experiencers .
人們買的不是你的產品 ; 他們買的是你的信念 。	people don't buy your product ; they buy your beliefs .
我再舉些著名的例子吧 , 證實創新傳播規律的一個失敗的例子和一個成功的例子 。	let me give you some famous examples of a failure of innovation in spreading patterns and a success story .
首先我們講這個失敗的例子 。	let's start with the failure example .
還是商業上的 。	it's a business .
就如我們一秒鐘前剛剛說過的 , 成功的要素是充足的資金 , 優秀的人才和良好的市場形勢 。 那麼 , 是不是如果有這些你就應該獲得成功 。	as we've just mentioned a second ago , the element of success is adequate funding , great talent and good markets . so , if you have those , you should be successful .
自從推出蒂沃機頂盒以來 , 大概是八、九年前 , 直到今天 , 它們一直是市場上唯一的最高品質的產品 , 這沒有任何異議 。	it's been about eight or nine years since the launch of the summit of the tivol machine box , until today , they've been the only highest quality product on the market , and there's no difference .
它們絕對是資金充足 ,	they're absolutely sufficient .
市場形勢也大好 。	markets are great .
其實 , " 蒂沃 " 都變成了一個日常用的動詞 。	in fact , " tiv " became a daily verb .
比如:我經常把東西蒂沃到我那臺華納數碼影片錄影機裡面 。	for instance: i've kept things up in my waltner digital video camera all the time .
但是蒂沃是個商業上的失敗案例 ,	but tivel was a commercial failure .
他們沒有賺到一分錢 。	they didn't make a penny .
他們上市時 , 股票價格大約在30到40美元 , 然後就直線下跌 , 而成交價格從沒超過10美元 。	when they came out , the price of the stock price was between 30 and 40 dollars , and then it went straight , and the cost was never over 10 dollars .
實際上 , 我印象中它的交易價格從來沒有超過6美元 , 除了幾次小的震盪之外 。	in fact , its price of transactions in my impression was never over six dollars , except for a few small concussions .
因為你會發現 , 蒂沃公司新推出他們的產品時 , 他們只是告訴我們他們產品是什麼 ,	because you'll notice that when the company launched their product , they just told us what their product was .
他們說 " 我們的產品可以把電視節目暫停 , 跳過廣告 , 回放電視節目 , 還能記住你的觀看習慣 , 你甚至都不用刻意設定它 。 "	they said , " our product can pause the television show , skip ads , release television , and remember your habits , and you don't even have to set it up . "
挑剔的人們說: " 我們不相信你 ,	choosy people say , " we don't trust you .
我們不需要這樣的東西 , 我們也不喜歡這樣的東西 。	we don't need something like this , and we don't like it either .
你在唬人 。 "	you're bluffing people . "
假如他們這麼說: " 如果你想掌控生活的方方面面 , 朋友 , 那麼就試試我們的產品吧 。	if they said , " if you want to take control of life , friends , let's try our product .
它可以暫停直播節目 , 跳過廣告 , 回放直播節目 , 還能記下你的觀看習慣 , 等等 。	it pauses livestreaming , skipping ads , going back to livestream , and remembering your habits , and so on .
人們買的不是你的產品 ; 人們買的是你的信念 。 你所做的僅僅只是你的信念的證明而已 。	people don't buy your product ; people buy your beliefs . all you do is prove your beliefs .
下面我給大家介紹一個成功的例子 。	i'm going to give you a success story .
1963年的夏天 , 25萬人聚集在華盛頓特區聆聽馬丁•路德•金博士的演講 。	in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people gathered in washington , d . c . to listen to dr . martin luther king .
那時 , 既沒有發請帖 , 也沒有可能在網上檢視日期 。	there was no review , no possibility of looking at the date online .
怎麼會有25萬人參加呢 ?	how do you get 250 , 000 people involved ?
而且 , 金博士不是美國唯一的偉大演說家 ,	and dr . king wasn't the only great american orator .
也不是美國唯一一位在民權法案實施前遭受歧視的人 。	it's not the only person in the united states who suffered discrimination before the civil rights act .
實際上 , 他的一些想法甚至不正確 。	in fact , some of his ideas weren't even true .
但是他有個天賦 。	but he had a gift .
他沒有到處宣揚美國需要改變什麼方面 ,	he wasn't advocating everywhere that america needed to change .
他只是到處告訴別人他所相信的 。	he just went around telling people what he believed .
" 我相信 。 我相信 。 我相信 。 " 他總是這麼跟別人說 。	" i believe . i believe . " he said to people all the time .
而那些和他懷有同樣信念的人受了他的啟發 , 他們也開始將自己的信念告訴別人 。	and he was inspired by the people he had the same beliefs , and they began to tell people about their beliefs .
有些人建立起一些組織機構將這些話傳給更多的人 。	some people have created organizations that are sending these words to more people .
你看 , 就這樣 , 25萬人在那天 , 那個時候 , 聚集在一起聽他演講 。	you see , that's it , 250 , 000 people were there , and at that time , they were all together and they were listening to him .
有多少人是為了聽 " 他 " 演說而去的呢 ?	how many people did it for his talk ?
他們是為了他們自己而去的 。	they were there for themselves .
那是他們對於美國的信念支援著他們坐8個小時的公車 , 站在華盛頓八月中旬的烈日下 。	it was their faith in the united states that supported them in eight hours of buses stood in the middle of august , washington .
是他們所相信的信念 , 而不是黑人跟白人之間的鬥爭 。 25%的聽眾是白人 。	it's the belief that they believe , not the struggle between black and white , 25 percent of the audience is white .
金博士相信世界上有兩種律法 , 一種是上天制定的 , 一種是世人制定的 。	dr . king believed there were two laws in the world , one made by god , one made by the world .
直到世人制定的法律和上天制定的律法相符合 , 我們才真正生活在公正的世界裡 。	it wasn't until the laws that had been created that fit together with the laws that had been made up of the day that we really lived in a world of justice .
民權運動只是碰巧幫他將信念付諸於現實的一件事情 。	the civil rights movement accidentally helped him to put belief into reality .
我們跟隨他 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。	we followed him , not for him , but for ourselves .
順便說一下 , 他的演講是 " 我有一個夢想 " , 而不是 " 我有一個方案 " 。	by the way , his talk is " i have a dream " speech , not " i have a solution . "
聽聽現在的政治家們提出的12點的大雜燴計劃 ,	listen to the 12point politicians that are proposing .
沒一點勁 。	nothing .
一些人是當官的 , 而另一些人是領袖 。	some people are official , and others are leaders .
當官的只是佔據在有權力和威嚴的位置上 , 但是隻有具有領袖素質的人才能激勵我們 。	it's only occupying the position of power and strictness , but it's the person with leadership quality that motivates us .
無論他們是個人還是組織 , 我們都追隨領袖 , 不是因為我們必須這樣做 , 而是因為我們願意 。	whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow leaders , not because we have to , but because we want to .
我們跟隨具有領袖能力的人 , 不是為他們 , 而是為我們自己 。	we follow people with leadership , not for them , but for ourselves .
也只有那些從 " 為什麼 " 這個圓圈出發的人才有能力激勵周圍的人 , 或者找到能夠激勵他們的人 。	it's the people who come from the " why " circle have the ability to motivate those around , or find people who can motivate them .
你是如何回憶起將車停在了什麼地方呢 ? 你怎麼判斷自己是否走對了方向呢 ? 神經系統科學家尼爾•伯吉斯研究了神經系統的定位功能原理 , 以及該原理與記憶和想象的關係 。	how do you recall what parking is , how do you determine whether you're going in the right direction , and neil berggis , who studied the positioning function of the nervous system , and the relationship between the principle and the memory and the imagination ?
brain , cognitivescience , exploration , neuroscience , science	that's cognitivescience .
尼爾•伯吉斯:大腦是怎樣幫我們定位的	ng: how does the brain work for us ?
當我們在大型停車場停車後 , 如何回憶起將車停在了哪個車位呢 ?	how do we recall where the cars are parked after a large parking lot ?
這就是現在困擾荷馬的問題 。	that's the problem now with homers .
接下來我們將嘗試瞭解此時他腦中正開展何種 " 運動 " 。	and then we're going to try and figure out what kind of exercise he's developing in his head right now .
我們先著眼於大腦海馬區 , 即黃色的區域這是我們的記憶器官 。	we looked at the hippocampus , the yellow area , and this is our memory organ .
如果海馬區出現損傷 , 像老年痴呆症患者一樣 , 你將喪失記憶力 , 乃至記不起將車停在了何處 。	if the hippocampus is injured , like the alzheimer's patient , you're going to lose memory , and you can't remember where the car is .
hippocampus這個詞源自拉丁語 , 有 " 海馬 " 之意因為腦中海馬區的形狀看上去有點像 " 海馬 " 。	the hippocampus is a word from latin , which means " hippocampus " because the shape of the hippocampus looks a little bit like " hippocampus . "
海馬區和大腦其它區域的組成相似 , 都由神經元構成 。	the hippocampus is similar to the rest of the brain , all made up of neurons .
人的大腦由大約一千億個神經元細胞組成 。	the human brain is made up of about 100 billion neurons .
每個神經元細胞之間透過一些連線中介互相傳送小的電脈衝或者尖峰電壓來進行 " 交流 " 。	each of these neurons communicates through some of the connections between them , or little electrical pulses or peak communication .
海馬區由兩層片狀的細胞群構成 , 這兩層細胞群緊密相連 。	the hippocampus is made up of two layers of cells that are intimately connected .
科學家們透過記錄老鼠在某環境中搜羅食物時其腦中單個神經元細胞的反應來了解 " 空間記憶 " 的工作原理與工作機制 。	scientists understand how spatial memory work and job mechanisms work and mechanisms work by recording rats in one environment .
現在想象一下 , 我們正在為這隻老鼠的海馬區中的一個神經元細胞 " 錄影 " 。	now imagine that we're recording a neuron in the hippocampus of this mouse .
每當這個細胞發出小型尖峰電壓 , 隨後會出現一個紅點以及咔噠的一聲 。	every time this cell fires a small peak peak pressure , a red dot and a click sound comes along .
我們可以看出每當老鼠進入環境中某一特定位置 , 這個神經元細胞便會有反應 。	we can see that whenever a mouse enters a certain location in the environment , this neuron will respond .
然後這個細胞再透過小型尖峰電壓將以上資訊傳遞給大腦的其它區域 。	and this cell then transmits information to other parts of the brain through a small peak rush .
這麼一來 , 我們可以憑藉這個細胞傳送訊號的頻率推知老鼠經過的相應位置 。	in this way , we can infer where the rat goes by by by the frequency of this cell .
倘若我們記錄的是很多不同的神經元細胞 , 就會發現當老鼠處於不同的位置上時 , 不同的神經元細胞會產生各自的電訊號 , 正如我們在這些方形中看到的那樣 。	if we document many different neurons , we find that different neurons produce their own electrical signals as we see them in different positions .
這些訊號為大腦中的其它區域勾勒出一張地圖 , 持續地向大腦指示出 , " 我現在位於環境中的哪個具體點上 ? "	these signals are mapped in other parts of the brain , constantly instructing to the brain , " what specific point am i sitting in ? "
我們也記錄人腦中的 " 定位神經元細胞 " 。	we also document " location neurons " in the human brain .
癲癇病患者有時需要監測他們的腦電活動情況 。	epilepsy patients sometimes need to monitor their brain electrical activity .
一些患者玩一種電子遊戲 , 遊戲中他們在一個小鎮上自由開車 。	some patients played a video game where they were driving freely in a town .
然後當他們驅車駛過鎮上的某一處時 , 他們大腦海馬區中的 " 定位神經元細胞 " 便會被啟用 , 發出訊號 。	and then when they drive across town somewhere , their location neurons in the hippocampus will be inspired , sending signals .
那麼這 " 定位細胞 " 是怎麼知道老鼠或人處於某個位置的呢 ?	so how does that position cell know that mice or people are in a position ?
這裡有兩個神經元細胞 , 它們告訴我們 , 在定位時環境的邊界是至關重要的 。	here are two neurons , and they tell us that the boundaries of the environment are essential .
上面的這個細胞傾向於在老鼠向盒子中部走去時產生訊號 。	the cell at the top tends to produce a signal as it travels in the middle of the box .
因此當你將盒子擴大 , 相應的訊號活躍區也隨之擴大 。	so when you expand the box , the signal activity zone expands .
下面的這個喜歡在老鼠緊鄰南面屏障時作出反應 。	this one down here likes to respond when the rat is clenched on the southern barrier .
因此當你在盒中放入另一屏障時 , 不論老鼠在盒中何處 , 只要它的南面有屏障 , 該細胞中的相應位置便會同時產生訊號 。	so when you put another barrier in the box , wherever the mouse is in the box , if it has a screen in the south , the correspondence in the cell will produce a signal at the same time .
這表明瞭解到達邊界比如周邊的建築物等需要的距離和方向對於海馬區的 " 工作 " 而言至關重要 。	it shows that the distance and direction that arrives at the border of buildings like the neighborhood is crucial for jobs in the hippocampus .
而且確實 , 在老鼠蒐羅環境時 , 我們在海馬區的輸入訊號中 , 檢測到能對距環境邊界的特定距離與方向作出精確感應的神經元細胞 。	and indeed , in mice , we input signals in the hippocampus , and we detect specific distances and directions that respond to precise sensing neurons from the border of the environment .
這裡左邊的細胞 , 你可以看出 , 當老鼠向東靠近邊界或屏障時 , 該細胞都會作出反應 , 不論這邊界是一個方盒的邊還是一個圓柱盒的邊甚至是老鼠繞著轉的桌布的垂簾 。	the cells on the left , as you can see , when the mouse approaches the east or the barrier , the cell responds , whether it's a box or a column box or even a rotating tablecloth by the mouse .
而右面的細胞則是在老鼠南面出現邊界時響應 , 不論這邊界是桌布的垂簾還是一堵牆甚至是兩個被隔開的桌子之間的間隙 。	and the cells on the right respond when the border appears on the south side of the mouse , whether it's the tablecloth curtain or whether it's the wall or whether it's the gap between two separated tables .
以上是我們所推測的一種 " 定位細胞 " 給動物定位的方式 。	so that's one way that we've speculated that we position cells to animals .
我們也可檢測 , 人類在簡單環境中 , 是怎樣給諸如這面旗這樣的物體定位的或者乾脆把這物體想成你的車 。	we can also detect how human beings , in a simple environment , position objects like this or just think of this object as your car .
我們先讓人們熟悉一下環境 , 同時記下物體所在的位置 。	let's get people familiar with the environment and remember where the objects are .
接著 , 再讓他們回到那個環境 , 通常他們都能根據記憶準確無誤地標出物體所在的位置 。	and then they return to that environment , usually they're able to tag objects based on memory accurately where they are .
但在一些試驗中 , 我們會改變環境的形狀和尺度 , 正如我們在 " 定位細胞 " 實驗中所做的那樣 。	but in some trials , we're going to change the shape and the scale of the environment , just like we did in the targeted cell experiment .
如此 , 我們可以透過研究實驗者改變環境的形狀和尺度 , 來了解旗幟發生了怎樣的位移	in this way , we can change the shape and scale of the environment by researchers to understand where the flag is shifting .
比如現在你所看到的 , 假設這面旗幟在如圖中小四方形內的 " × " 的位置 , 然後接著你問人們小旗在哪 , 但實際上你已經將總環境的尺度擴大了 , 結果他們所認為的旗所在的位置也相應地向外擴張 , 而這擴張的模式和 " 定位細胞 " 的一模一樣 。	so , for example , what you're seeing now , suppose that flag is expanding in the location of the four squares , and then you ask people where the flag is , but you actually expand the scale of the total environment , and it turns out that the flag is expanding in exactly the same way as the pattern of the position cell .
這就好像你是透過儲存被某一特定位置所激發的 " 定位細胞 " 產生的訊號模式來記憶小旗的位置的 , 接著當你回到那個地點的時候 , 透過四處打量 , 便可以將你當前腦中 " 定位細胞 " 的訊號模式與之前的模式進行匹配 。	it's as if you're storing the signal patterns that are fired by a specific location cell that are inspired by a specific location to match the patterns of where the flag is , and then when you go back to that location , you can match the patterns of the specific cells that you have in your brain around .
這個過程便可讓你回到 " 老地方 " 。	and that allows you to go back to old places .
我們也能透過位移來給自己定位 。	we can also define ourselves by shifting our places .
因此當我們外出時或許是我們停車後下來隨便走走我們可以給自己定位 , 因為我們可以粗略地將自己的運動路線與大體的返回方向進行整合 。	so when we go out and maybe we stop and we can position ourselves , because we can sort of integrate our own sports routinely with our bodies back in .
" 定位細胞 " 也能從一種叫做 " 網狀細胞 " 的細胞那兒獲得此類線路整合的資訊 。	positioning cells can also receive information from a cell called a mesh cell , a combination of these lines .
目前在向海馬區的訊號輸入中又發現了 " 網狀細胞 " , 它們與 " 定位細胞 " 有點類似 。	and what's currently found in the hippocampus is that mesh cells are a little bit like position cells .
隨著老鼠的 " 四處探索 " , 每一個神經元細胞被大量各種位置所激發的訊號組合在一起 , 貫穿整個環境構成一個令人驚歎的規整的三角網格 。	as mice explore , each neuron is assembled by massive locations of signals that run throughout the environment to form an extraordinary triangle grid .
倘若你對一系列 " 網狀細胞 " 進行記錄這裡以不同的顏色區分每一個細胞發出的訊號都能形成網狀 , 遍及整個環境 , 而且每一個細胞的網狀訊號集的位置都與其他細胞有一定偏差 。	if you document a series of mesh cells in different colors , each cell's signal can form a mesh , all the way throughout the environment , and each cell's signal collection has a bias in its position with each other .
因此紅色標註的細胞訊號集合在這個網格上 , 綠色的是這個 , 而藍色的是這個 。	so the signals that are labeled in red are gathered on this grid , and green are this , and blue are this one .
因此綜合來看 , 這就好像老鼠可以在它所到達的環境中建立一個虛擬的位置訊號網這就有點像你在地圖上所看到的經線和緯線 , 只不過要將線替換成 " 三角形 " 。	so in a synthesis , it's like a mice can create a virtual location network in its environment , which is kind of like the lines and latitudes you see on a map , except for replacing the lines with triangles .
當老鼠移動的時候 , 這些電訊號能透過這些細胞傳遞給下一個神經元細胞從而為老鼠定位 , 這樣老鼠就能在運動時知道自己身在何處 。	and as the mouse moves , these electrical signals can pass to the next neuron from these cells so that the mouse can know where they're moving .
那麼人類是否有 " 網狀細胞 " 呢 ?	so , do we have a mesh ?
因為所有的網狀訊號集合體都有相同的對稱軸 , 以及相同的網格朝向 , 這裡以橘紅色標識 , 這就意味著大腦中特定部位的所有網狀細胞的聯網行為的變化應該取決於我們是在向著這六個方向運動還是沿著六個方向之間所夾的某一個方向運動 。	because all the signals collectively have the same axes of symmetry and the same grid fluctuations here in orange red , which means that all the networking behaviors of a particular part of the brain depends on whether we're moving in these six directions or whether we're moving in one direction between six directions .
我們可以為人們做核磁共振掃描 , 與此同時讓他們玩一個小型電子遊戲 , 還是之前所說的那個遊戲 , 然後來看看當時的訊號 。	we can do mri scans for people , and let them play a little video game , or that game , earlier , and see what the signals were .
啊哈沒錯 , 你在人腦中的內嗅皮層上看到了網狀細胞 , 而它們出現的位置和老鼠的網狀細胞在大腦中所出現的位置一樣 。	aha , exactly , you see the net cells in the human brain , and they're located exactly the same location as the cell in a mouse's brain .
現在我們回頭看看荷馬 。	now let's go back to homer .
他可能憑藉與周邊建築以及四周邊界的相對距離和方向來回憶他的車停在哪兒 。	he could recall where his car parked by relative distances and directions with the surrounding borders .
而那將由專門 " 檢測邊界 " 的神經元細胞發出的訊號來執行 。	and that's going to be enforced by a signal from a neuron called specialized boundaries .
他可能也記得自己是怎麼從停車場走出來的 , 而這就有賴於網狀細胞發出訊號了 。	he might also remember how he came out of a parking lot , and that's a signal that's dependent on cyber cells .
這兩種型別的神經元細胞都可以啟用 " 定位細胞 " 。	each of these two different types of neurons can activate a positioning cell .
因此荷馬成功折返的方法便是在走動中尋求與他之前停車時腦中所建立的訊號集樣式最為匹配的一個腦中即時形成的訊號集樣式 。	so the way homer's successful folding returns is by walking around seeking signals from his previous parking specifically matching one of the most immediate signals formed in the brain .
而那就能將他領回 " 老地方 " 了 , 這個過程與最終的目標視物無關不論他的車是否還在那兒他都能找到停車點 。	and that brings him back to the old place , which has nothing to do with the ultimate goal , whether or not his car is still there , he can find the parking spot .
或許車已經被拖走了 ,	maybe the car has been dragged off .
但他仍然知道車原來停在哪 , 因此他會回到原位去取車 。	but he still knew where the car was parked , so he would go back to the original vehicle .
撇開 " 空間記憶力 " 而言 , 倘若我們單獨觀察這種網狀訊號集在整個大腦中的活動情況 , 就會發現這種訊號形式分佈廣泛 , 每當我們需要回憶一些自己過去的經歷時這種網狀的訊號形式就會活躍起來 , 譬如 , 當你試圖回憶上次參加婚禮的情況時	and aside from spatial memory , if we alone observe this signal in activity across the brain , this signal is widely distributed , and every time we need to recall some of the experiences of our past , this form of mesh is activated , like when you're trying to recall the previous wedding .
因此有可能 , 神經元細胞再現空間的功能也參與視覺畫面的呈現這樣當我們試圖回憶一個曾經置身其中的場面時 , 至少可以藉助想象而勾勒出整個場景 。	so it's possible that neurons recreate the function of the space and also the visual representations of this so that when we try to recall a scene where they've been , at least we can reclaim the entire scene by imagining it .
倘若事實果真如此 , 記憶的形成就開始於: " 定位細胞 " 透過這些縝密的連結相互啟用然後 " 邊界感應細胞 " 被再次啟用從而形成我們視點周圍的場景的空間格局 。	if that's true , the formation of the memory begins with the fact that position cells are activated through these carefully interconnected connections , and then the border sensory cells are reactivated again to form the spatial space space scene that we see around us .
網狀細胞可以使視點穿透那個空間 。	the mesh cells can make their perspective through that space .
而另一種 " 方位細胞 " , 我之前沒有提到它 , 它們像指南針一樣 , 都是根據你的朝向來作出反應的 。	and the other digital cell , which i didn't mention earlier , they respond like a compass , based on where you're headed .
它們可以明確你需要在腦中形成哪個方位的影象 , 就拿回憶婚禮情景來說 , 以上過程就能讓你回想起那一切 。	they can specifically image which dimension you need to form in your head , take back the wedding scenario , and remind you of all of those things .
好了 , 以上就是在認知神經科學領域所開闢的新紀元 , 在這個領域中 , 我們開始嘗試從大腦中數以億計的單個神經元細胞的行為出發 , 來了解人類心理活動產生的過程 。 比如人們是如何記憶、想象甚至思考的	all right , so that's the new era in the cognitive neuroscience community , where we're trying to go from the behaving of hundreds of millions of individual neurons in the brain to understand how human psychological activity is produced .
謝謝各位 。	thank you .
想象一個由合作多部門 , 多政府 , 公私力量組成的全球安全 。 這不僅是開放安全支持者的幻想 , 而是jamesstavridis , 北約最高長官的設想 , 他從分享了從現代軍事史的生動瞬間到解釋了為什麼要靠修橋而不是修牆來構築未來安全 。	imagine a global security made up of cooperation , multiple governments , private forces , not just the illusion of opensource supporters , but james stavridis , the tallest officer in north , who shared the moment of the history of modern military to explain why to build a security future on bridges rather than fixing walls .

jamesstavridis:北約的最高長官如何看待全球安全	james stavridis: the highest commissioner of northern journals think about global security .
我將要介紹一些開放式安全性問題 , 因為我們在21世紀已經離安全越來越近了 。	i'm going to show you some opensource security issues , because we're getting closer and closer to safety in the 21st century .
我們先回顧一下20世紀吧 , 然後我們就能瞭解安全這個概念是如何為我們而工作 。	let's go back to the 20th century , and then we can understand how this idea of security works for us .
這裡是verdun , 一個法國的戰場 , 就在北約在比利時總部的北邊 。	this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .
1916年 , 在verdun這個戰場上 , 700000人在300天內被殺了 , 那就是差不多2000人一天 。	in 1916 , on verdun , in this battlefield , 7 , 000 people were killed in 300 days , and that's about 2 , 000 a day .
咱們繼續往前看--20世紀的安全--看到二戰 , 我們看得到在斯大林格勒保衛戰 , 300天內有二百萬人戰死 。	let's keep looking forward 20th century security seeing world war ii , we can see the war in stalingrade , 300 days , 2 million people died .
進入冷戰 , 我們繼續建造圍牆 。	we went into the cold war , and we continued to build the walls .
我們從一戰的壕溝 , 到二戰的馬其頓防線 , 再到冷戰中的鐵幕 , 柏林牆 。	we went from the trenches of world war ii to the macedonian defense line , to the iron curtains of the cold war , the berlin wall .
所以我今天的主題是為了完成 " 安全 " 這個目標 , 我們不建造牆 , 而建造橋 。	so my thesis today is to accomplish this safety goal , we don't build walls and we build bridges .
在歐洲有一個很著名的橋 。	there's a very famous bridge in europe .
它在drina河上 , 是作家ivoandric的一個小說的主題 , 這部小說講述了如何在歐洲和巴爾幹地區最動盪的部分大量的牆被築起 。	it's on the drina river , a novel by the author iivo andric , and it describes some of the most turbulent parts of how to build in europe and the balkans .
而最近 , 也就是在近十年 , 我們開始看到這些地區開始 , 儘管有些猶豫不決 , 逐漸融合在一起 。	and recently , in the last 10 years , we're starting to see these regions start , even though they're hesitant and they're coming together .
我想再次重申 , 開放式安全是關於聯絡國際的不同地區的 , 跨部門的 , 私人的和公共的 , 並且把它們透過戰略性溝通 , 在社交網上聯絡在一起 。	i want to repeat that , again , opensource security is about connecting international , interagency , privatepublic , and bringing them together through strategic communication , social networking .
所以 , 接下來我將說一些為什麼我們需要那麼做 , 因為我們的共同目標正在受到威脅 , 而且是多方面的 , 同時沒有一種威脅能被透過築牆隔離解決 。	so i'm going to tell you a little bit about why we need to do that , because our common goals are being threatened , and they're multiple ways , and no threat is being resolved by building walls .
現在 , 很明顯我是一個水手 。	now , obviously i'm a sailor .
有一個船在印度洋上航行 。	there's a boat sailing on the indian ocean .
這個照片有什麼問題嗎 ?	what's wrong with this picture ?

海盜依然在馬六甲海峽很猖狂 ,	pirates are still rampant in the channel of malacca .

在加勒比海地區 。	it's in the caribbean .
它在全球交通運輸中每年造成了一百億美元的損失 。	it costs 10 billion dollars a year in global transportation .

這是一個對全球共同利益的威脅 。	it's a threat to global common good .

兩萬億每年 。	two trillion dollars a year .
這僅低於英國的國民生產總值.	that's less than the gdp of the uk .
所以網路世界 , 一個我們深知是由最根本的開放組成的地方 , 正在受到威脅 。	so the internet world , a place that we know is threatened by the most fundamental openness .
另一個我要擔心的是由於物流造成的威脅 , 也就是麻醉劑 , 鴉片等毒品從阿富汗穿過歐洲到達美國的整個一條運輸線 。	the other thing i worry about is the threat caused by logistics , called anesthetics , opioids , all the way across europe to the united states .
我們擔心從andeanridge北部運過來的可卡因 。	we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .
我們擔心非法武器的運輸 。 但最重要的是 , 我們擔心人力的運輸 , 以及它的成本 。	we worry about illegal weapons trafficking , but most importantly , we worry about human transportation and its costs .
大多數運輸是透過海洋的但也透過我們的共同利益 。	most of it is through the ocean but through our common interest .

所以 , 在21世紀 ,	so , in the 21st century .

我們不能僅僅依靠槍支 ,	we can't just rely on guns .

你也許是對的 。	you might be right .
當他們進入安全部隊的時候 , 85%是不識字的 。	when they enter the security forces , 85 percent of them are illiterate .
為什麼 ? 因為塔利班在這些人該學習的時候不提供教育 。	why ? because the taliban are not providing education when these people are supposed to learn .
所以問題是 , 為什麼他們手裡拿著書站在那裡 ?	so the question is , why are they holding books in their hands ?
答案是 , 我們在叫他們閱讀 , 透過北約組織的課程 , 透過和私人組織的合作 , 透過和發展署的合作 。	and the answer is , we're asking them to read , through the course of nato , through collaboration with private organizations , through collaboration with development agencies .
我們已經教了超過200000的阿富汗安全部隊士兵來進行最基本的讀寫 。	we've taught more than 2 , 000 afghan security forces to read the most basic list .
當你能讀和寫的時候 , 你就會在你的口袋裡放一支筆 。	when you can read and write , you put a pen in your pocket .
在畢業典禮上 , 當這些人畢業時 , 他們很驕傲的拿出筆 , 並放在他們的口袋裡 。	at the ceremony , when these people graduated , they were proud to take out pen and put it in their pocket .
這個舉動把全世界有五十個國家跨部門的力量私人和公共資源都聯絡到了一起 , 來進行這種安全的建立 。	this has contacted the power of 50 countries across the world , private and public resources , to build this kind of security .

通常 , 他會進行400000個治療 ,	typically , he's going to perform 4 , 000 treatments .
船員不是嚴格的部隊人員 , 而是很多人道主義組織 , 比如 " 希望專案 " , " 微笑工程 " 。	crew is not a strict military personnel , but a lot of humanitarian organizations , like " hope project , " " " smiling engineering . "

舉個例子來說明這個專案的影響力 , 這個小孩 , 8歲 , 和他的媽媽走了兩天來到安慰號上的眼科診所 。	to give you an example of the impact of this project , this kid , eight years old , walked with his mother for two days to come to eye clinic on comfort .
當他被治好他的重度近視是 , 他突然抬頭 , 然後說: " mama , veoelmundo. "	when he was cured of his weight , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "
" 媽媽 , 我看到世界了 。 "	" mom , i see the world . "
把這個乘以400000 , 也就是治療數目 , 這個私人和公共的合作 , 同時融合了安全力量的專案 , 開始顯現它的力量 , 來以一個很不同的方式創造安全 。	multiply this by 4 , 000 , which is the number of treatments , this private and public collaboration that integrates the power of security and begins to show its power to create security in a very different way .
這張照片是棒球運動員 。	this is a picture of a baseball player .
你能在其中找出兩名美國部隊計程車兵嗎 ?	can you find two american taxi troops ?
他們是每側最邊上的兩位 。 這是棒球診所的一部分 , 在這裡我們嘗試棒球聯賽 , 國務院 , 在軍隊中的棒球運動員 , 也就是那些能真正上戰場的人 , 之間的合作 , 並且他們把這種診所開到了拉丁美洲和加勒比地區 , 開到了宏都拉斯 , 開到了尼加拉瓜 , 開到了所有中美洲和加勒比的棒球很流行國家 , 而且它創造了安全感 。	they're the two people on each side . this is part of a baseball clinic , where we've tried baseball leagues , state departments , baseball players in the military , collaboration between the people who can actually go to war , and they've taken this clinic to latin america and the caribbean area , and they've gone to honduras , to nicaragua , to open all the central american and caribbean baseball nations , and it's creating security .
他為年輕人建立了關於健身和生活的榜樣 , 而且我想說這些理念幫助創造了安全 。	he built role models for young people about fitness and about life , and i want to say that these ideas help create security .
這個合作的另一部分是災後救援與後續工作 。	another part of this partnership is after disaster rescue and subsequent work .
這是一個美國空軍的直升機 , 它參加了2004年一個殺死250000人的海嘯的救援 。	this is a u . s . air force helicopter participating in a tsunami rescue that killed 25 , 000 people in 2004 .
在所有的大災難中2004年海嘯 , 250000死 , 2005年巴基斯坦地震 , 85000人死亡 , 海地地震 , 300000人死亡 , 還有最近的對於日本機器核工業的地震海嘯雙重打擊在所有這些例子中 , 我們看到了國際間 , 跨部門 , 公私結合的合作 , 這個合作與安全力量同時響應這種自然災害 。	tsunami in 2004 , 25 , 000 dead , the pakistani earthquake in 2005 , 85 , 000 dead , the haitian earthquake , 3 , 000 dead , and most recently , to the earthquake of the japanese nuclear machine industry , in all of these examples , we saw international , interagency , privatepublic collaboration with the power of security and this natural disaster .

我在倫敦發表一個像這個的演講 。 我說 , 我對你們說 , 我在facebook上 , 加我好友吧 。	i published a talk like this in london , and i said , " i'm telling you , i'm on facebook . "

這個故事是一個催化劑 , 明天早上我就會有上百個facebook好友請求 , 來自印尼和芬蘭 , 大多數都會說: " 司令 , 我們聽說你需要好友 , 哦 , 還有 , nato是什麼 ? "	the story is a catalyst , and tomorrow morning i'm going to have hundreds of facebook friends requests from indonesia and finland , mostly saying , " command , we're going to hear you need a friend , oh , and what is nato ? "
是的 , 我們笑了 , 但這就是我們如何傳播資訊 , 也就是我們如何把國際 , 不同部門 , 私人和公共 , 以及那些社會網聯絡起來來創造安全 。	yes , we laugh , but that's how we communicate information , and that's how we bring international , interagency , private and public , and those social networks together to create security .
現在 , 讓我說一個嚴肅的訊息 。	now , let me tell you a serious message .

正在helmand站崗 , 在阿富汗南部 。	he's standing there in helmand , in southern afghanistan .

但你知道 , 生活不是開關 。	but you know , life is not a switch .
我們沒有要麼在戰爭 , 要麼在兵營的軍事力量 。	we're not fighting or we're camping military power .
我認為生活是一個可變電阻器 ,	i think life is an electrical resistrator .
你需要調一個數值 , 並且正像我認為我們該如何在21世紀製造安全一樣 , 我們會需要在真正的戰爭和危機中使用真正強硬的力量 , 但會有很多時候 , 就像我們已經討論的 , 我們的部隊可以使21世紀安全 , 也就是國際 , 跨部門 , 公私結合 , 的安全模式的一部分 , 透過溝通來結合起來 。	you need to address a score , and just as i think we can make security in the 21st century , we need to use really hard power in real war and crisis , but there will be times when , as we've talked about , our troops can combine 21stcentury security , international , interagency , interagency , privatepublic , combined by communication .
在結束時 , 我想說在今天早些時候聽到的關於維基百科的一些東西 。 我經常用維基百科查一些東西 , 就像你所知道的 , 維基百科不是靠12個聰明的人把自己關在屋子裡寫文章建立的 。	so to close , i want to say that some of the things that i heard about wikipedia earlier today , i used wikipedia all the time to look at things , and as you know , wikipedia isn't built by 12 smart people who are locked up in a room writing articles .
維基百科是靠每天數萬人的更新 , 數百萬人的提取資訊而建立的 。	wikipedia is built every day by updating tens of thousands of people , extracting information from millions of people .
這完美的說明了沒有一個人能比共同思考更聰明 。	it's a perfect illustration that nobody is smarter than thinking together .
沒有一個人 , 沒有一個聯盟 , 沒有一個國家 , 能有我們共同思考更睿智 。	none of us , none of the coalitions , none of the countries , can think intelligently together .
維基百科的宣言很簡單:建立一個能人人自由共享所有知識的世界 。	the statement of wikipedia is simple: create a world free to share all knowledge .
所以 , 我想說 , 透過結合國際 , 多部門 , 公私力量 , 戰略通訊在一起 , 在21世紀 , 我們能創造共同的安全 。	so i would like to say that by combining international , interagency , privatepublic , strategic communications together , we can create shared security in the 21st century .
非常感謝 。	thank you very much .
